**1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Act                                      Key Provision/Impact
    1. Pitt's India Act                           :   Established a Board of Control
    2. Charter Act of 1793                     :   Mandated annual payment to the British government
    3. Charter Act of 1833                     :   Ended the East India Company's trade monopoly
    4. Government of India Act 1919           :   Introduced Dyarchy in provinces

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched.  The Pitt's India Act of 1784 established the Board of Control to oversee the East India Company's activities, significantly increasing British government control. The Charter Act of 1793, while renewing the Company's charter, imposed a significant financial obligation on the Company by requiring an annual payment to the British government.  The Charter Act of 1833 marked a pivotal moment by ending the East India Company's monopoly on trade with India, opening up the Indian market to other British entities. Finally, the Government of India Act of 1919 implemented the Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms, a key feature of which was the introduction of Dyarchy, a dual system of governance in the provinces. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.  A comprehensive understanding of the major legislative acts governing British India is crucial for answering this question correctly.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Act/Reform                                     Specific Consequence
    1. Charter Act of 1833                         :   Appointment of a Law Member to the Governor-General's Council
    2. Government of India Act 1919               :   Establishment of a statutory Public Service Commission
    3. Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms                  :   Introduction of responsible government at the provincial level
    4. Charter Act of 1793                         :   Separation of revenue administration from judicial functions

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched. The Charter Act of 1833 included the addition of a Law Member to the Governor-General's council, providing legal expertise in governance. The Government of India Act of 1919 established a statutory Public Service Commission to oversee recruitment and administration within the civil service. The Charter Act of 1793 led to the separation of revenue administration from judicial functions, improving efficiency and reducing the concentration of power in the hands of District Collectors. However, statement 3 is incorrect. While the Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms aimed towards responsible government, the Government of India Act of 1919, based on these reforms, introduced Dyarchy, a system of dual governance, not full responsible government at the provincial level.  This nuanced distinction highlights the importance of precise understanding of historical events and avoiding generalizations.


**3. With reference to the evolution of the Indian administrative system under British rule, consider the following pairs:**

    Administrative Reform/Act                  Associated Governor General/Viceroy
    1. Permanent Settlement                      :   Lord Cornwallis
    2. Introduction of Dyarchy                   :   Lord Curzon
    3. Financial Decentralisation (initial steps)   :   Lord Mayo
    4. Abolition of the dual system of government :   Lord Dalhousie

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched. Lord Cornwallis is rightly associated with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement of land revenue in Bengal.  Lord Mayo initiated crucial steps towards financial decentralization by granting fixed sums to provincial governments for specific services.  However, the introduction of Dyarchy is linked to the Government of India Act of 1919, not Lord Curzon's tenure. Similarly, the abolition of the dual system of government is primarily associated with the Regulating Act of 1773 and its subsequent implementations, not Lord Dalhousie.  This question tests the candidate's knowledge of key administrative reforms and their association with specific viceroys/governors-general, demanding precise factual recall.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

    Legislative Act/Council                   Specific Characteristic
    1. Indian Councils Act of 1861            :   Established legislative councils in Bombay and Madras
    2. Indian Councils Act of 1892            :   Introduced an element of indirect election to the councils
    3. Government of India Act 1919           :   Created a bicameral legislature at the center
    4. Charter Act of 1853                    :   Introduced local representation in the Indian legislature

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched. The Indian Councils Act of 1861 is correctly paired with the establishment of legislative councils in Bombay and Madras, signifying a devolution of legislative power. The Indian Councils Act of 1892 introduced a degree of indirect election, albeit limited, to the legislative councils. The Government of India Act of 1919 established a bicameral legislature at the center, comprising the Council of State and the Legislative Assembly. Lastly, the Charter Act of 1853 is correctly associated with the introduction of local representation in the Indian legislature, a significant step towards greater Indian participation in governance.  This question tests the candidate's ability to accurately recall and correlate details about various legislative acts and their impact on the Indian legislative structure.


**5. With reference to the evolution of the Indian judicial system under British rule, consider the following pairs:**

    Judicial Reform/Act                         Prominent Feature/Impact
    1. Regulating Act of 1773                    :   Established a Supreme Court in Calcutta
    2. Cornwallis Code                           :   Separation of revenue and judicial functions
    3. Establishment of High Courts               :   Merged Supreme Courts and Sadar Adalats
    4. Macaulay's Law Commission                 :   Codification of Indian laws


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs accurately reflect aspects of the evolution of the Indian judicial system under British rule. The Regulating Act of 1773 established the Supreme Court in Calcutta, marking a significant step towards a formalized judicial system. The Cornwallis Code, implemented during Lord Cornwallis's tenure, was instrumental in separating revenue and judicial functions, enhancing administrative efficiency and reducing the concentration of power. The establishment of High Courts involved merging the Supreme Courts and Sadar Adalats, creating a more streamlined judicial structure. Finally, Macaulay's Law Commission played a crucial role in codifying Indian laws, resulting in landmark legal documents like the Indian Penal Code and the Code of Criminal Procedure.  The question assesses the candidate's detailed knowledge of the historical development of the Indian judicial system, requiring precise factual recall and understanding of key reforms.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Associated Institution/Event
1. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar : Bethune School
2. Raja Rammohan Roy         :  Vedanta College
3. Dayanand Saraswati        :  Arya Samaj
4. Harbilas Sarda             :  Shuddhi Movement


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar served as the secretary of the Bethune School, a significant institution for women's education during the 19th century in Bengal.  His contributions to education and social reform are well-documented. Raja Rammohan Roy is renowned as the founder of the Brahmo Samaj, but he also played a key role in establishing the Vedanta College, furthering his commitment to education and religious reform.  Dayanand Saraswati is inextricably linked to the Arya Samaj, a reformist Hindu movement he founded, emphasizing Vedic principles and social reform.  Harbilas Sarda, a prominent Arya Samaji, was significantly involved in the Shuddhi movement, a campaign aimed at reconverting those who had converted to other religions back to Hinduism.  These figures and their associations represent key aspects of 19th-century socio-religious reform movements in India, a crucial topic within the UPSC syllabus.  The options designed to mislead the candidate include incorrect pairings of individuals with institutions or movements they were not directly associated with, testing the candidate's precise knowledge of these historical figures and their activities.

**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reformer           Advocated Reform
1. Raja Rammohan Roy       :  Abolition of Sati
2. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar :  Child Marriage
3. Dayanand Saraswati       :  Widow Remarriage


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Only the first pair is correctly matched. Raja Rammohan Roy was a staunch advocate for the abolition of Sati, a practice involving the immolation of widows on their husband's funeral pyres. His relentless efforts, including petitions to the British government and public campaigns, significantly contributed to the eventual ban on Sati in 1829.  The other pairs are incorrect. While Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar championed widow remarriage and opposed child marriage, he is not primarily known for advocating against child marriage specifically. His work focused broadly on improving the lives and status of women in society.  Similarly, Dayanand Saraswati, while advocating for many social reforms, did not primarily focus on widow remarriage. His reformist agenda within the Arya Samaj encompassed a wider range of social issues, including education and the revival of Vedic traditions. The options are designed to test the candidate’s nuanced understanding of the individual contributions of these social reformers, avoiding simple generalizations about their reformist agendas.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Governor-General/Viceroy     Significant Act/Policy
1. Lord Curzon                  :  Partition of Bengal
2. Lord Lytton                   :  Vernacular Press Act, 1878
3. Lord Ripon                    :  Repeal of the Vernacular Press Act


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Lord Lytton is correctly associated with the implementation of the Vernacular Press Act of 1878, a restrictive measure aimed at controlling the Indian-language press. Lord Ripon is correctly linked to the repeal of this same act in 1882, demonstrating a more liberal approach towards freedom of the press.  However, the partition of Bengal is associated with Lord Curzon, not Lord Lytton.  While the partition was eventually reversed, its initial implementation was a defining act of Curzon's tenure as Viceroy. The incorrect pairing of Lord Curzon with the partition of Bengal and the inclusion of other potentially plausible but incorrect pairings effectively tests the candidate's detailed knowledge of the specific actions and policies enacted by these significant figures in British India.


**4.  Consider the following pairs:**

   Act                                  Key Provision
1. Charter Act of 1813                 :  Ended the East India Company's trade monopoly in India
2. Charter Act of 1833                 :  Established a Law Member in the Governor-General's Council
3. Government of India Act, 1935      :  Introduced provincial autonomy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2 and 3

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched. The Charter Act of 1813 was a landmark legislation that ended the East India Company's monopoly over trade in India, although it retained control over the tea trade and trade with China. The Charter Act of 1833 added a Law Member to the Governor-General's Council, marking a significant step towards codifying Indian laws and improving the legal system. Finally, the Government of India Act of 1935 is famously known for establishing provincial autonomy, transferring significant administrative and legislative powers to the provinces, a major step towards self-governance. The options are carefully constructed to include plausible but incorrect pairings, testing the candidate's ability to differentiate between similar acts and their specific provisions.  The question effectively tests the candidate's knowledge of crucial legislative milestones in the evolution of British rule in India.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                      Role/Association
1. Warren Hastings             :  Established a regular police force in India
2. Lord Cornwallis              :  Implemented the Permanent Settlement
3. Lord Dalhousie               :  Doctrine of Lapse


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched.  Warren Hastings, though not the first to establish any form of policing, is credited with establishing a more formalized and regular police force in British India, building upon pre-existing structures.  Lord Cornwallis is directly associated with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement, a significant land revenue system in Bengal.  Finally, Lord Dalhousie's tenure as Governor-General is strongly linked to the Doctrine of Lapse, a controversial policy that led to the annexation of several Indian states.  These figures and their actions represent crucial aspects of the administrative and political history of British India. The distractor options are designed to test the candidate's precise knowledge of these historical figures and their roles, rather than allowing for general knowledge to suffice.  The question demands specific and detailed knowledge of administrative and political history.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Event                                     Significant Impact/Provision
1. Indian Councils Act, 1861                   :   Established separate legislative councils in Bombay and Madras
2. Pitt's India Act, 1784                       :   Ended the dual system of government in India
3. Government of India Act, 1858               :   Transferred power from the East India Company to the British Crown
4. Indian Councils Act, 1892                   :   Introduced indirect elections to legislative councils


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The Indian Councils Act of 1861 is correctly paired with the establishment of separate legislative councils in Bombay and Madras.  This act marked a significant step towards decentralizing legislative power, returning powers previously held centrally.  The Pitt's India Act of 1784 is incorrectly paired with ending the dual system. While it significantly altered the power dynamic between the British government and the East India Company, effectively ending the Company's independent authority, it didn't directly abolish the dual system of government in India which was a gradual process. The Government of India Act of 1858 accurately reflects the transfer of power from the East India Company to the British Crown, marking the end of the Company's rule and the beginning of direct Crown rule in India. The Indian Councils Act of 1892 correctly matches with the introduction of indirect elections to legislative councils, a key step in expanding Indian participation in governance.  Option (a) is incorrect as it only includes one correct pair. Option (b) is incorrect because while 1 and 3 are correct, 4 is also correct. Option (c) is incorrect because it only includes the correctly matched pair related to the Government of India Act, 1858, neglecting the other accurate matches.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                        Role/Association
1. Lord Cornwallis                               :   Introduced the Permanent Settlement
2. Lord Curzon                                   :   Implemented major police reforms
3. Lord Dalhousie                               :   Introduced the Doctrine of Lapse
4. Lord Lytton                                   :   Implemented the Vernacular Press Act


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

Lord Cornwallis is correctly linked to the introduction of the Permanent Settlement in Bengal, a significant land revenue system with long-lasting consequences. Lord Curzon's tenure as Viceroy saw major police reforms aimed at strengthening law enforcement and intelligence gathering.  Lord Dalhousie is accurately associated with the Doctrine of Lapse, a controversial annexation policy that significantly expanded British territory. Lord Lytton implemented the Vernacular Press Act, a restrictive measure targeting the Indian press.  All four pairs are correctly matched, showcasing the significant contributions and actions of these individuals within the British administration in India. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude correctly matched pairs.  The question tests knowledge of key figures in British India and their associated policies and administrative reforms.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legislation                                   Key Provision/Impact
1. Charter Act of 1813                           :   Ended the Company's monopoly over trade with China
2. Indian Councils Act, 1861                     :   Expanded the Viceroy's Executive Council
3. Government of India Act, 1919                 :   Introduced Dyarchy in provinces
4. Indian Councils Act, 1909                     :   Introduced separate electorates for Muslims


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1813 correctly ended the East India Company's monopoly on trade with China, opening it up to British subjects. The Government of India Act of 1919 accurately introduced the system of Dyarchy in provinces, dividing administrative powers between Indian ministers and British officials. The Indian Councils Act of 1909 correctly introduced separate electorates for Muslims, a significant development in Indian politics with long-term consequences.  The Indian Councils Act of 1861, however, did not expand the Viceroy's Executive Council in the way the statement suggests. While it did expand the legislative council, the executive council remained largely unchanged.  Therefore, option (c) is the correct answer, accurately reflecting the key provisions and impacts of three out of the four legislations. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they include the incorrectly matched pair concerning the Indian Councils Act of 1861.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Administrative Reform                          Viceroy/Governor-General
1. Financial Decentralization                   :   Lord Mayo
2. Police Reforms                               :   Lord Curzon
3. Introduction of Portfolio System             :   Lord Canning
4. Expansion of Legislative Councils            :   Lord Ripon


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Lord Mayo is correctly associated with initiating financial decentralization, transferring financial responsibilities to provincial governments. Lord Curzon implemented significant police reforms, including improvements to training and intelligence gathering. Lord Canning introduced the portfolio system, which organized the administration into distinct departments headed by council members.  However, while Lord Ripon made many significant contributions to Indian administration, the expansion of legislative councils was a process spanning multiple acts and governors-general.  It's not solely attributable to Lord Ripon. Therefore, options (a) and (b) are incomplete, and (d) is incorrect because it includes the inaccurate pairing with Lord Ripon. Option (c) accurately reflects the correct matches, showcasing the key administrative reforms associated with these specific viceroys.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                                  Primary Objective/Consequence
1. Permanent Settlement                        :   Secure land revenue for the British
2. Doctrine of Lapse                           :   Annexation of Indian states
3. Subsidiary Alliance                          :   Establish British political control
4. Ryotwari System                             :   Direct land revenue collection from cultivators


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

The Permanent Settlement aimed to secure a stable and predictable land revenue stream for the British East India Company. The Doctrine of Lapse was a policy that resulted in the annexation of many Indian princely states. The Subsidiary Alliance system was designed to establish British political control over various Indian states. The Ryotwari System established direct revenue collection from individual cultivators, bypassing intermediaries.  All four pairs are correctly matched, demonstrating an understanding of key British policies in India and their intended objectives and outcomes. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect as they omit correctly matched pairs.  This question tests the understanding of British land revenue systems and their impact on Indian society and the political landscape.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and test a deep understanding of the material, going beyond simple factual recall.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Policy/Act                                  Implementation Year
1.  Vernacular Press Act                     :   1882
2.  First Indian Factory Act                  :   1891
3.  Second Indian Factories Act              :   1881
4.  Regulations empowering Zamindars       :   1812


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 4 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Vernacular Press Act was passed in 1878, not 1882.  It was repealed in 1882 after public outcry. The First Indian Factory Act was enacted in 1881, not 1891, while the Second Indian Factories Act was passed in 1891.  The Regulations (1793, 1799, and 1812) which significantly empowered Zamindars to seize tenant property without court permission are correctly paired with 1812 as one of the years.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect due to the mismatched years for the Acts related to the press and factory legislation.  The question tests factual recall and the ability to discern accuracy within a set of potentially confusing similar dates.


**2. With reference to British policies in 19th-century India, consider the following pairs:**

   Land Revenue System                  Area of Implementation
1.  Ryotwari System                       :  Bengal
2.  Mahalwari System                     :  Madras Presidency
3.  Permanent Settlement                 :  Parts of Bombay Presidency


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Ryotwari system was primarily implemented in Madras Presidency and parts of Bombay Presidency, not Bengal.  The Mahalwari system was introduced in parts of North-Western Provinces, Central Provinces, and the Punjab, not Madras Presidency. The Permanent Settlement was indeed implemented in parts of the Bombay Presidency, along with Bengal, Bihar, Orissa, and Banaras.  Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched. This question tests conceptual understanding of the geographical reach of different land revenue systems and the ability to identify inaccuracies in the given information.  The options are designed to create plausible distractors based on the general knowledge of these systems.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Individual                                    Association/Action
1.  Lord Cornwallis                             :  Implemented Ryotwari System
2.  Thomas Munro                               :  Introduced Permanent Settlement
3.  Philip Francis                              : Recommended Permanent Settlement


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Cornwallis is correctly associated with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement, not the Ryotwari System. Thomas Munro is known for his role in devising and implementing the Ryotwari system, not the Permanent Settlement. Philip Francis did indeed recommend a permanent settlement in land revenue.  Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched.  This question tests factual recall of key individuals and their contributions to land revenue policies. The incorrect options provide plausible distractors by associating individuals with policies they were not directly involved with.


**4. With reference to the British administration in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                                  Primary Focus
1.  Vernacular Press Act of 1878            :  Promoting Indian Language Newspapers
2.  Factory Act of 1881                       :  Regulating Working Conditions for Adults
3.  1863-1882 Plantation Labour Laws       : Protecting Plantation Workers' Rights


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Vernacular Press Act of 1878 aimed to curb the freedom of the Indian-language press, not promote it. The Factory Act of 1881 primarily focused on child labor, not regulating conditions for adult workers.  The plantation labor laws of 1863-1882 were designed to facilitate the exploitation of labor, not protect workers' rights.  All three pairs are incorrectly matched, highlighting the manipulative and exploitative nature of British policies. This question tests the ability to analyze the underlying intent of British legislation and avoid superficial interpretations.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                      Stance on Drain Theory
1.  B.G. Tilak                                 :  Supported Drain Theory
2.  R.C. Dutt                                  :  Rejected Drain Theory
3.  Sir Syed Ahmad Khan                       :  Supported Drain Theory


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

B.G. Tilak and Dadabhai Naoroji were strong proponents of the Drain theory. R.C. Dutt also supported the Drain theory, while Sir Syed Ahmad Khan did not. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched.  This question tests the understanding of the Drain theory and the stances of various prominent figures on this important economic concept. The inclusion of R.C. Dutt as a potential distractor adds to the complexity.


These questions are designed to be challenging, requiring in-depth knowledge of the subject matter and the ability to critically analyze the information provided.  The distractors are carefully chosen to be plausible yet incorrect, forcing candidates to demonstrate a thorough understanding beyond superficial recall.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                      Associated Organization/Movement
1. Dadabhai Naoroji             :   East India Association
2. Sir Syed Ahmad Khan         :   Muslim League
3. Jawaharlal Nehru             :   Forward Bloc


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji founded the East India Association in London, a crucial organization for advocating Indian interests in Britain.  This is a well-established fact in Indian history.  Option (a) is therefore correct.

Option (b) is incorrect because while Sir Syed Ahmad Khan was a highly influential figure, he is not directly associated with the Muslim League's founding.  Although he played a significant role in the development of Muslim political consciousness in India, his association with the Muslim League is not as direct as Naoroji's with the East India Association. The Muslim League was founded later by others.

Option (c) is incorrect because Jawaharlal Nehru was a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress, not the Forward Bloc. The Forward Bloc was a political party founded by Subhas Chandra Bose, representing a more radical faction within the nationalist movement. Nehru's association is primarily with the Congress.

Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the inaccuracies described above concerning both Sir Syed Ahmad Khan and Jawaharlal Nehru.  It incorrectly links them to organizations they did not directly found or lead.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Significant Contribution/Association
1. Dadabhai Naoroji             :   Authored "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India"
2. G.V. Ranade                 :   Proponent of Drain Theory
3. Warren Hastings              :   Established the Asiatic Society of Bengal


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji's authorship of "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India," a seminal work analyzing the economic exploitation of India under British rule, is a well-documented fact.  Warren Hastings, the first Governor-General of Bengal, played a key role in establishing the Asiatic Society of Bengal, a significant institution for the study of Indian history, culture, and languages. Therefore, option (c) is correct.

Option (b) is incorrect because while G.V. Ranade was a significant figure in Indian nationalism and contributed to economic thought, he is not primarily known as the *proponent* of the Drain Theory.  That distinction belongs to Dadabhai Naoroji, who formulated and popularized the theory.  Ranade's work often intersected with and built upon Naoroji's ideas but did not originate the theory.

Option (a) is incorrect because it omits the correct pairing of Warren Hastings with the Asiatic Society of Bengal.

Option (d) is incorrect as it includes the incorrect attribution of the Drain Theory to G.V. Ranade.


**3. With reference to the early years of British rule in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Land Revenue System       Region of Implementation
1. Ryotwari System            :   Bengal
2. Mahalwari System           :   Madras Presidency
3. Permanent Settlement       :   North-Western Provinces


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Permanent Settlement, introduced by Lord Cornwallis, was primarily implemented in Bengal, Bihar, and parts of Orissa.  The Mahalwari system was implemented in the North-Western Provinces (present-day Uttar Pradesh and Uttarakhand), and parts of Punjab. The Ryotwari system was implemented in Madras Presidency (present-day Tamil Nadu, Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka, and Kerala). Therefore, only option (c) correctly matches the land revenue system with its primary region of implementation.

Options (a) and (b) are incorrect because they misrepresent the geographic scope of the Ryotwari and Mahalwari systems respectively.  Option (d) is incorrect because at least one pairing is correct.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation           Primary Focus/Impact
1. Vernacular Press Act, 1878:   Promoted freedom of the Indian press
2. Indian Factory Act, 1881  :   Regulated child labour
3. Charter Act of 1813        :   Ended the East India Company's trade monopoly completely


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Indian Factory Act of 1881 primarily focused on regulating child labour in factories, setting minimum age limits and working hours. This is a well-established fact. Option (b) is therefore correct.

Option (a) is incorrect because the Vernacular Press Act of 1878 aimed to restrict, not promote, the freedom of the Indian-language press.  It was a measure of censorship.

Option (c) is incorrect because it includes the incorrect pairing of the Vernacular Press Act.

Option (d) is incorrect because the Charter Act of 1813 did not completely end the East India Company's trade monopoly; it ended the monopoly on trade *except* for tea and trade with China.  The complete end of the Company's trade monopoly came later.


**5. With reference to the British colonial administration in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Governor-General/Viceroy     Significant Policy/Event Associated

3. Warren Hastings             :   Permanent Settlement


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Dalhousie is famously associated with the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy that led to the annexation of several Indian princely states. Warren Hastings is associated with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement, a landmark land revenue system. Therefore, option (c) is correct.

Option (a) is incorrect as Lord Cornwallis is associated with the Permanent Settlement, not the Mahalwari system.

Option (b) is incorrect as it excludes the correct association of Warren Hastings.

Option (d) is incorrect as it includes the incorrect association of Lord Cornwallis with the Mahalwari system.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act                                          Key Provision
1. Charter Act of 1793                   :   Established a system of competitive examinations for civil service recruitment
2. Charter Act of 1813                     :   Ended the East India Company's monopoly over the tea trade
3. Charter Act of 1833                     :   Allocated funds for the education of Indians
4. Charter Act of 1853                      :   Dissolved the East India Company's patronage system

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1833, not 1793, allocated one lakh rupees annually for the education of Indians.  The Charter Act of 1793 primarily focused on renewing the East India Company's charter and regulating its affairs, not introducing competitive examinations for civil service.  The introduction of open competition for the Indian Civil Service came much later, with the Charter Act of 1853 playing a significant role in this reform by dissolving the Company's patronage system, paving the way for merit-based recruitment. The Charter Act of 1813 is correctly matched as it ended the East India Company's monopoly over trade in India except for the trade with China and the tea trade. Option (c) is correct because both the Charter Act of 1833 (allocation of funds for Indian education) and the Charter Act of 1853 (dissolution of patronage) are accurately paired with their key provisions.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect due to the mismatching of the Charter Acts with their respective provisions.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legislation                                  Impact on Governance
1. Regulating Act of 1773                   :   Established a Board of Control to oversee the East India Company
2. Pitt's India Act of 1784                   :   Defined the jurisdiction of the Supreme Court in Calcutta
3. Charter Act of 1813                      :   Increased the power of the Board of Control over the East India Company
4. Charter Act of 1853                      :   Introduced a system of dyarchy in the provinces

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Pitt's India Act of 1784, not the Regulating Act of 1773, established the Board of Control. The Regulating Act of 1773 primarily focused on establishing a Supreme Court in Calcutta and centralizing the administration of the East India Company.  The Amending Act of 1781, not the Pitt's India Act of 1784, clarified the jurisdiction of the Supreme Court. The Charter Act of 1813 correctly reflects the increased power of the Board of Control. The introduction of dyarchy occurred much later, as a key feature of the Government of India Act of 1919, not the Charter Act of 1853. The Charter Act of 1853 focused on ending the Company’s patronage system and opening up the Indian Civil Service to competitive examinations. Therefore, only the pairing of the Charter Act of 1813 with the increased power of the Board of Control is accurate. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect due to the mismatching of the Acts with their impacts on governance.

   Act                                         Significant Feature

(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

The Charter Act of 1813 is correctly paired with its allocation of funds for Indian education. The establishment of a functioning Legislative Council is associated with the Charter Act of 1853, not 1833. The Charter Act of 1833 made significant changes to the governance structure but didn't establish a fully functioning Legislative Council in the way the 1853 Act did. The Charter Act of 1853 correctly reflects the introduction of competitive examinations for the Indian Civil Service, a crucial step towards reforming the colonial administration.  Therefore, only the pairs concerning the Charter Acts of 1813 and 1853 are correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because of the inaccuracies in the pairing of the Charter Acts with their features.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Policy/Act                                    Implementing Official/Year
1. Vernacular Press Act                     :    Lord Ripon, 1882
2.  Wood's Despatch                          :    Lord Dalhousie, 1853
3.  Hunter Commission Report                  :    Lord Curzon, 1902
4.  Indian Universities Act, 1904           :   Lord Lytton, 1878


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Vernacular Press Act was implemented by Lord Lytton in 1878, not Lord Ripon in 1882.  Lord Ripon actually repealed the act in 1882, demonstrating a more liberal approach to press freedom. Wood's Despatch, a landmark document in the history of education in India, was formulated and issued in 1854 by Charles Wood, under the administration of Lord Dalhousie. The Hunter Commission, which focused on the state of education, was appointed in 1882 under the Viceroyalty of Lord Ripon, not Lord Curzon in 1902.  The Indian Universities Act of 1904 was passed during the Viceroyalty of Lord Curzon, aiming to improve the quality and governance of Indian universities, not under Lord Lytton.  Therefore, only the pairing of Wood's Despatch with 1854 and the Indian Universities Act with 1904 are correct.  The other options present inaccuracies regarding the implementing officials and years.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Newspaper                                     Founder/Editor
1.  Kesari                                      :    Gopal Krishna Gokhale
2.  Indian Mirror                              :    Dadabhai Naoroji
3.  Amrita Bazar Patrika                      :    Surendranath Banerjea
4.  The Bengalee                               :    Sisir Kumar Ghosh


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Kesari was founded and edited by Bal Gangadhar Tilak, not Gopal Krishna Gokhale.  Gokhale was a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress but not associated with Kesari. The Indian Mirror was edited by N.N. Sen, not Dadabhai Naoroji, who was a significant early nationalist leader but known for other publications. Amrita Bazar Patrika was indeed associated with Sisir Kumar Ghosh and Motilal Ghosh.  The Bengalee was, in fact, edited by Surendranath Banerjea, a prominent figure in the early nationalist movement. Thus, only the pairings of Amrita Bazar Patrika and The Bengalee with their respective editors are correct.  The other options contain incorrect attributions of newspapers to their founders/editors.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                        Significant Contribution/Association
1.  Lord Cornwallis                           :    Introduction of the Ryotwari System
2.  Lord William Bentinck                     :    Abolition of Sati
3.  Lord Curzon                               :    Partition of Bengal
4.  Lord Lytton                                :    Introduction of the Ilbert Bill


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Lord Cornwallis is primarily known for introducing the Permanent Settlement, not the Ryotwari system.  The Ryotwari system was a different land revenue system implemented in other parts of British India. Lord William Bentinck played a crucial role in the abolition of Sati, a significant social reform. Lord Curzon is indeed associated with the Partition of Bengal, a controversial administrative decision.  Lord Lytton introduced the Vernacular Press Act, not the Ilbert Bill. The Ilbert Bill was an attempt to grant Indian judges the power to try European British citizens in criminal cases and was introduced by Lord Ripon. Therefore, only the associations of Lord William Bentinck with the abolition of Sati and Lord Curzon with the Partition of Bengal are correct.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                                   Primary Aim/Effect
1. Charter Act of 1813                          :   Allocation of funds for Western education
2. Macaulay's Minute (1835)                   :   Promotion of vernacular education
3.  Wood's Despatch (1854)                    :   Emphasis on mass education
4.  Hunter Commission Report (1882)           :   Recommendation for compulsory primary education


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1813 did indeed allocate funds, albeit a small amount initially, for the promotion of education in India, although not exclusively Western education at that point. Macaulay's Minute (1835) advocated for the promotion of Western education through the English language, directly contradicting the promotion of vernacular education. Wood's Despatch (1854), while aiming for a more comprehensive system, did not initially prioritize mass education as its primary focus; its implementation faced challenges. The Hunter Commission Report (1882) did emphasize primary education but didn't explicitly recommend compulsory primary education throughout British India.  Therefore, only the association between the Charter Act of 1813 and the allocation of funds for education is accurately matched. The other options present inaccurate interpretations of the aims and effects of the given policies and Acts.


**5. With reference to the development of education in British India, consider the following pairs:**

   Educational Reform/Commission             Key Feature/Recommendation
1.  Wood's Dispatch                            :  Establishment of Universities in Presidency Towns
2.  Hunter Commission                          :  Emphasis on Technical Education
3.  Sadler Commission                          :  Advocacy for twelve-year school curriculum
4.  Hartog Committee                          :  Focus on improving the quality of primary education


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Wood's Dispatch (1854) did lay the groundwork for the establishment of universities in the major presidency towns of Calcutta, Bombay, and Madras.  The Hunter Commission (1882) primarily focused on primary and secondary education, not technical education. While technical education was important, it wasn't the central theme of their report. The Sadler Commission (1917-19) significantly advocated for a twelve-year school curriculum to better prepare students for university education. The Hartog Committee (1929) conducted a thorough review of the education system and emphasized the need to improve the quality of primary education, addressing issues like high dropout rates and low learning outcomes.  Therefore, options 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Option 2 is incorrect because the Hunter Commission's main focus was on primary and secondary education.  Option (d) is also incorrect because option 2 is false.

**3. Consider the following pairs:**

  Act/Legislation                  Key Provision/Impact
1.  Indian Councils Act of 1892   :   Introduced the principle of communal representation
2.  Indian Councils Act of 1909   :   Introduced dyarchy in the provinces
3.  Government of India Act, 1935:   Established a bicameral legislature at the centre

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 1 is correctly matched. The Indian Councils Act of 1892 is significant for introducing a measure of elected representation, albeit limited, and indirectly paved the way for the introduction of communal representation. The Indian Councils Act of 1909 (Morley-Minto Reforms), while expanding representation, did *not* introduce dyarchy; that came with the Government of India Act, 1919. The Government of India Act, 1935, did establish a bicameral legislature at the center, comprising the Council of State and the Federal Assembly. The other options combine incorrect pairings of acts and their provisions, testing the candidate's detailed understanding of the evolution of the Indian legislative system under British rule. A thorough understanding of these acts is crucial for success in the UPSC exam.

(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 2 is correctly matched. Lord Dalhousie is correctly associated with the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy that led to the annexation of several Indian states during his tenure as Governor-General.  Sir Thomas Munro is associated with the Ryotwari system, not the Permanent Settlement, which was implemented by Lord Cornwallis. Lord Wellesley did not implement the Ryotwari settlement directly; it was developed and implemented by officials under him in different regions.  Lord Cornwallis is associated with the Permanent Settlement, not the Mahalwari Settlement, which was introduced later. The question tests the candidate's understanding of the land revenue systems and policies implemented by various British Governors-General in India.  Understanding these policies is crucial to analyzing the impact of British rule on the Indian agrarian economy.

**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                     Key Provision/Feature

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2 and 3

The Indian Councils Act of 1909, also known as the Morley-Minto Reforms, introduced separate electorates for Muslims, allowing them to elect their representatives to legislative councils.  The Indian Independence Act of 1947 formalized the partition of India into India and Pakistan. All three pairs accurately reflect key features of the respective legislations.  This question tests the examinee's understanding of significant legislative milestones in India's journey towards independence.  All options except (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.

**7. Consider the following pairs:**

   Revenue System                    Region/Presidency Primarily Implemented
1.  Permanent Settlement             :  Bombay Presidency
2.  Ryotwari System                  :  Madras Presidency
3.  Mahalwari System                 :  North-Western Provinces


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Ryotwari system, characterized by direct revenue collection from individual cultivators, was primarily implemented in the Madras Presidency.  The Mahalwari system, which involved revenue collection from village communities, was predominantly implemented in the North-Western Provinces. However, the Permanent Settlement, which granted proprietary rights to Zamindars, was primarily implemented in Bengal and Bihar, not the Bombay Presidency. The Bombay Presidency largely adopted the Ryotwari system. This question tests the examinee's understanding of the different land revenue systems introduced by the British and their geographical distribution. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they mistakenly include the Permanent Settlement's association with the Bombay Presidency.

**10. With reference to the impact of British policies in India, consider the following pairs:**

   British Policy                     Consequence
1.  Divide and Rule                   :  Increased communal tensions
2.  Permanent Settlement              :  Rise of absentee landlordism
3.  Ryotwari System                   :  Improved agricultural infrastructure


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

The British policy of "Divide and Rule" exacerbated existing communal tensions, exploiting religious and caste differences to maintain control. The Permanent Settlement, while aiming to streamline revenue collection, led to the rise of absentee landlordism, as Zamindars focused on rent extraction rather than land improvement. However, the Ryotwari system, while not necessarily improving agricultural infrastructure directly, did not inherently lead to its improvement.  It often led to over-assessment and exploitation of peasants. This question tests the examinee's understanding of the long-term consequences of British policies on Indian society and economy.  Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either miss one or both of the correctly matched pairs or wrongly include the incorrect association of Ryotwari system with improved agricultural infrastructure.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Reform                                   Key Provision/Impact
1. Indian Councils Act, 1892                  : Increased number of non-official members in Legislative Councils
2. Minto-Morley Reforms, 1909               : Introduced separate electorates for Muslims
3. Government of India Act, 1935             : Established provincial autonomy

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Indian Councils Act of 1892 aimed to expand the Legislative Councils by increasing the number of non-official members, albeit maintaining an official majority. This was a step towards greater Indian participation in the legislative process.  The Minto-Morley Reforms of 1909, a significant landmark, introduced the principle of communal representation, granting separate electorates to Muslims. This addressed Muslim concerns about their political representation within the larger Indian context.  The Government of India Act of 1935, a comprehensive piece of legislation, introduced provincial autonomy, granting significant self-governing powers to the provinces.  All three pairs accurately reflect the key provisions or impacts of the respective Acts/Reforms. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete and thus incorrect, as they fail to acknowledge the accurate match in all three pairs.  Understanding the evolution of constitutional reforms in British India requires a grasp of these key legislative milestones and their respective impact on the political landscape.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Newspaper                                    Founder/Prominent Figure
1. Kesari                                       : Gopal Krishna Gokhale
2. Indian Opinion                               : Mahatma Gandhi
3. The Comrade                                  : Bipin Chandra Pal

(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

Mahatma Gandhi founded the *Indian Opinion* newspaper in South Africa during his time there, using it as a platform to advocate for Indian rights and voice concerns against racial discrimination.  While *Kesari* was indeed a prominent nationalist newspaper, it was founded and edited by Bal Gangadhar Tilak, not Gopal Krishna Gokhale. Gokhale was a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress but not associated with the founding of *Kesari*. Similarly, *The Comrade* was associated with the nationalist movement and particularly with the extremist faction, but it was primarily associated with Bipin Chandra Pal, not solely founded by him. **3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Land Revenue System                         Region of Initial Implementation
1. Ryotwari System                             : Bengal
2. Permanent Settlement                        : Madras Presidency
3. Mahalwari System                            : North-Western Provinces

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Mahalwari system, a significant land revenue system in British India, was initially implemented in the North-Western Provinces. This system differed from the Ryotwari and Permanent Settlement systems in its approach to revenue collection and land ownership.  The Ryotwari system, which directly assessed revenue from individual cultivators (ryots), was primarily implemented in Madras Presidency and other regions, not Bengal. The Permanent Settlement, in contrast, established a fixed land revenue demand on zamindars, was primarily implemented in Bengal, Bihar, and parts of Orissa – not Madras Presidency.  Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched. This highlights the importance of understanding the geographical distribution and characteristics of different land revenue systems in colonial India, a crucial element of understanding economic policies during that period.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                      Significant Contribution/Association

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Curzon is famously known for the Partition of Bengal in 1905, a controversial administrative decision with significant political repercussions. Lord Ripon is known for significant administrative reforms and initiating the Hunter Commission, not the first Indian Education Commission (that was established earlier). The first Indian Education Commission was appointed by Lord William Bentinck. Lord Lytton is remembered for the controversial Vernacular Press Act of 1878, which aimed to curb the freedom of the Indian press. Thus, only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched. This question tests understanding of the major figures in British India and their specific actions and policies, which significantly impacted the political, social, and cultural landscape.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Viceroy/Governor-General          Action/Policy
1. Lord Curzon                       :  Introduced the Indian Universities Act, 1904
2. Lord Ripon                         :  Repealed the Vernacular Press Act, 1878
3. Lord Dalhousie                     :  Implemented the Doctrine of Lapse
4. Lord Wellesley                      :  Established the Subsidiary Alliance System
5. Lord Lytton                        :  Implemented the Ilbert Bill


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Lord Curzon is indeed associated with significant educational reforms in India, but the Indian Universities Act was passed in 1904, not by him.  The primary legislation associated with Curzon's educational reforms is the Indian Universities Act, 1904, which aimed to improve the standards and governance of Indian universities. While he did implement other significant policies, the given pairing is incorrect due to the year mentioned.  Lord Ripon's association with the repeal of the Vernacular Press Act, 1878, is well-documented. This act, which restricted the freedom of the vernacular press, was a significant step towards restricting freedom of expression.  Lord Dalhousie's implementation of the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy that led to the annexation of several princely states, is a crucial aspect of his tenure. This policy significantly altered the political landscape of India during the British Raj. Lord Wellesley's introduction of the Subsidiary Alliance System, a key strategy for British expansion in India, is also historically accurate. This system involved alliances with Indian rulers, often leading to British control over their territories and resources. Lord Lytton did not implement the Ilbert Bill; it was actually introduced and modified by Lord Ripon.  The Ilbert Bill, which aimed at granting Indian judges the power to try European offenders, sparked significant controversy. Therefore, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.

Gopal Krishna Gokhale's association with Kesari is incorrect;  it was primarily associated with Bal Gangadhar Tilak. Thus, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. **3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                 Contribution/Association
1. Dadabhai Naoroji                     :  Introduced the concept of Purna Swaraj
2. Gopal Krishna Gokhale                 :  Founded the Servants of India Society
3. Lala Lajpat Rai                       :  President of the Indian National Congress
4. Bal Gangadhar Tilak                  :  Leader of the Home Rule Movement
5. Mahatma Gandhi                       :  Authored Hind Swaraj


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2, 4, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

Gopal Krishna Gokhale founded the Servants of India Society, a significant organization dedicated to social and political reform. Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a prominent leader of the Home Rule Movement, which aimed at achieving self-governance for India. Mahatma Gandhi authored Hind Swaraj, a seminal work outlining his political philosophy. However, the other pairings are incorrect.  Dadabhai Naoroji is associated with the "Drain of Wealth" theory, not the introduction of Purna Swaraj (complete independence), which is primarily attributed to Jawaharlal Nehru. Lala Lajpat Rai was a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress, but he never served as its President.  The question assesses the candidate's knowledge of key figures in the Indian independence movement and their specific contributions, testing factual recall and conceptual understanding of the personalities and their roles.  The distractors are designed to challenge the candidate's understanding of the nuances of the movement's leadership.


**4. With reference to the Indian National Movement, consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Movement                        Year
1.  Partition of Bengal                   :  1905
2.  Formation of the Muslim League      :  1906
3.  Non-Cooperation Movement             :  1920
4.  Salt Satyagraha                      :  1930
5.  Quit India Movement                  :  1942


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. The Partition of Bengal occurred in 1905, a major event that fueled the Indian nationalist movement. The All India Muslim League was founded in 1906, representing the political interests of the Muslim community. The Non-Cooperation Movement, launched in 1920, marked a significant phase of the struggle for independence. The Salt Satyagraha, a pivotal moment in the Civil Disobedience Movement, started in 1930.  The Quit India Movement, a mass civil disobedience campaign, was launched in 1942. This question tests the candidate's chronological understanding of significant events in the Indian National Movement.  The options are designed to check if the candidate can accurately recall the years associated with these events.  The inclusion of all correct pairs makes it a challenging question, rewarding precise factual knowledge.


**5. With reference to the early phase of the Indian National Congress, consider the following pairs:**

   Organization                          Founder/Prominent Leader
1.  East India Association              :  Dadabhai Naoroji
2.  Bombay Presidency Association     :  Ferozeshah Mehta
3.  Poona Sarvajanik Sabha             :  Gopal Krishna Gokhale

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji is correctly paired with the founding of the East India Association in London, a crucial organization for lobbying British opinion on Indian affairs.  Ferozeshah Mehta's leadership of the Bombay Presidency Association is historically accurate; this organization played a significant role in the political landscape of Bombay. Surendranath Banerjea's role in founding and leading the Indian Association in Calcutta is also a well-established fact.  However, the other pairings are incorrect.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale was prominently associated with the Poona Sarvajanik Sabha, but he wasn't the founder;  Raja Ram Mohan Roy was not the founder of the Landholders’ Society. This question tests factual knowledge about the pre-Congress organizations and their leaders, assessing the candidate's understanding of the early stages of organized nationalist activity in India. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Commission                                     Feature
1. Government of India Act, 1919                    :   Established a Public Service Commission
2. Government of India Act, 1935                    :   Advocated the creation of a Federal Court
3. Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms                       :   Formed the basis of the Government of India Act, 1919
4. Hunter Commission (1882)                         :   Endorsed the Despatch of 1854 with greater emphasis on primary education

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act, 1919, significantly restructured the Indian administrative and legislative framework.  A key feature of this Act was the establishment of a Public Service Commission, aiming to improve the impartiality and efficiency of recruitment to the civil services.  Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched.

The Government of India Act, 1935, introduced significant constitutional changes, including the establishment of a Federal Court in India. This court was designed to handle appeals from High Courts and to adjudicate disputes between the federal and provincial governments.  Thus, pair 2 is also correctly matched.

The Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms, outlined in the report of the same name, laid the groundwork for the Government of India Act, 1919.  The reforms proposed significant changes, many of which were incorporated into the subsequent Act. This makes pair 3 a correct match.

The Hunter Commission (1882), appointed to investigate the state of education in India, did not endorse the Despatch of 1854 wholesale. While it acknowledged the Despatch, the Hunter Commission focused more on primary education and highlighted issues within the existing system, including criticisms of the grant-in-aid system. Hence, pair 4 is incorrectly matched.  The commission's report emphasized the need to improve primary education significantly more than the 1854 Despatch had.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                          Action/Association
1. Lord Curzon                                     :   Started the Indian Agricultural Service
2. Lord Minto                                      :   Granted separate electorates
3. William Bentinck                               :   Implemented the abolition of Sati


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Lord Curzon, during his viceroyalty, played a crucial role in establishing the Indian Agricultural Service. This initiative aimed to improve agricultural practices and research in India. Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched.

Lord Minto's tenure as Viceroy is associated with the introduction of separate electorates.  This controversial policy granted separate voting rights to different religious communities, particularly Muslims, a significant event in the lead-up to the partition of India. Thus, pair 2 is correct.

William Bentinck, as Governor-General, oversaw the abolition of Sati, a practice involving the immolation of widows on their husband's funeral pyres. This reform was a significant step in social reform during the British Raj.  Consequently, pair 3 is also correctly matched.  All three pairs accurately reflect historical facts.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                                    Key Provision/Impact
1. Deccan Agriculturalists’ Relief Act of 1879       :   Restricted the sale of land for indebtedness to outsiders
2. Limitation Law of 1859                          :   Loan bonds signed between moneylenders and ryots would have validity only for three years
3. The Summary Settlement of 1856                  :   Assumed the Talukdars were interlopers with no permanent stakes in the land


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

The Deccan Agriculturalists’ Relief Act of 1879 was enacted primarily to address the issue of escalating rural indebtedness in the Deccan region.  A key feature of the Act was to restrict the sale of land to outsiders due to debt, aiming to protect the land ownership rights of the peasants. Hence, pair 1 is correctly matched.

The Limitation Law of 1859 aimed to regulate the validity of loan bonds, specifically those between moneylenders and ryots (peasants).  The Act limited the legal validity of these bonds to three years, preventing moneylenders from indefinitely extending the debt burden on the peasantry. Pair 2 is accurate.

The Summary Settlement of 1856, implemented in Oudh (Awadh), was predicated on the assumption that many of the Talukdars (local landlords) were not legitimate owners of the land but had acquired it relatively recently. The settlement aimed to assess and regularize land ownership, challenging the claims of certain Talukdars.  Pair 3 is therefore correctly matched.  The three pairs accurately reflect the historical context and provisions of these legislative measures.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Journal                                          Editor
1. Indian Social Reformer                         :   Gopal Krishna Gokhale
2.  Indian Opinion                                  :   Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
3.  The Hindu                                      :   Kasturi Ranga Iyengar


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

While Gopal Krishna Gokhale was a prominent figure in Indian journalism and social reform, he wasn't the editor of the *Indian Social Reformer*.  That journal was primarily associated with G. Subramaniam. Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect.

Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi was indeed closely associated with the *Indian Opinion*, a journal published in South Africa during his time there.  He played a significant role in its editing and management. Pair 2 is therefore correct.

Kasturi Ranga Iyengar was a prominent figure in Indian journalism and played a key role in the development of *The Hindu* newspaper.  Pair 3 is accurate.  The question highlights the need for precise knowledge of journalistic history.

   Person                                         Role/Association

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d) None

**Explanation:**

Sarojini Naidu was a prominent poet and political activist, but she was not the founder of Mahakali Pathshala in Calcutta.  That institution was founded by Sister Nivedita.  Pair 1 is incorrect.

Sister Nivedita, while a significant figure in the Indian National Movement, was not a president of the Indian National Congress.  Pair 2 is incorrect.

Her Holiness Mataji Maharani Tapaswini was not the editor of the *Indian Social Reformer*.  Pair 3 is incorrect.  This question tests knowledge of individuals and their contributions, showcasing the need for precise factual recall.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Location                      Associated Entity
1. Assam                           :   Gupta artistic influence
2. Bengal                          :   Pala artistic style
3. Brahmaputra Valley             :   Ahom Kingdom
4. Rangagora Tea Estate          :   British colonial rule
5. DaParvatia                       :   Assamese sculptures


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 5 only
(c) 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Assam's art and architecture show a clear influence of the Gupta idiom, demonstrating cultural exchange and interaction during historical periods. The Pala dynasty, known for its significant contributions to Buddhist art, primarily flourished in Bengal, resulting in a distinct Pala artistic style. The Brahmaputra Valley was the heartland of the powerful Ahom kingdom, which ruled a large part of Assam for centuries. The Rangagora Tea Estate exemplifies the impact of British colonial rule on Assam's economy and landscape, as tea cultivation became a major industry under British control.  Finally, DaParvatia is indeed a location in Assam known for its sculptures, reflecting the region's rich artistic heritage.  Therefore, all five pairs demonstrate accurate associations between locations and their associated entities.  There are no incorrect or misleading pairings in this question.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Event             Location Primarily Affected
1. Partition of Bengal           :   Assam
2. Moamaria Revolt               :   Bengal
3. Khmpati rebellion             :   Assam
4.  Agitation against ‘Cunningham Circular’ : Bengal
5.  Indigo Revolt                 :   Assam


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) Only 1


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Partition of Bengal directly impacted Assam, as some districts were transferred to the newly created province. The Khmpati rebellion was indeed a significant event within the Assam region.  However, the Moamaria Revolt primarily occurred in Assam, not Bengal. The Agitation against the ‘Cunningham Circular’ was a significant event in Assam, not Bengal. The Indigo Revolt was concentrated in Bengal, not Assam. Options (b), (c), and (d) therefore contain incorrect pairings. Only options 1 and 3 accurately reflect the primary location affected by these historical events.


**3. With reference to the British revenue policies in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Revenue System            Primary Region of Implementation
1. Ryotwari System           :   North-Western Provinces
2. Mahalwari System          :   Madras Presidency
3. Permanent Settlement      :   Bengal and Bihar


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 3 only

**Explanation:**

Only the third pair is correctly matched. The Permanent Settlement was primarily implemented in Bengal and Bihar. The Ryotwari system was predominantly implemented in Madras and Bombay Presidencies, not the North-Western Provinces. The Mahalwari system was implemented in the North-Western Provinces, Central Provinces, and Punjab, not the Madras Presidency.  Options (a), (c), and (d) include incorrectly matched pairs.  Therefore, only option (b) accurately reflects the primary region of implementation for the Permanent Settlement.
