**5. With reference to the Indian Legislative Council, consider the following pairs:**

    Person                       Role/Association
1. Vithalbhai Patel             :   Speaker, Central Legislative Assembly
2.  Harbilas Sarda              :   Member, Central Legislative Assembly
3.  Muhammad Yakub             :   Governor-General of India


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) Only 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Vithalbhai Patel was indeed the first non-official member elected as Speaker of the Central Legislative Assembly. Harbilas Sarda was a prominent member of the Central Legislative Assembly.  However, Muhammad Yakub was not the Governor-General of India; this role was held by various individuals during different periods of British rule. Options (b), (c), and (d) are therefore incomplete or incorrect.  Option (a) accurately reflects the correct roles and associations of Vithalbhai Patel and Harbilas Sarda with the Central Legislative Assembly.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Land Tenure System          Region of Implementation
1. Ryotwari System             :   Bihar
2. Zamindari System            :   Madras Presidency
3. Mahalwari System            :   North-Western Provinces

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Mahalwari system was primarily implemented in the North-Western Provinces (now Uttar Pradesh and Uttarakhand), parts of the Punjab, and Central Provinces.  The Ryotwari system was predominantly implemented in Madras Presidency (present-day Tamil Nadu, Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka, and Kerala), and parts of Bombay Presidency. The Zamindari system was introduced in Bengal, Bihar, Orissa, Banaras (Varanasi), and parts of northern Madras.  Option 1 is incorrect because the Ryotwari system was not a primary feature of Bihar; Option 2 is incorrect because the Zamindari system's core area was not the Madras Presidency; Option 4 is incorrect as only option 3 is correct. Therefore, only option (c) is the correct answer.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the specific geographical application of different land revenue systems under British rule in India, highlighting the nuances of colonial administration and its impact on various regions. The distractors are designed to test the candidate's in-depth understanding of the subject, rather than superficial knowledge.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                      Key Characteristic
1.  Permanent Settlement          :  Introduced in 1813
2.  Charter Act of 1833           :  Established the Board of Control
3.  Government of India Act 1858 :  Created the office of the Secretary of State for India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Permanent Settlement, a key land revenue system, was implemented starting in 1793 under Lord Cornwallis, not 1813. The Charter Act of 1833 didn't establish the Board of Control; that was established by Pitt's India Act of 1784.  The Government of India Act of 1858, however, did indeed create the office of the Secretary of State for India, transferring the governance of India from the East India Company to the British Crown. Therefore, only statement 3 is correctly matched. This question assesses factual recall regarding significant legislative acts and policies during British rule in India and tests the candidate's ability to differentiate between closely related historical events. The incorrect options serve as plausible distractors, requiring precise knowledge to eliminate them.


**3. With reference to the British colonial economy in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Economic Policy/System      Effect on Indigenous Capitalism
1. Laissez-faire                 :   Actively promoted indigenous capitalism
2. Permanent Settlement         :   Strengthened indigenous merchant class
3. White collective monopoly     :   Inhibited indigenous capitalism

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The laissez-faire policy, while often associated with free markets, did not actively promote indigenous capitalism in India. The British implemented it selectively, often to their own advantage, hindering the growth of Indian businesses. The Permanent Settlement, while creating a class of zamindars, didn't significantly strengthen the indigenous merchant class; in fact, it often led to their exploitation.  The "white collective monopoly," however, is accurately described as a system that directly inhibited the growth of indigenous capitalism through controlled trade and resource extraction. This question assesses the candidate's understanding of the complex interplay between British economic policies and the development (or lack thereof) of indigenous capitalism in India.  The distractors test a nuanced understanding of the colonial economic system and the limitations of applying simplistic economic theories to a complex historical context.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                           Role/Association
1. Lord Cornwallis                  :   Implementation of Ryotwari System
2. Lord Ripon                       :   Introduction of Non-Official Majority in Local Bodies
3. Lord Dalhousie                   :   Abolition of Sati

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Lord Cornwallis is known for the implementation of the Permanent Settlement, not the Ryotwari System.  Thomas Munro is associated with the Ryotwari System. Lord Ripon's administration saw the introduction of a policy that aimed for a non-official majority in local bodies, a crucial step towards self-governance. Lord William Bentinck is credited with the abolition of Sati, not Lord Dalhousie.  Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of key figures in British India and their association with specific administrative and social reforms. The incorrect pairing of Lord Cornwallis with the Ryotwari system acts as a strong distractor, requiring precise knowledge to answer correctly.


**5. With reference to the 19th-century Indian education system, consider the following pairs:**

   Educational Policy/Act              Characteristic
1. English Education Act of 1835    :   Emphasis on Sanskrit and Persian learning
2. Wood's Dispatch of 1854           :   Establishment of universities in Calcutta, Bombay, and Madras
3. Hunter Commission Report of 1882 :   Advocated for mass education

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The English Education Act of 1835 prioritized English as the medium of instruction, not Sanskrit and Persian. The Wood's Dispatch of 1854 played a significant role in laying the foundation for the establishment of universities in major cities, influencing the structure of the Indian education system. While the Hunter Commission Report did address the issue of education, it didn't specifically advocate for widespread mass education; its focus was more on improving the existing system.  Hence, only statement 2 is accurately matched. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of educational policies and their impact, requiring a precise understanding of the nuances of each policy's implementation. The distractors are constructed to challenge the candidate's comprehension of the historical context.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Land Tenure System          Associated Feature
1. Ryotwari System             :   Land revenue collected directly from cultivators
2. Zamindari System            :   Intermediaries (zamindars) collected land revenue
3. Mahalwari System           :   Revenue assessment based on village communities

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Ryotwari system, primarily implemented in Madras and Bombay Presidencies, involved the direct collection of land revenue from individual cultivators (ryots).  The Zamindari system, prevalent in Bengal, Bihar, and parts of eastern India, established zamindars as intermediaries who collected revenue from peasants and paid a share to the British government. The Mahalwari system, implemented in parts of North India, assessed revenue based on village communities (mahals) as a collective unit. All three pairs accurately reflect the core features of these land revenue systems. Option (a) is incorrect as it only includes one correct pair. Option (b) is partially correct but omits the Mahalwari system. Option (d) is incorrect as it only includes one correct pair, neglecting the accurate representation of the Ryotwari and Zamindari systems.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                  Key Provision
1. Charter Act of 1833            :   Established a separate legislative council in Bombay
2. Government of India Act 1919   :   Introduced Dyarchy in provinces
3. Government of India Act 1935   :   Abolished Dyarchy in provinces

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1833 significantly restructured the governance of India, but did not establish a separate legislative council in Bombay.  The Bombay Presidency, like other regions, was under the Governor-General's control.  The Government of India Act of 1919, also known as the Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms, famously introduced the system of Dyarchy, dividing subjects into 'reserved' and 'transferred' categories. The Government of India Act of 1935 abolished Dyarchy, granting greater provincial autonomy. Therefore, only the second pair is correctly matched. Option (a), (c), and (d) are all incorrect because they include the mismatched pair relating to the Charter Act of 1833.

   Person                             Role/Association

3. Thomas Munro                        :   Introduction of the Ryotwari System


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Cornwallis, as Governor-General, is directly associated with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement of land revenue in Bengal. Lord William Bentinck, also a Governor-General, is known for his social reforms, including the abolition of Sati. Thomas Munro, a significant figure in the administration of Madras Presidency, played a crucial role in the development and implementation of the Ryotwari system of land revenue. All three pairs accurately represent the historical connections between these individuals and their respective actions or policies.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are therefore incorrect, as they exclude at least one of these correctly matched pairs.

**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Governor-General/Viceroy    Significant Administrative Reform

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three

Lord Dalhousie's tenure as Governor-General is significantly marked by the implementation of the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy that led to the annexation of several Indian states. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                     Provision
1. Charter Act of 1793                :   Extended the Company's trade monopoly for 20 years
2. Pitt's India Act of 1784             :   Established a Board of Control to oversee the Company
3. Regulating Act of 1773              :   Created the post of Governor-General of Bengal
4. Charter Act of 1813                : Abolished the Company's monopoly on trade with China except for tea


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1793 indeed extended the East India Company's trade monopoly in India for another two decades.  This was a crucial element of the Act, solidifying the Company's economic power and control over Indian trade.  Pitt's India Act of 1784 established the Board of Control, a significant step in increasing British government oversight of the Company's activities in India. This marked a shift towards greater direct control from the British Crown. The Regulating Act of 1773 is correctly paired with the creation of the Governor-General of Bengal, a pivotal position that centralized administrative power within the Company's territories.  The Charter Act of 1813 partially ended the Company's trade monopoly, but it's important to note that the monopoly on the tea trade with China remained.  Therefore, option (d) is incorrect as it incorrectly describes the Charter Act of 1813. Options (a) and (b) are incomplete, failing to include all the correctly matched pairs.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                  Action/Association
1. Lord Cornwallis                        :   Implemented the Permanent Settlement
2. Lord Wellesley                         :   Founded the Fort William College
3. Raja Ram Mohan Roy                   :   Collaborated with David Hare on Hindu College
4.  Maulana Abul Kalam Azad             : Founded Al-Hilal


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Lord Cornwallis is rightly associated with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement, a significant land revenue system in Bengal.  Lord Wellesley's establishment of Fort William College is well-documented, aiming to train civil servants in Indian languages and culture. Raja Ram Mohan Roy's collaboration with David Hare in establishing Hindu College is also historically accurate, marking a crucial step in the introduction of Western education in India.  Finally, Maulana Abul Kalam Azad's founding of the Urdu newspaper Al-Hilal is a known fact.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched, making option (d) the correct answer.  The other options are incorrect because they exclude one or more of these historically accurate pairings.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                         Key Impact
1. Charter Act of 1793                 :   Separated revenue administration from judiciary
2. Government of India Act, 1919       :   Introduced Dyarchy in provinces
3. Indian Councils Act, 1861           :   Introduced the portfolio system
4. Government of India Act, 1935       : Abolished Dyarchy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1793 is correctly linked to the separation of revenue administration from judicial functions. This was a significant administrative reform. The Government of India Act, 1919, indeed introduced the system of Dyarchy (dual governance) in the provinces, a step towards limited self-government.  The Indian Councils Act of 1861 introduced the portfolio system, where executive council members headed specific departments, laying the foundation for a more structured cabinet system.  The Government of India Act, 1935, abolished Dyarchy, replacing it with provincial autonomy, thus making option (d) incorrect. Options (a) and (b) are incomplete, omitting correctly matched pairs.

**Correct Answer:** (c)

Lord William Bentinck's abolition of Sati is a landmark event in social reform during British rule in India. Kumar was involved in the Ghadar movement but didn't publish *Free India*.  The question tests factual recall of individuals and their associated publications.  The distractors are designed to be plausible, leveraging the close association of some individuals with movements or publications other than those explicitly stated in the correct pairings. For instance, Annie Besant's association with *New India* and Gandhi's with *Young India* are well-known, making these incorrect pairings deceptively appealing.  Similarly, G.D. Kumar's involvement in the Ghadar movement might lead candidates to incorrectly associate him with *Free India*. Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires a nuanced understanding of the historical context of Dutch and other European presence in India, specifically focusing on their trade, territorial acquisitions, and interactions with Indian rulers and entities.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Dutch East India Company Action              Location/Entity
    1.  Established a major trading post          :   Surat
    2.  Secured a farman from                     :   Bijapur Sultanate
    3.  Competed fiercely with                     :   English East India Company
    4.  Ousted from key coastal forts by          :   British East India Company
    5.  Dominated the spice trade in             :   Malabar Coast


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Dutch East India Company (VOC) did indeed establish a significant trading post in Surat, a major port city in Gujarat. This was crucial for their access to Indian textiles and other goods.  Their intense rivalry with the English East India Company is well-documented, marked by periods of cooperation and conflict as both vied for control of lucrative trade routes and markets within India.

Option (b) is incorrect because while the VOC did operate on the Malabar Coast, their dominance of the spice trade there was not absolute.  The Portuguese, for example, initially held significant power in the region.  Option (c) is wrong because the complete ouster of the Dutch by the British was a gradual process, not a single event. The British gradually gained ascendancy in the 18th century, but the Dutch maintained a presence for some time. Option (d) is incorrect because the VOC obtaining a farman from the Bijapur Sultanate is not entirely accurate; while they interacted with various Indian powers to secure trading rights, a direct farman from Bijapur is not consistently supported by historical evidence.  The focus was more on Golconda and other kingdoms.


**2. With reference to the Dutch presence in India, consider the following pairs:**

    Geographical Area                Dutch Activity
    1.  Coromandel Coast                :   Establishment of multiple factories
    2.  Pulicat                              :   Initial base of operations
    3.  Bengal                               :   Limited trading presence
    4.  Gujarat                              :   Significant textile trade
    5.  Spice Islands (Indonesia)        :  Primary focus of colonial expansion


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, and 5 only
(d) All of the above


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

The Dutch established a network of factories along the Coromandel Coast to facilitate trade in textiles and other goods.  Pulicat served as one of their early key settlements in India.  Their trade in textiles was especially significant in Gujarat. While the Dutch had some commercial interests in Bengal, it wasn't a major area of focus compared to other regions. The Dutch East India Company's primary colonial ambitions and resources were directed toward the Spice Islands of Indonesia, where they dominated the spice trade for a considerable period.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

    Mughal Emperor                     Interaction with the English East India Company
    1. Jahangir                              : Granted permission for the establishment of factories in Surat
    2. Shah Jahan                           :  Conceded trading rights in specific locations
    3. Aurangzeb                            : Imposed restrictions on Company activities
    4. Akbar                                 : Initial contact and limited trade agreements
    5. Farrukhsiyar                         : Granted significant privileges through farmans


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 3, and 5 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

Jahangir's reign saw the granting of permission to the English East India Company to establish factories, notably in Surat. Aurangzeb, known for his conservative policies, imposed restrictions on the Company's activities and expansion.  Farrukhsiyar's reign was marked by the granting of significant privileges to the Company through farmans, which provided considerable legal and economic advantages.

Options (a) and (c) are partially correct but incomplete. While Akbar did have initial interactions with the English, it didn't involve extensive trade agreements.  Shah Jahan's policies towards the Company were more nuanced and varied than simply conceding trading rights. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes inaccurate pairings of Mughal Emperors with their policies toward the English East India Company.


**4. With reference to the economic impact of the Industrial Revolution on India during the 19th century, consider the following pairs:**

    Impact                                      Specific Example
    1. Decline of Indian textiles                  :  High tariffs imposed on Indian textiles in Britain
    2. Growth of Indian railways                 :  Facilitated the export of raw materials from India
    3.  Rise of Indian-owned industries          :  Establishment of the first cotton mill in Bombay
    4.  Increased agricultural commercialization :  Shift towards cash crops like cotton and jute
    5.  Deindustrialization of India              :  The closure of many traditional weaving workshops


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) All of the above


**Correct Answer:** (d) All of the above

**Explanation:**

The Industrial Revolution in Britain directly impacted India's economy. High tariffs in Britain effectively shut out Indian textiles from British markets, leading to the decline of the Indian textile industry. The construction of railways in India facilitated the export of raw materials, benefiting British industries but harming Indian ones.  The establishment of the first cotton mill in Bombay represents the early stages of modern industrialization in India, although this was a limited response to the overall deindustrialization.  The shift towards cash crops such as cotton and jute exemplifies the commercialization of Indian agriculture, driven by British demand.  The closure of many traditional weaving workshops, alongside other craft industries, is a clear example of the deindustrialization that India experienced under British rule.  All the pairs accurately reflect aspects of the multifaceted economic impact of the Industrial Revolution on India.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    British Policy in India                     Consequence
    1.  One-way free trade                      :  Flooding of Indian markets with cheap British goods
    2.  Excessive land revenue demands        :  Increased rural indebtedness
    3.  Promotion of cash crops                 :  Vulnerability to international price fluctuations
    4.  Lack of tariff protection for Indian industries:  Suppression of indigenous industries
    5.  Investment in railways                  :  Primarily benefited British industries


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 1, 3, and 5 only
(c) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) All of the above


**Correct Answer:** (d) All of the above

**Explanation:**

The British implemented policies in India that had profound and largely negative consequences for the Indian economy. One-way free trade policy allowed the import of cheap British manufactured goods into India without reciprocal benefits for Indian products.  Excessive land revenue demands imposed on Indian peasants led to widespread indebtedness and poverty.  The British promotion of cash crops made Indian agriculture dependent on global markets and vulnerable to price shocks.  The lack of tariff protection for Indian industries allowed British industries to dominate the Indian market, leading to the decline of indigenous industries.  The British investment in railways, while improving infrastructure, primarily served British economic interests.  Each pair accurately depicts a British policy and its related negative impact on the Indian economy.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Ruler                      Action/Policy
1. Akbar                     Introduced the Dahsala system of land revenue
2. Jahangir                  Granted permission to the English East India Company to establish factories in India
3. Aurangzeb                 Abolished the Jizya tax
4. Bahadur Shah I            Released Shahu, the Maratha prince, from Mughal captivity
5. Muhammad Shah           Witnessed the establishment of the independent state of Hyderabad

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Akbar is known for his land revenue reforms, including the introduction of the Dahsala system (ten-year settlement).  Jahangir's reign saw the expansion of the English East India Company's presence in India, granting them permission to establish factories. Aurangzeb, despite his religious conservatism, temporarily abolished the Jizya tax at certain points in his reign. Bahadur Shah I, adopting a relatively conciliatory approach, released Shahu, a significant Maratha leader, from captivity. Finally, Muhammad Shah's reign was marked by the weakening of central authority, leading to the emergence of independent states like Hyderabad under Nizam-ul-Mulk.  The options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.  This question tests factual recall and understanding of Mughal administrative and political history.  It also requires the candidate to differentiate between various Mughal emperors and their distinct policies.  The distractors in the incorrect options are designed to test the candidate's depth of knowledge and ability to eliminate incorrect pairs based on historical accuracy.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   European Power       Action in India

(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

The English established Fort William in Calcutta, which became a crucial center of their power in Bengal. However, the Portuguese established their first factory in India at Kochi, not Surat, and the French established their earliest factory at Surat, not Pulicat.  Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they include at least one incorrectly matched pair. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of the establishment and expansion of European powers in India, requiring them to differentiate between the actions of different colonial entities. **3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Mughal Emperor         Significant Event During Reign

(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 3 only

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3 is correctly matched.  Muhammad Shah's reign coincided with Nadir Shah's devastating invasion of India in 1739. The other pairs are incorrect. The Third Battle of Panipat occurred during the reign of Alamgir II, not Jahangir. The Battle of Plassey took place during the reign of Alamgir II, not Aurangzeb.  The Battle of Buxar occurred during the reign of Shah Alam II, not Alamgir II. Options (a), (b), and (d) are therefore incorrect because they include at least one incorrectly matched pair. **4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                    Association with the English East India Company
1. Jahangir                  Granted the Company its first farman

3. Aurangzeb                 Initially hostile, later allowed the Company to resume trade after the sack of Hooghly

(d) 1, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, and 4

Farrukhsiyar, in 1717, issued a farman confirming and extending previous trading rights, significantly expanding the Company's influence. Aurangzeb, after an initial period of hostility following the sack of Hooghly, eventually allowed the Company to resume trading activities. Shah Alam II, under pressure, granted the Company the Diwani rights, giving them control over revenue collection in Bengal, Bihar, and Orissa – a pivotal step in the Company's rise to power.  The incorrect options (a), (b), and (d) are flawed because they inaccurately exclude at least one of the correctly matched pairs. **7. With reference to 18th-century India, consider the following pairs:**

   Battle                       Outcome
1. Battle of Plassey           British victory, establishing their dominance in Bengal
2. Battle of Buxar            Solidified British control over Bengal, Bihar, and Orissa
3. Third Battle of Panipat     Maratha victory, securing their supremacy in North India


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Only the first two pairs are correctly matched. The Battle of Plassey led to a decisive British victory, marking the beginning of their dominance in Bengal.  The Battle of Buxar further consolidated British control over Bengal, Bihar, and Orissa. The Third Battle of Panipat, however, resulted in a decisive victory for Ahmad Shah Abdali, weakening the Maratha Empire significantly, not securing their supremacy.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are thus incorrect because they either include the incorrectly matched pair related to the Third Battle of Panipat or omit correctly matched pairs. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of significant 18th-century battles in India and their consequences for the power dynamics in the region. The mismatched pair related to the Third Battle of Panipat is designed to test the candidate's deep understanding of this pivotal event and its ramifications.


**8. With reference to the decline of the Mughal Empire, consider the following pairs:**

   Factor                        Contribution to Decline
1. Aurangzeb's religious policies Increased discontent among Hindu population, leading to rebellions
2. Weak successors             Inability to effectively administer the vast empire, leading to regional fragmentation
3. Jagirdari crisis              Shortage of land grants to nobles, leading to internal conflicts and instability
4. External invasions           Continuous incursions from the northwest, weakening the empire’s defenses


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs accurately reflect factors contributing to the decline of the Mughal Empire. Aurangzeb's rigid religious policies alienated many Hindu groups, sparking rebellions that weakened the empire. The succession of weak and incompetent rulers after Aurangzeb's death led to administrative chaos and the rise of independent regional powers. The jagirdari crisis, characterized by a shortage of land grants for the nobility, fueled internal conflicts and destabilized the empire.  Finally, repeated invasions from the northwest, particularly by Nadir Shah and Ahmad Shah Abdali, severely weakened the Mughal military and political structure. The incorrect options (a), (b), and (c) incorrectly exclude at least one correctly matched pair. This question requires a comprehensive understanding of the multifaceted causes of the Mughal decline, encompassing political, religious, economic, and military factors. The question's difficulty is enhanced by the inclusion of all correctly matched pairs, requiring the candidate to possess a substantial level of knowledge about the topic.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on the early European presence in India.  Each question adheres to the specified format and criteria.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Location             Early European Presence
1. Surat                 Portuguese factory
2. Pulicat               Dutch factory
3. Cochin                Portuguese fort
4. Qasim Bazar          French factory

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (c) because while the Portuguese did establish a presence in Surat, and the Dutch in Pulicat,  the earliest significant presence for those powers were elsewhere.  The Portuguese initially focused on Goa, establishing a crucial foothold in 1510, and the Dutch prioritized Pulicat as a trading post among their other enterprises.  The statement about Cochin is correct; the Portuguese established a major fort there, signifying their early and significant presence in the region.  The French did indeed establish their factory at Qasim Bazar, marking their early presence in Bengal.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they incorrectly attribute the earliest significant European presence to specific locations for certain powers.  The question tests factual recall and understanding of the geographic distribution of early European colonial activity in India.


**2. With reference to the early establishment of European trading posts in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Trading Company       Location of Earliest Factory
1. English East India Company  :   Surat
2. Dutch East India Company     :   Pulicat
3. French East India Company    :   Cochin
4. Portuguese East India Company :   Masulipatnam

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct option is (b). The English East India Company's earliest factory was not in Surat; while they traded there extensively, their first factory was established in Masulipatnam. The Dutch East India Company's earliest factory was indeed at Pulicat. The French East India Company's earliest significant establishment was at Surat (though later at Qasim Bazar).  The Portuguese East India Company's earliest major factory was in Cochin. This question tests the examinee's knowledge of the chronology and geography of European trading company establishments in India. The distractors utilize plausible yet incorrect information to challenge the candidates' depth of knowledge.

**3. With reference to the European presence in India, consider the following pairs:**

   European Power      Major Early Settlement/Fort
1. Portuguese           Surat
2. Dutch                 Masulipatnam
3. French                Pondicherry
4. English               Goa

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only option (b) is correct.  While the Portuguese, Dutch, and English all had significant presence in the locations mentioned in the other pairs, their *major* early settlements differed. The Portuguese primarily established Goa as their major early settlement, the Dutch focused on Pulicat, and the English established Madras (Fort St. George) as their main base. The French established Pondicherry as a major settlement, making option (b) the only correct match.  This question evaluates the candidate's understanding of the dominant early settlements of each European power and their strategic importance.  The other options include plausible but incorrect pairings to increase the difficulty level.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Entity                      Association
1.  Thanjavur school of painting     :   Vijayanagara Empire
2.  Malwa                        :   Maratha control
3.  Shivaji                       :   Portuguese rivalry
4.  Aurangzeb                     :   Maratha negotiations


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because it accurately reflects the historical associations.  The Marathas significantly controlled the Malwa region, establishing their power and influence in the Deccan. Shivaji, the founder of the Maratha Empire, engaged in constant rivalry with the Portuguese for dominance in coastal regions and trade. Aurangzeb, the Mughal emperor, engaged in prolonged negotiations and conflicts with the Marathas throughout his reign.

Option (a) is incorrect because the Thanjavur school of painting was primarily patronized by the Nayakas of Thanjavur, not the Vijayanagara Empire. Although the Vijayanagara Empire had a significant influence on the region, the direct patronage of the Thanjavur school is attributed to the Nayakas.

Option (b) is partially correct, as it correctly identifies the Maratha control of Malwa and Shivaji's rivalry with the Portuguese. However, it omits the important interaction between Aurangzeb and the Marathas, which is a crucial aspect of the period.

Option (c) is incorrect as it only includes the accurate pairing of Shivaji and Portuguese rivalry, neglecting the equally significant relationships between the Marathas and Malwa and Aurangzeb and the Marathas.  A comprehensive understanding of the Maratha's rise requires acknowledging these multiple interactions.

   Historical Figure        Action/Association

Malik Ambar, a prominent Abyssinian general, led Maratha forces during a critical period of their early development and expansion within the Deccan.  

Option (a), (c) and (d) are incorrect because they misrepresent the historical roles and actions of the named individuals. Nana Phadnavis, a highly influential Peshwa minister, was instrumental in the Maratha administration and diplomacy, but he did *not* sign the Treaty of Bassein; that was the Peshwa Baji Rao II.  Tipu Sultan's interactions were primarily with the British, not Aurangzeb.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Mughal Emperor       Significant Event During Reign
1. Bahadur Shah I        :   Suppression of Banda Bahadur's Sikh rebellion
2. Jahandar Shah        :   Abolition of Jizya tax by Zulfiqar Khan
3. Farrukhsiyar          :   Granting of farmans to the British East India Company
4. Muhammad Shah       :   Invasion of Nadir Shah

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched based on established historical accounts. Bahadur Shah I's reign is indeed marked by his campaign against Banda Bahadur, the prominent Sikh leader who challenged Mughal authority in Punjab.  Jahandar Shah's reign, though short, is notable for Zulfiqar Khan's administrative actions, including the abolition of the Jizya tax, a significant policy shift.  Farrukhsiyar granted farmans (edicts) to the British East India Company, which were crucial in establishing their foothold in India.  Finally, Muhammad Shah's reign saw the devastating invasion of Nadir Shah, a major turning point in Mughal decline.  These events are well-documented and consistently featured in standard historical narratives of the Mughal Empire's decline. The options provided offer plausible distractors by isolating specific events, but a thorough understanding of the Mughal period confirms the accuracy of all four pairings.

   Regional State Founder  Capital City

(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The correct answer highlights the founding and capital cities of three significant regional states that emerged during the decline of the Mughal Empire. Awadh, founded by Saadat Khan, had Lucknow as its capital. Bengal, under Murshid Quli Khan, established Murshidabad as its administrative center. Mysore, initially under the Wodeyars and later ruled by Hyder Ali and Tipu Sultan, had Seringapatam as its prominent capital. Option (c) incorrectly pairs Hyderabad with Aurangabad.  While Aurangabad held historical significance for the Mughal empire and was later associated with the Nizams, Hyderabad was the actual capital of the independent Nizam's dominion.    Person                  Title/Position

   Mughal Emperor   Policy/Action

Jahandar Shah’s reign saw the implementation of the Ijara system, a regressive revenue-farming practice under Zulfiqar Khan. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Governor General       Action Related to Bengal
    1. Lord Curzon          : Introduced the Bengal Partition
    2. Lord Wellesley        : Implemented the Subsidiary Alliance System in Bengal
    3. Lord Dalhousie       : Annexed Awadh, impacting Bengal's trade routes
    4. Warren Hastings      :  Established the Supreme Court in Bengal


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Lord Curzon's administration saw the controversial Partition of Bengal in 1905, aiming to weaken the nationalist movement in the province.  Lord Wellesley's aggressive expansionist policies significantly impacted Bengal through the Subsidiary Alliance System, bringing several Indian states under British influence and altering the political and economic landscape of the region. Lord Dalhousie's annexation of Awadh in 1856 directly affected Bengal's trade routes and economic stability, disrupting established commercial networks.  While Warren Hastings was Governor-General of Bengal, the Supreme Court was established in Calcutta during his tenure, but its establishment was under the Regulating Act of 1773, not solely his action. Therefore, option (d) is incorrect. Options (a) and (b) are incomplete, omitting correctly matched pairs.

**7. With reference to the early establishment of European trading companies in India, consider the following pairs:**

    2. Dutch          : Second
    3. English         : Third
    4. French         : Fourth

(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**8. Consider the following statements:**

    1. The Portuguese initially maintained relatively tolerant relations with Hindus.
    2. The Dutch primarily focused their commercial efforts on the spice trade of the East Indies.
    3. The English East India Company's early success was largely due to its superior naval power.
    4.  The French East India Company’s ambition for territorial control hindered its financial stability.

(a) 1 and 2 only

(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

All four statements are accurate reflections of historical events.  The Portuguese, while persecuting Muslims, initially showed more tolerance towards Hindus.  The Dutch prioritized the lucrative spice trade of Indonesia over establishing a vast empire in India.  The English benefited greatly from their superior naval strength, facilitating trade and military operations. The French, prioritizing territorial ambitions over pure commerce, often faced financial difficulties due to costly military campaigns.  These statements accurately capture key aspects of the European experience in India.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Ruler              Action/Policy
1. Aurangzeb          Abolished the Jizya tax permanently.
2. Bahadur Shah I     Conciliated the Sikhs by granting Guru Gobind Singh a high mansab.
3. Muhammad Shah     Founded the independent state of Hyderabad.
4. Jahandar Shah       Introduced the Ijara system to improve finances.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 4 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Aurangzeb's policy was actually characterized by the *reimposition* of the Jizya tax, a significant factor contributing to the decline of the Mughal empire. Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect. Bahadur Shah I, known for his conciliatory approach, did indeed grant Guru Gobind Singh a high mansab, making statement 2 correct.  Muhammad Shah's reign witnessed the *establishment* of independent states, including Hyderabad, but he did not found it. Nizam-ul-Mulk is credited with founding Hyderabad. Thus, statement 3 is incorrect. Jahandar Shah, under the influence of Zulfikar Khan, did introduce the Ijara system, a revenue farming system, in an attempt to improve the empire's financial condition, making statement 4 correct.  The Ijara system, while initially intended to improve finances, ultimately led to increased oppression of peasants.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Mughal Emperor      Significant Event During Reign
1. Aurangzeb           Battle of Plassey
2. Bahadur Shah I      War of Succession
3. Alamgir II           Death of Guru Tegh Bahadur
4. Muhammad Shah      Nadir Shah's invasion


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Battle of Plassey occurred during the reign of Alamgir II, not Aurangzeb.  Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect.  Bahadur Shah I's ascension to the throne was indeed preceded by a protracted war of succession, making statement 2 correct. The execution of Guru Tegh Bahadur took place during the reign of Aurangzeb, not Alamgir II. Therefore, statement 3 is incorrect.  Nadir Shah's devastating invasion of India occurred during the reign of Muhammad Shah, making statement 4 correct.  Nadir Shah's invasion significantly weakened the Mughal Empire and is a crucial event in 18th-century Indian history. The other options incorrectly link events to the wrong rulers.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Military Leader/Ruler    Outcome/Action
1.  Sir Eyre Coote           Defeated Tipu Sultan in the Third Anglo-Mysore War
2.  Haidar Ali              Defeated by the British in the Battle of Porto Novo
3.  Tipu Sultan             Signed the Treaty of Mangalore
4.  Robert Clive            Expelled by Aurangzeb


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Sir Eyre Coote was a prominent British general, but he is primarily associated with victories against Haidar Ali, not Tipu Sultan, in the Second Anglo-Mysore War.  Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect. Haidar Ali was indeed defeated by the British at Porto Novo under the command of Sir Eyre Coote, making statement 2 correct.  Tipu Sultan did sign the Treaty of Mangalore, marking a temporary end to hostilities with the British, making statement 3 correct. Robert Clive was a significant figure in the early stages of British expansion in India but was never expelled by Aurangzeb; Sir John Child was expelled.  Therefore, statement 4 is incorrect. The other options incorrectly pair individuals with events or outcomes.


**4.  Consider the following pairs:**

   Policy/Event              Impact on Mughal Empire
1. Aurangzeb's Deccan Policy:  Strengthened the Mughal Empire's southern frontiers.
2.  Reimposition of Jizya Tax: Led to widespread revolts and weakened the empire.
3.  Wars of Succession:     Contributed to the empire's fragmentation and decline.
4.  Nadir Shah's Invasion:   Brought about a period of relative peace and stability.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Aurangzeb's prolonged campaigns in the Deccan, far from strengthening the empire, drained its resources and weakened its overall stability. This prolonged military engagement in the south significantly distracted from other areas and weakened the central government. Thus, statement 1 is incorrect. The reimposition of the Jizya tax alienated the Hindu population, leading to widespread revolts and contributing significantly to the weakening of the empire. Thus, statement 2 is correct. The frequent wars of succession following Aurangzeb's death plunged the empire into chaos and weakened its central authority, paving the way for the rise of regional powers. This internal conflict further fragmented the empire. Thus, statement 3 is correct.  Nadir Shah's invasion was catastrophic, leading to immense devastation and plunder, further weakening the Mughal Empire, not establishing peace and stability. Thus, statement 4 is incorrect.  Only options (b) correctly identifies the pairs with accurate impacts.



**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Mughal Ruler             Characteristic/Policy
1.  Bahadur Shah I           Known for his policy of religious tolerance and conciliation.
2.  Farrukhsiyar            Successfully resisted the power of the Sayyid brothers.
3.  Muhammad Shah          Ruled during the invasion of Nadir Shah.
4.  Alamgir II              Oversaw the Battle of Buxar.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Bahadur Shah I, unlike his father Aurangzeb, adopted a more conciliatory approach, particularly towards the Hindus, and is known for his relatively tolerant policies. This is an accurate reflection of his reign. Therefore, statement 1 is correct. Farrukhsiyar's reign was characterized by a power struggle with the Sayyid brothers, whom he ultimately failed to resist, leading to his deposition and death. Therefore, statement 2 is incorrect.  Muhammad Shah's reign is indeed notable for the devastating invasion of Nadir Shah, a turning point in Mughal history. Therefore, statement 3 is correct. The Battle of Buxar took place during the reign of Shah Alam II, not Alamgir II.  Therefore, statement 4 is incorrect.  Only option (a) accurately matches the Mughal rulers with their characteristics or policies.


**6. Consider the following pairs:**

   Regional Power       Key Figure/Founder

2.  Awadh               Nizam-ul-Mulk

(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

**7. Consider the following pairs:**

   Treaty/Agreement      Significance/Outcome
1. Treaty of Allahabad   Ended the Third Anglo-Mysore War.
2. Treaty of Mangalore  Granted the Diwani of Bengal, Bihar, and Orissa to the East India Company.
3.  Tripartite Treaty      Involved Ranjit Singh, Shah Shuja, and the British.
4. Treaty of Amritsar    Marked a temporary peace between Tipu Sultan and the British.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Treaty of Allahabad, signed in 1765, is correctly associated with the grant of the Diwani rights to the East India Company, not the end of the Third Anglo-Mysore War.  The Treaty of Seringapatam concluded that war.  Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect. The Treaty of Mangalore ended the First Anglo-Mysore War, not granting the Diwani rights.  Therefore, statement 2 is incorrect. The Tripartite Treaty of 1838 is accurately described as involving Ranjit Singh, Shah Shuja, and the British, concerning the situation in Afghanistan. Therefore, statement 3 is correct. The Treaty of Mangalore, signed in 1784, established a temporary peace between Tipu Sultan and the British, not the Treaty of Amritsar. Therefore, statement 4 is incorrect. Only option (b) correctly identifies the accurately matched pair.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   City                     Significant Event/Institution
1. Madras                  First meeting of the Indian Social Conference
2. Calcutta                 Location of the Supreme Court
3. Bombay                  Establishment of the Arya Samaj
4. Dhaka                    Significant decline after the mid-eighteenth century

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Indian Social Conference held its first meeting in Madras in 1887, highlighting the growing social reform movement in India during the late 19th century.  The establishment of the Supreme Court in Calcutta in 1774 was a crucial step in the British legal system's expansion in India, signifying the assertion of British authority and the beginning of a new legal framework.  The Arya Samaj, founded by Swami Dayanand Saraswati in Bombay in 1875, played a pivotal role in promoting Vedic ideals and social reform, challenging traditional practices and contributing significantly to the socio-religious landscape of India.  Dhaka, a prominent commercial center in the earlier part of the 18th century, experienced a decline in its economic importance after the mid-18th century due to factors including the rise of Calcutta and shifting trade patterns under British rule.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.

**6. Consider the following pairs:**

    Event/Policy              Location Primarily Affected
1. Permanent Settlement      Bengal
2. Doctrine of Lapse         Several Princely States
3. Subsidiary Alliance       Awadh

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Permanent Settlement, a significant land revenue system, was primarily implemented in Bengal, having long-term consequences on land ownership and agrarian relations.  The Doctrine of Lapse, a controversial annexation policy, was applied to several princely states, leading to their incorporation into British India.  The Subsidiary Alliance, a key instrument of British foreign policy, was implemented in Awadh and other princely states, leading to their increasing dependence on British power.  All three pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (d) are thus incorrect.

(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Saadat Khan, also known as Burhan-ul-Mulk, is widely recognized as the founder of the Awadh state, establishing its independent status during the decline of the Mughal Empire.  Wajid Ali Shah was indeed the last Nawab of Awadh before its annexation by the British.  Lord Dalhousie implemented the Doctrine of Lapse, leading to the annexation of Awadh under his governorship.  Finally, Shuja-ud-Daulah was the Nawab of Awadh during the crucial Battle of Buxar, a significant event in the consolidation of British power in India. All four pairs accurately reflect historical facts related to the Awadh region and its rulers. **2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person/Group                     Action/Association with Banaras
1.  Brahmin pundits                  :   Established a major textile industry
2.  Ramananda                        :   Associated with the development of Banaras as a center of learning
3.  Muizzuddin                       :   Completely destroyed Banaras's infrastructure

(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Explanation:**

While Banaras (Varanasi) had a rich history of learning and religious significance,  the association of Brahmin pundits with a major textile industry is not a primary historical association;  the city's fame was more closely tied to its religious and scholarly importance.  Ramananda, a prominent Bhakti movement figure, is correctly linked to Banaras's development as a significant center of learning and religious activity, attracting scholars and devotees.  The extent of Muizzuddin's destruction of Banaras is debated historically, with sources indicating varying levels of damage, making "completely destroyed" an overstatement. Balwant Singh's successful defense against the Marathas is not definitively supported by primary historical sources, as the situation was more complex than a simple victory or defeat.  Therefore, only pair 2 represents an undisputed and accurate historical connection.

   Treaty/Agreement                 Outcome/Significance

(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Treaty of Surat did precede the First Anglo-Maratha War but did not conclude it. The Treaty of Purandar is correctly linked to the Maratha-Mughal conflict, representing a key moment in Shivaji's negotiations with the Mughals. The Convention of Wadgaon is accurately described as initially reversing British gains during the First Anglo-Maratha War. The Treaty of Salbai did not establish British dominance in South India; that was a gradual process involving multiple wars and treaties. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 present accurate and well-established historical connections.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader of the Revolt of 1857           Associated Location
1. Bahadur Shah Zafar                   :   Meerut
2. Rani Lakshmibai                     :   Jhansi
3. Nana Saheb                          :   Kanpur
4. Tantia Tope                         :   Gwalior


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Bahadur Shah Zafar, the last Mughal emperor, was declared the nominal leader of the 1857 revolt, which originated in Meerut due to the controversial greased cartridges of the Enfield rifle.  Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi played a crucial role in the rebellion, leading the fight from her state of Jhansi.  While Nana Saheb and Tantia Tope were significant participants in the 1857 revolt, their primary areas of operation were not solely limited to Kanpur and Gwalior respectively.  Nana Saheb's influence extended beyond Kanpur, and Tantia Tope's military activities encompassed a broader geographical area than just Gwalior. Therefore, options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they include these mismatched pairs.  Only the association of Bahadur Shah Zafar with Meerut and Rani Lakshmibai with Jhansi are definitively accurate as their primary centers of rebellion. The question tests factual recall and requires precise knowledge of the geographical locations associated with key figures of the 1857 revolt.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reformer                     Key Reform Advocated
1. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar           :   Abolition of Sati
2. Jyotiba Phule                        :   Widow Remarriage
3. Raja Ram Mohan Roy                  :   Establishment of the Arya Samaj


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was a prominent figure in the social reform movement in Bengal, actively campaigning for widow remarriage and women's education.  While he contributed to the overall reform movement that eventually led to the abolition of Sati, it was primarily Raja Ram Mohan Roy who spearheaded that particular reform. Jyotiba Phule, a significant social reformer in Maharashtra, championed the cause of widow remarriage and fought against caste discrimination.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy did not establish the Arya Samaj; that was Swami Dayanand Saraswati.  Therefore, option (d) is incorrect. Option (a) is incorrect because it omits Jyotiba Phule's significant contribution to widow remarriage reform. Option (c) is incorrect because it omits Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar's role.  The correct answer highlights the specific contributions of Vidyasagar and Phule to social reform, demonstrating the candidates' understanding of the nuances within the movement. The question tests factual recall and analytical skills to differentiate between the contributions of various social reformers.



**3.  With reference to the Socio-Religious Reform Movements in 19th Century India, consider the following pairs:**

   Organization                         Founder/Key Figure

3.  Satyashodhak Samaj                 :   Jyotiba Phule

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

While Keshab Chandra Sen was a significant figure in the Brahmo Samaj,  it was Raja Ram Mohan Roy who founded it.  Swami Dayanand Saraswati is correctly identified as the founder of the Arya Samaj, and Jyotiba Phule is correctly paired with the Satyashodhak Samaj, which he founded to address caste inequalities in Maharashtra.  Therefore, option (d) is incorrect because of the misattribution of the Brahmo Samaj's founder. Options (a) and (c) are also incorrect because they omit the correct pairings of Arya Samaj and Satyashodhak Samaj with their respective founders. This question tests factual recall of key figures and organizations associated with the 19th-century socio-religious reform movements in India, assessing the candidate's knowledge of the historical context.


**4. With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following pairs:**

   Participant                             Role/Association
1.  John Lawrence                       :   Governor-General of India during the revolt.
2.  Rani of Jhansi                       :   Leader of the rebellion in Jhansi.
3.  General Bakht Khan                  :   Military leader during the revolt in Delhi.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Lord Canning was the Governor-General of India during the 1857 revolt, not John Lawrence who was the Lieutenant Governor of the Punjab at that time and played a crucial role in suppressing the rebellion in the Punjab. Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi was a prominent leader of the rebellion in Jhansi, and General Bakht Khan was indeed a key military leader during the revolt, particularly in Delhi.  Therefore, option (c) is incorrect because it omits the correct matching of Rani Lakshmibai and General Bakht Khan. Option (b) is also incorrect due to the inaccurate pairing of John Lawrence.  Option (d) is incorrect because of the incorrect pairing of John Lawrence. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of key figures and their roles during the 1857 Revolt and emphasizes the importance of accurate factual recall.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reform Movement             Primary Goal
1. Self-Respect Movement             :   Upliftment of Dalits in Bihar
2. Satya Shodhak Samaj               :   Anti-caste movement in Maharashtra
3. Arya Samaj                         :   Reform of Hinduism through Vedic principles


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Self-Respect Movement, primarily led by E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker, focused on social justice and self-respect for the lower castes, particularly in South India, not Bihar.  The Satya Shodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotiba Phule, directly addressed caste inequalities in Maharashtra, making the second pair accurate.  The Arya Samaj, established by Swami Dayanand Saraswati, aimed to reform Hinduism by returning to what it considered the original Vedic principles, making the third pair correct.  Therefore, options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either misrepresent the goals of the Self-Respect Movement or omit the accurate pairings of the Satya Shodhak Samaj and Arya Samaj. This question assesses the candidate's understanding of the primary objectives of various social reform movements in India and their regional contexts.  It requires both factual recall and analytical skills.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reformer          Significant Contribution
1. Jyotirao Phule           :  Established the Satyashodhak Samaj
2. Gopal Hari Deshmukh    :   Founded the Prarthana Samaj
3. Pandita Ramabai         :  Established the Arya Mahila Samaj

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Jyotirao Phule's pioneering work in social reform in Maharashtra is well-documented. He founded the Satyashodhak Samaj, a movement dedicated to challenging caste discrimination and promoting social justice.  This organization played a crucial role in advocating for the rights of marginalized communities and pushing for educational opportunities for all, regardless of caste.  Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched.

Pandita Ramabai, a prominent social reformer and advocate for women's rights, established the Arya Mahila Samaj. This organization focused on improving the lives of women, particularly widows, through education and social support.  Her work significantly contributed to the women's rights movement in India. Therefore, pair 3 is correctly matched.

Pair 2 is incorrect. While Gopal Hari Deshmukh, known as Lokhitwadi, was a significant rationalist and social reformer in Maharashtra, he did not found the Prarthana Samaj.  The Prarthana Samaj was established by a different group of reformers.  This demonstrates the importance of precise factual knowledge in answering UPSC questions, as even closely related but incorrect information can lead to an incorrect response.  Understanding the specific contributions of each reformer is essential to accurately match the pairs.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization              Primary Area of Focus
1. Satyashodhak Samaj      :   Women's Education
2. Arya Samaj               :   Vedic Revivalism
3. Brahmo Samaj             :   Monotheistic Reform within Hinduism

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Arya Samaj, founded by Swami Dayananda Saraswati, was primarily focused on Vedic revivalism.  It aimed to purify Hinduism by returning to the original Vedic scriptures and rejecting later accretions of ritual and superstition.  The movement championed the authority of the Vedas and promoted a monotheistic interpretation of Hinduism.  Therefore, pair 2 is correctly matched.

The Brahmo Samaj, initiated by Raja Ram Mohan Roy, was a significant reformist movement within Hinduism. Its central tenet was the belief in one God, rejecting idolatry and polytheism.  It advocated for social reforms such as widow remarriage and women's education, aligning with broader humanist principles.  Therefore, pair 3 is correctly matched.

Pair 1 is incorrect. While the Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotirao Phule, did indirectly support women's education as part of its broader social reform agenda, its primary focus was on challenging caste discrimination and promoting social justice for the marginalized communities of Maharashtra.  The question tests the ability to distinguish between primary and secondary areas of focus for a given organization, a critical skill in UPSC-style analysis.  A superficial understanding of the movement could lead to incorrect matching.


**3. With reference to 19th-century social reform movements in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Social Issue Addressed       Prominent Advocate
1. Child Marriage               :   E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker
2. Widow Remarriage            :   Pandit Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar
3. Untouchability                :   Gopal Krishna Gokhale

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Pandit Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar's tireless advocacy for widow remarriage is a well-known aspect of 19th-century social reform in Bengal. His efforts played a pivotal role in the passage of the Hindu Widows' Remarriage Act of 1856, a landmark legislation that legalized the practice.  His deep understanding of Hindu scriptures and his persuasive arguments effectively challenged the prevailing social norms and taboos.  Therefore, pair 2 is correctly matched.

Pairs 1 and 3 are incorrect.  E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker, though a prominent social reformer, is more closely associated with the Self-Respect Movement in South India, which primarily addressed caste issues and challenged Brahminical dominance, rather than specifically focusing on child marriage.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale, a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress, while a supporter of broader social reform, did not specifically champion the cause of untouchability to the same extent as other reformers like Mahatma Gandhi or B.R. Ambedkar.  These distractors highlight the need for precise knowledge of individual contributions within the broader context of 19th-century social reform. The question requires a nuanced understanding of the specific social issues championed by each individual.


**4. With reference to social reform movements in India, consider the following pairs:**

   Reform Movement          Key Ideology/Goal
1. Aligarh Movement          :   Reconciliation of Islamic teachings with modern science
2. Prarthana Samaj          :   Monotheistic reform within Hinduism
3. Ramakrishna Mission     :   Universalism and social service

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2 and 3

**Explanation:**

The Aligarh Movement, spearheaded by Sir Syed Ahmed Khan, aimed to modernize Muslim society by reconciling Islamic teachings with the advancements in modern science and education.  It emphasized the importance of Western education for Muslims, while simultaneously promoting a progressive interpretation of Islamic tenets. Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched.

The Prarthana Samaj, a reformist movement in Maharashtra, sought to reform Hinduism by emphasizing monotheism and rejecting idolatry and ritualistic excesses. It drew inspiration from the Brahmo Samaj and promoted social reform alongside religious reform.  Therefore, pair 2 is correctly matched.

The Ramakrishna Mission, founded by Swami Vivekananda, propagated the philosophy of his guru, Ramakrishna Paramahamsa.  It emphasized the universal nature of religion, asserting the essential unity of all faiths.  The Mission also placed strong emphasis on social service and humanitarian work as a path to spiritual growth.  Therefore, pair 3 is correctly matched.  This question tests the candidate's understanding of the diverse ideologies and goals of various reform movements, demanding more than superficial knowledge. The inclusion of all correctly matched pairs makes simple guessing less effective.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reformer          Region of Primary Activity
1. Savitribai Phule         :   Bengal
2. Raja Ram Mohan Roy      :   Maharashtra
3. Swami Dayananda Saraswati :   Punjab

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b) 3 only

**Explanation:**

Swami Dayananda Saraswati, the founder of the Arya Samaj, primarily worked in the Punjab region. His teachings and the Arya Samaj's activities had a profound impact on the social and religious landscape of Punjab.  Therefore, pair 3 is correctly matched.

Pairs 1 and 2 are incorrect. Savitribai Phule, along with her husband Jyotirao Phule, carried out their social reform work primarily in Maharashtra. Raja Ram Mohan Roy's reformist activities were mainly concentrated in Bengal, where he founded the Brahmo Samaj.  This question tests the candidate's ability to accurately associate social reformers with their primary regions of influence. The distractors are designed to test precise geographical knowledge, a common feature in UPSC questions on Indian history.  Incorrect options are plausible enough to test deeper factual recall.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and require in-depth knowledge of Indian history and social movements.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Location                      Prominent Event/Person Associated
1.  Meerut                        :    Beginning of the 1857 Revolt
2.  Jagdishpur                   :    Kunwar Singh's Zamindari
3.  Delhi                          :    Bahadur Shah Zafar's Leadership during 1857 Revolt
4.  Pochampalli                 :    Production of Silk and Cotton Sarees
5.  Andhra Pradesh                :    Location of Pochampalli

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. The 1857 Revolt famously began in Meerut.  Kunwar Singh, a significant leader of the 1857 Revolt, was the Zamindar of Jagdishpur. Bahadur Shah Zafar, the Mughal Emperor, played a crucial, albeit controversial, role as a symbolic leader of the rebellion in Delhi. Pochampalli is renowned for its silk and cotton saree production.  Finally, Pochampalli is located in Andhra Pradesh.  The options attempt to create plausible distractors by separating geographically related pairs (4 and 5) and chronologically significant events (1, 2, 3) to test the candidate's comprehensive understanding.


**2. With reference to the Revolt of 1857, consider the following pairs:**

   Person                         Role/Location
1.  Nana Saheb                    :   Led the revolt in Lucknow
2.  Rani Lakshmibai                :   Ruler of Jhansi
3.  Tantia Tope                    :   Key military strategist for Nana Saheb
4.  Bahadur Shah Zafar             :   Nominal leader in Delhi
5.  General Bakht Khan            :    Led the revolt in Kanpur


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1 and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (a) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Options 2, 3, and 4 are accurate. Rani Lakshmibai was indeed the ruler of Jhansi and a prominent leader of the revolt. Tantia Tope served as a crucial military commander under Nana Saheb. Bahadur Shah Zafar held the nominal leadership in Delhi, though the actual command rested with others. However, Nana Saheb led the revolt in Kanpur, not Lucknow, and General Bakht Khan's key role was in Delhi, not Kanpur. These inaccuracies in options 1 and 5 serve as effective distractors, testing the candidate's detailed knowledge of the revolt's leadership structure.



**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reform Movement           Prominent Figure
1.  Brahmo Samaj                   :   Dayananda Saraswati
2.  Arya Samaj                     :   Keshab Chandra Sen
3.  Self-Respect Movement           :   E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker
4.  Prarthana Samaj                :   M.G. Ranade


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c) 3 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched. E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker led the Self-Respect Movement. M.G. Ranade was associated with the Prarthana Samaj.  The other options are incorrect because Dayananda Saraswati founded the Arya Samaj, not the Brahmo Samaj (which was founded by Raja Ram Mohan Roy), and Keshab Chandra Sen was a prominent leader within the Brahmo Samaj, not the Arya Samaj.  This question tests the candidate's ability to differentiate between similar social reform movements and their key figures, demanding precise factual recall.


**4. With reference to early 20th-century Indian nationalism, consider the following pairs:**

   Person                          Political Affiliation/Role
1.  Jawaharlal Nehru              :   Leader of the Swaraj Party
2.  Lala Lajpat Rai                :   Prominent Moderate Nationalist
3.  M.K. Gandhi                    :   Promoter of Non-Cooperation Movement
4.  Subhas Chandra Bose           :   President of the Indian National Congress


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b) 3 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 3 and 4 are accurate. M.K. Gandhi is undeniably linked to the Non-Cooperation Movement. Subhas Chandra Bose served as President of the Indian National Congress.  The other pairs are incorrect. Jawaharlal Nehru was not a leader of the Swaraj Party (that was primarily C.R. Das and Motilal Nehru); he was a prominent figure in the Congress's left wing. Lala Lajpat Rai was an extremist nationalist, not a moderate.  The question aims to test nuanced understanding of political affiliations and roles within the Indian National Congress during a period of significant shifts in the nationalist movement.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Revolt/Movement              Primary Location

(b) 1 and 5 only
(c) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a) 2, 3, and 4 only

Options 2, 3, and 4 accurately reflect the primary locations of these movements. The Santhal Rebellion primarily affected parts of Bengal and Bihar.  The Eka Movement was centered in the United Provinces. The Moplah Rebellion took place in Kerala. However, the Indigo Revolt was primarily in Bengal, not Bihar, and the Pabna Revolt occurred in Bengal, not Punjab.  This question tests the candidate's knowledge of the geographical spread of various peasant uprisings and regional movements, requiring precise location recall.  The inclusion of plausible but incorrect locations acts as a strong distractor.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                        Association/Organization
