(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 3 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is correct because Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar served as the secretary of the Bethune School, and B.R. Ambedkar was affiliated with and headed the Scheduled Castes Federation.  Option (1) is incorrect because while M.G. Ranade was influential in the Poona Sarvajanik Sabha, he did not found it; Gopal Krishna Gokhale was not directly associated with the Poona Sarvajanik Sabha in a founding capacity although he was a prominent figure in Maharashtra. Option (2) is incorrect because, while M.G. Ranade helped found the Servants of India Society, it was primarily founded by Gopal Krishna Gokhale. The other options incorrectly include pairs 1 and 2, demonstrating a misunderstanding of the roles and affiliations of these prominent figures in the Indian social and political landscape.    Organization                 Primary Focus/Activity

**Explanation:**

The Prarthana Samaj primarily focused on religious and social reform within the context of Western India. Option (2) is incorrect; while the Arya Samaj did address social issues, its primary aim was religious reform, emphasizing a return to Vedic principles. Option (4) is incorrect; the Ramakrishna Mission's core focus was religious and spiritual reform based on Vedanta philosophy; it didn't primarily concentrate on promoting Vedic studies although it certainly valued them.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the specific goals and activities of various reformist organizations during a period of significant social and religious change in India. Option (2) is incorrect; Phule was a strong advocate for widow remarriage, actively working to challenge societal norms. Option (4) is incorrect; Gandhi vehemently opposed untouchability, dedicating a significant portion of his life to its eradication. Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar,  the 1857 Revolt,  and related figures and events.  Each question adheres to the specified format and criteria.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Association
1. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar :  Darul Uloom
2. Raja Ram Mohan Roy         :  Brahmo Samaj

4. Annie Besant                :  Theosophical Society

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2, 3 and 4 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b) 2, 3 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Raja Ram Mohan Roy is closely associated with the founding and propagation of the Brahmo Samaj, a significant socio-religious reform movement in 19th-century Bengal. Dayanand Saraswati is the founder of the Arya Samaj, another influential reform movement known for its emphasis on Vedic principles and social reform. Annie Besant was a prominent leader of the Theosophical Society, advocating for education and social reform in India.  Option (1) is incorrect because Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar's primary affiliations were with educational institutions like the Sanskrit College and the Bethune School, and not with Darul Uloom, which was a prominent Islamic seminary founded much later. **2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Social Reformer           Key Reform Advocated

3. M.G. Ranade                 :  Promotion of Western Education

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2 and 3

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched.  While Raja Ram Mohan Roy is primarily remembered for his campaign against Sati, Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar played a crucial role in advocating for and achieving the legalisation of widow remarriage.  M.G. Ranade, a prominent social reformer and jurist, strongly advocated for the introduction and spread of Western education in India as a means to social and intellectual progress. The options are designed to test the candidate's knowledge of the specific reforms associated with each social reformer,  avoiding easy generalizations. The inclusion of all correct matches differentiates it from other questions.



**3. With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following pairs:**

(c) 2 only
(d) 2 and 4 only

Bahadur Shah Zafar was the nominal leader of the revolt centered in Delhi, not Lucknow. Maulvi Liyaqat Ali was a significant leader in Allahabad.  The other options present plausible but incorrect pairings, testing the candidate's specific knowledge of the revolt's geography and leadership.   Reform Movement          Primary Focus

**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Known For

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader of 1857 Revolt        Region of Prominent Activity
1.  Nana Saheb                   :  Bihar
2.  Kunwar Singh                 :  Kanpur
3.  Begum Hazrat Mahal          :  Lucknow
4.  Rani Lakshmibai              :  Delhi
5.  Bahadur Shah Zafar           :  Jhansi

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 2, 3 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (c) 2 and 3 only.  Begum Hazrat Mahal played a significant role in the 1857 Revolt in Lucknow, leading the rebellion in Awadh.  Kunwar Singh, the zamindar of Jagdishpur, was a key figure in the revolt in Bihar, demonstrating significant military leadership and strategic prowess.  The other pairings are incorrect. Nana Saheb's primary area of activity was Kanpur, not Bihar. Rani Lakshmibai's leadership was crucial in Jhansi, not Delhi. While Bahadur Shah Zafar was the symbolic head of the revolt, his influence was primarily centered in Delhi, not Jhansi.  The question tests factual recall of key leaders and their geographical locations of influence during the 1857 Revolt. The distractors effectively challenge the candidate's knowledge by presenting plausible but ultimately incorrect associations.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Cause of 1857 Revolt           Specific Example
1.  Economic Exploitation        :  Introduction of the Enfield rifle
2.  Religious Grievances         :  Heavy taxation on peasants
3.  Political Resentment        :  Annexation of Awadh
4.  Administrative Corruption   :  Greased cartridges controversy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) is correct because the annexation of Awadh was a significant political grievance that fuelled the 1857 Revolt.  The annexation violated treaties and fuelled resentment among the sepoys, many of whom hailed from Awadh.  The other options incorrectly link causes with examples.  The introduction of the Enfield rifle and the greased cartridges controversy were primarily related to religious grievances, not economic exploitation. Heavy taxation was indeed an aspect of economic exploitation, but it doesn't directly relate to the specific example given. Administrative corruption was a broader issue; the greased cartridges controversy, while having administrative aspects, was primarily a religious issue. The question tests the candidate's ability to analyze the multifaceted causes of the 1857 Revolt and accurately connect them to specific historical events.  The distractors aim to test the candidate's depth of understanding by using plausible examples that are related to other causes of the revolt.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Outcome of 1857 Revolt        Specific Consequence
1.  Abolition of the East India Company :  Transfer of power to the Crown
2.  Reorganization of the Army      :  Increased number of Indian sepoys
3.  Queen's Proclamation           :  Introduction of the Doctrine of Lapse
4.  Policy of Divide and Rule        :  Increased racial tensions


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (a) 1 and 4 only. The 1857 Revolt directly led to the abolition of the East India Company's rule and the transfer of power to the British Crown. This was a significant political restructuring. The policy of divide and rule, while not explicitly stated in any single document, became a more pronounced feature of British policy after the revolt to prevent future uprisings by playing different groups against each other. This exacerbated racial tensions. The other options incorrectly pair outcomes with consequences. The reorganization of the army involved a significant reduction in the number of Indian sepoys, not an increase. The Doctrine of Lapse was a pre-existing policy, not a direct consequence of the revolt, although the revolt may have hastened its eventual abandonment.  The Queen's Proclamation was a response to the revolt aiming to pacify the Indian population; it did not introduce the Doctrine of Lapse. The question tests the candidate's understanding of the long-term consequences of the 1857 Revolt and its impact on British administrative policies. The distractors present plausible but incorrect connections to test the candidate's nuanced understanding of historical causality.

Tilka Manjhi's resistance was primarily in the Santhal Parganas, not Awadh. Wazir Ali Khan's rebellion was centered in Awadh, not the Santhal Parganas. Dhundia Wagh's activities were in Bednur (present-day Karnataka), not Bundelkhand.    Historian/Perspective           Interpretation

(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) 3 only. S.N. Sen's interpretation of the 1857 Revolt aligns with the statement provided. He argued that while the revolt began with religious grievances as a catalyst, its trajectory evolved into a broader struggle for independence.  The other options incorrectly attribute interpretations to historians. R.C. Majumdar famously argued against the characterization of the revolt as a "First War of Independence," emphasizing its localized nature and lack of widespread national participation. V.D. Savarkar, conversely, championed the narrative of the 1857 Revolt as the "First War of Independence." **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                     Role in the Bardoli Satyagraha
1. Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel                 :   Key organizer and leader
2. Mahatma Gandhi                           :   Provided crucial support and guidance
3. K.M. Munshi                              :   Offered legal and administrative expertise
4. Lalji Naranji                             :   Played a significant financial role


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Bardoli Satyagraha, a significant peasant movement led by Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, stands as a testament to the power of non-violent resistance in the Indian freedom struggle.  Sardar Patel's leadership was instrumental in organizing and mobilizing the Bardoli peasants, successfully challenging the unjust land revenue hike imposed by the British government.  Mahatma Gandhi's support and guidance were crucial in providing the movement with ideological backing and national prominence, making it a landmark event in the struggle for independence. K.M. Munshi, a prominent lawyer and administrator, played a vital role in providing legal and administrative expertise, ensuring the movement was conducted within a well-defined framework.  Lalji Naranji's financial contribution was essential, as he provided the movement with much-needed financial resources, enabling its effective operations.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched, reflecting the collective effort and leadership that made the Bardoli Satyagraha a success.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude crucial figures who significantly contributed to the movement's success.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Event                                      Key Tactic Employed
1. Bardoli Satyagraha                        :   Civil Disobedience
2. Non-Cooperation Movement                 :   Boycott of British Goods
3. Salt Satyagraha                           :   Salt Production
4. Quit India Movement                       :   Individual Satyagraha


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Bardoli Satyagraha primarily utilized civil disobedience as its core tactic. The peasants, under Sardar Patel's leadership, collectively refused to pay the increased land revenue, a direct act of defiance against the British authority. The Non-Cooperation Movement involved a widespread boycott of British goods, schools, and courts. The Salt Satyagraha saw Indians defying the British salt monopoly by producing their own salt, a symbolic act of challenging colonial rule.  However, the Quit India Movement's main tactic was mass civil disobedience, not Individual Satyagraha, which was a later, more focused approach. Therefore, only the first three pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incomplete as they fail to encompass the full range of tactics effectively used in these major movements.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

The Permanent Settlement, while initially intended to streamline revenue collection, led to widespread exploitation and impoverishment of the peasantry, fueling discontent.  The introduction of Enfield rifles, rumored to be greased with animal fat, significantly aggravated religious sentiments among sepoys, sparking the initial mutiny.  The annexation of Awadh is more accurately classified as a political grievance, leading to widespread resentment among the populace and sepoys from that region.  Over-assessment of land revenue was a consequence of various revenue systems, contributing to economic hardship but not a unique cause in itself. While administrative corruption certainly played a role, the examples given for options 3 and 4 are not the most accurate representation of their direct causal link to the revolt. Therefore, only options 1 and 2 directly and accurately reflect causes and specific examples related to the 1857 Revolt.

(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The question tests factual recall and the ability to identify accurate pairings amidst plausible distractors.

   Reform Movement             Founder/Key Leader

(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only

The Aligarh Movement was spearheaded by Sir Syed Ahmed Khan, not Dadabhai Naoroji.  Naoroji was a prominent figure in the Indian National Congress and a leader of the early nationalist movement.  The Prarthana Samaj, while influenced by Keshab Chandra Sen, was primarily founded by Atmaram Pandurang and later significantly shaped by Mahadev Govind Ranade.  Jyotirao Phule indeed founded the Satyashodhak Samaj, a movement for social reform among the lower castes in Maharashtra.  Finally, Shiv Narayan Agnihotri correctly founded the Dev Samaj, a religious and social reform movement that emphasized the eternity of the soul and good action. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they include incorrectly matched pairs.  The question tests factual recall of key figures associated with significant social and religious reform movements in 19th and early 20th century India.  Understanding the distinct ideologies and goals of these movements is crucial for a comprehensive understanding of the socio-political landscape of the period.

**4. With reference to the Sepoy Mutiny of 1857, consider the following pairs:**

   Cause of Rebellion           Description
1.  Religious Concerns        :   Introduction of Enfield rifles with greased cartridges
2.  Economic Grievances      :   Discrimination in payment and promotions
3.  Administrative Issues      :   Inefficiency of British officers

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched. The Sepoy Mutiny was sparked by a multitude of factors, including religious concerns related to the perceived sacrilege of the greased cartridges, economic grievances stemming from discriminatory practices in the army's payment and promotion systems, and administrative issues related to the perceived inefficiency and mistreatment by British officers.  The options (a), (b), and (c)  act as distractors by offering incomplete sets of causes, testing the candidate's comprehensive understanding of the multifaceted nature of the Sepoy Mutiny's origins. The question assesses factual recall, analytical skills, and the ability to synthesize information from multiple sources to arrive at a complete and accurate understanding of a historical event.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader of the Revolt of 1857        Location of Major Activity
1.  Nana Sahib                       :   Delhi
2.  Begum Hazrat Mahal               :   Kanpur
3.  Rani Lakshmibai                   :   Lucknow
4.  Kunwar Singh                     :   Jhansi

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) is correct because Begum Hazrat Mahal led the revolt in Lucknow, and Kunwar Singh was a key leader in Bihar, particularly around Arrah and Jagdishpur.  Nana Sahib's main area of operation during the 1857 revolt was Kanpur, not Delhi.  Rani Lakshmibai's significant actions were centered in Jhansi, although her influence extended beyond that region. The question deliberately uses plausible distractors by placing Delhi (the main center of the revolt) with Nana Sahib and Jhansi (Rani Lakshmibai's main base) with Kunwar Singh. This tests the candidate's precise knowledge of the geographical scope of each leader's involvement. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect due to the mismatched pairings of leaders and their primary locations of activity during the 1857 revolt.


**2. With reference to the Indian Rebellion of 1857, consider the following pairs:**

   Individual/Group                     Role/Association
1.  Mangal Pandey                     :   Initial spark at Meerut
2.  General Bakht Khan                :   Military leader in Delhi
3.  Maulavi Ahmadullah                :   Preached rebellion in Madras
4.  Bahadur Shah Zafar                :   Symbolic leader, lacked decisive action


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) is the correct answer. General Bakht Khan played a significant military role in Delhi during the revolt. Maulavi Ahmadullah indeed began preaching rebellion in Madras before moving north. Bahadur Shah Zafar, while the symbolic head, is accurately described as a leader lacking decisive action.  The distractor in option (b) is the inclusion of Mangal Pandey, whose actions at Barrackpore were significant but did not directly initiate the revolt at Meerut.  The question tests the candidate's understanding of the nuanced roles played by different figures in the rebellion. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they misrepresent the roles of at least one of the individuals mentioned.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Post-1857 Reform/Policy           Implementing Body/Individual
1.  Army Reorganization              :   Peel Commission
2.  Vernacular Education Promotion  :   Hunter Commission
3.  Constitutional Reforms (1909)     :   Morley-Minto Reforms


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Option (b) is correct because the Hunter Commission focused on education reform, including the promotion of vernacular languages. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909 were a significant set of constitutional changes. The distractor is the Peel Commission, which is commonly associated with police reform in the UK, not army reorganization in India after 1857.  The actual commission responsible for army reorganization after 1857 is not explicitly mentioned in the source, making this a challenging question requiring precise knowledge and the ability to eliminate incorrect options. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect due to the mismatched pairs.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Note that due to the nature of the provided text (a collection of excerpts), some questions might focus on specific events or figures mentioned prominently within the excerpts rather than comprehensively covering the entire Indian nationalist movement.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader                                      Associated Movement/Organization
1.  Dadabhai Naoroji                           :   Indian National Congress, Surat Split
2.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale                    :   Indian National Congress, Lucknow Pact
3.  C.R. Das                                   :   Swarajist Party, Nagpur Session
4.  Motilal Nehru                             :   Swarajist Party, Non-Cooperation Movement
5.  Jawaharlal Nehru                          :   All India Youth Congress, Socialist Ideology

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. Dadabhai Naoroji was a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress and his presidency during the Surat Split is well documented.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale played a crucial role in the Lucknow Pact, which fostered Hindu-Muslim unity within the Congress. C.R. Das was a key figure in the Swarajist Party and actively participated in the Nagpur Session of the Congress. Motilal Nehru was instrumental in forming the Swarajist Party and participated in the Non-Cooperation Movement. Jawaharlal Nehru's leadership in the All India Youth Congress and his advocacy of socialist ideology are also well-known facts.  The options attempt to create plausible distractors by suggesting that some of these individuals were not associated with certain movements or organizations, but this is factually incorrect.

**5. With reference to the Indian National Congress, consider the following pairs:**

   Congress Session                        Significant Decision/Event

5.  Ahmedabad Session (1921)              :   Gandhi appointed sole authority on civil disobedience.

(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched. The Lucknow Session is famous for the Lucknow Pact.  The Nagpur Session formally adopted the Non-Cooperation program. The Surat Session witnessed the major split within the Congress. The Ahmedabad Session granted Gandhi sole authority. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reform Movement             Prominent Leader

(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Prarthana Samaj was indeed founded in 1867 by Atmaram Pandurang, with Mahadev Govind Ranade playing a crucial role in its growth and popularity.  The Arya Samaj was founded by Swami Dayananda Saraswati in 1875, aiming for a reformist and revivalist approach within Hinduism.  While Keshab Chandra Sen was a prominent leader of the Brahmo Samaj,  he was not the founder; that credit belongs to Raja Ram Mohan Roy.  Gopal Ganesh Agarkar was a significant social reformer in Maharashtra, but his primary association wasn't with the Satyashodhak Samaj; that movement was spearheaded by Jyotirao Phule.  Option (d) correctly identifies the accurate pairings for the Arya Samaj and Prarthana Samaj, and while Keshab Chandra Sen's leadership within the Brahmo Samaj is undeniable,  the question focuses on the founder which is a more precise match.  Options (a), (b), and (c) contain at least one incorrect pairing, making them unsuitable. The question tests factual recall and analytical skills by requiring precise knowledge of the leaders associated with each social reform movement.

Gopal Baba Walangkar, a Dalit leader, founded the Anarya Dosh-Parihar Mandali to address the issues faced by the non-Aryan communities.  However, Savitribai Phule's main contributions were focused on women's education and the upliftment of lower castes in Maharashtra; she was not associated with the Vaikom Satyagraha, which took place in Kerala.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy was a key figure in the Brahmo Samaj and its related reform activities but had no direct involvement with the Paramahansa Mandali. **4. With reference to 19th-century Indian social reform movements, consider the following pairs:**

   Movement                             Primary Focus
1.  Singh Sabha Movement               :   Gurudwara Reform
2.  Rahnumai Mazdayasnan Sabha       :   Widow Remarriage
3.  Dev Samaj                           :   Caste Abolition
4.  Aligarh Movement                   :   Monotheism


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Singh Sabha Movement primarily focused on promoting modern education among Sikhs and countering missionary activities, while also reinforcing Sikh religious traditions.  The Rahnumai Mazdayasnan Sabha aimed at reforming Zoroastrian religious practices and the social conditions of Parsis. The Dev Samaj, founded by Shiv Narayan Agnihotri, emphasized social reforms like opposing child marriage and promoting ethical conduct,  but its primary focus wasn't caste abolition, although it did address social inequalities. The Aligarh Movement, led by Sir Syed Ahmad Khan, concentrated on modernizing Muslim education and social reforms, not on promoting monotheism as a core tenet; its emphasis was on reconciling Islamic teachings with modern education and thought.  Option (c) accurately reflects the primary focus of the Singh Sabha Movement and the Rahnumai Mazdayasnan Sabha. The other options present incorrect primary focuses for at least one movement, demonstrating the need for careful consideration of the historical context of each movement. This question tests factual recall and analytical skills, demanding specific knowledge of the central goals of each movement.

Each pair accurately reflects a significant contribution or association. Ram Mohan Roy's *Precepts of Jesus* is a well-known work showcasing his theological and social reformist ideas. Bethune is directly linked to the founding of the Bethune School, a landmark in women's education. Rabindranath Tagore's renunciation of his knighthood in protest against the Jallianwala Bagh massacre is a highly significant event. Mahatma Gandhi's Dandi March is a defining moment of the Indian independence movement.  These individuals and their actions are central to understanding the socio-religious and political transformations in India during the colonial period and the struggle for independence.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they omit at least one correctly matched pair, demonstrating incomplete knowledge of the historical figures and their impact.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Institution     Location
1.  English East India Company  :  Bengal
2.  Bethune School            :  Calcutta
3.  Jamia Millia Islamia       :  Delhi
4.  Kashi Vidyapith            :  Benares (Varanasi)
5.  Bihar Vidyapith            :  Patna


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(c) 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. The English East India Company had extensive operations and influence in Bengal. The Bethune School was located in Calcutta. The Jamia Millia Islamia, a prominent Muslim educational institution, eventually moved its headquarters to Delhi. The Kashi Vidyapith, a national university, was established in Benares (Varanasi). The Bihar Vidyapith, another national university, was founded in Patna.  Understanding the geographic locations of these organizations and institutions is important for comprehending the dynamics of education, politics, and socio-cultural movements during the British colonial era and the Indian independence struggle. The other options are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair, showing an incomplete understanding of the geographical context of these pivotal institutions.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Movement/Event              Key Figure/Leader
1.  Non-Cooperation Movement   :  Mahatma Gandhi
2.  Khilafat Movement           :  Ali Brothers
3.  Salt Satyagraha             :  Mahatma Gandhi
4.  Quit India Movement         :  Mahatma Gandhi
5.  Civil Disobedience Movement:  Mahatma Gandhi


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(c) 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All five pairs accurately connect movements/events with their key leaders. Mahatma Gandhi was the central figure in the Non-Cooperation Movement, Salt Satyagraha, Quit India Movement, and the broader Civil Disobedience Movement. The Ali Brothers (Muhammad Ali and Shaukat Ali) were prominent leaders of the Khilafat Movement, which played a significant role in mobilizing Muslim support for the Indian independence struggle. These leaders' roles are well-documented and crucial to understanding the various stages of the Indian independence movement and the strategies employed to achieve freedom.  Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they fail to recognize the central role of Mahatma Gandhi and the Ali Brothers in these historically significant movements.  A thorough grasp of the Indian independence struggle necessitates understanding these key figures and their leadership.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Note that the difficulty level is inherently subjective, and the "difficult" designation reflects the need for precise factual recall and the inclusion of plausible but incorrect distractors.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Governor-General/Viceroy          Action Related to Awadh
1. Lord William Bentinck             :  Annexation of Awadh
2. Lord Dalhousie                    :  Deposed Nawab Wajid Ali Shah
3. Lord Hastings                      : Involved in the affairs of Awadh
4. Lord Amherst                       : Involved in the affairs of Awadh

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Dalhousie's actions directly led to the annexation of Awadh in 1856, including the deposition of Nawab Wajid Ali Shah.  Lord Hastings and Lord Amherst, while not directly responsible for the annexation, were involved in the political affairs of Awadh during their respective tenures as Governor-General, influencing the trajectory leading to its eventual annexation by Dalhousie. Lord William Bentinck, although a significant figure in the history of British India, is not directly linked to the annexation of Awadh.  Option (a) is incorrect because Bentinck did not annex Awadh. Option (b) is partially correct in including Dalhousie and Hastings but omits Amherst's involvement. Option (d) is incorrect because it wrongly includes Bentinck.  The question tests factual recall and the ability to differentiate between direct and indirect involvement in historical events.



**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Policy Implemented in British India      Governor-General/Viceroy
1. Subsidiary Alliance                    : Lord Curzon
2. Doctrine of Lapse                      : Lord Dalhousie
3. Permanent Settlement of Land Revenue : Lord Cornwallis
4.  Policy of Non-Intervention in Social Affairs : Lord William Bentinck


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Doctrine of Lapse was a key policy of Lord Dalhousie's administration, used to annex several Indian states. The Permanent Settlement of Land Revenue was implemented by Lord Cornwallis in Bengal.  Option (a) is incorrect as Lord Curzon is associated with other policies and reforms. Option (c) is incorrect as it falsely attributes the policy of non-intervention in social affairs to Lord William Bentinck - while Bentinck was a reformer, he didn't initiate a blanket policy of non-intervention. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the incorrectly matched pair involving Lord Curzon and the Subsidiary Alliance. This question tests the knowledge of key British administrative policies and their association with the respective Governor-Generals/Viceroys, demanding accurate factual recall.


**3. With reference to the annexation of Indian states by the British East India Company, consider the following pairs:**

   State Annexed                      Method of Annexation Primarily Used
1. Satara                              : Doctrine of Lapse
2. Jhansi                              :  Doctrine of Lapse
3. Awadh                              :  Accusation of Misgovernance
4. Punjab                              :  Military Conquest


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Satara and Jhansi were annexed using the Doctrine of Lapse, while Awadh's annexation was justified on grounds of misgovernance.  The annexation of Punjab was primarily achieved through military conquest. Option (a) is incomplete as it omits Awadh. Option (c) is incorrect as it incorrectly links Punjab's annexation to a method other than military conquest. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the inaccurate pairing of Punjab's annexation with a method other than military force. This question assesses the understanding of different methods employed by the British in annexing Indian states, demanding precise knowledge of specific cases and the ability to identify the primary method used in each instance.



**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                    Role/Association
1.  Nawab Wajid Ali Shah                  :  Ruler of Awadh before annexation
2.  Nana Saheb                             :  Adopted son of Baji Rao II
3.  Lord Canning                           :  Governor-General during the Sepoy Mutiny
4.  Azimullah Khan                         :  Advisor to Rani Lakshmibai


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Nawab Wajid Ali Shah was indeed the ruler of Awadh before its annexation by Lord Dalhousie. Nana Saheb was the adopted son of the last Peshwa, Baji Rao II. Lord Canning succeeded Lord Dalhousie and was Governor-General during the Sepoy Mutiny of 1857.  However, Azimullah Khan was an advisor to Nana Saheb, not Rani Lakshmibai. Options (a), (b), and (d) are therefore incorrect due to the inaccurate association of Azimullah Khan with Rani Lakshmibai. This question tests factual recall of key historical figures and their roles, requiring precise knowledge to identify the correct pairings and eliminate the distractor.



**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Policy/Act                          Primary Aim/Effect
1. Vernacular Press Act, 1878         : To promote vernacular literature
2. Indian Factory Act, 1881            : To regulate child labour in factories
3. Doctrine of Lapse                    : To expand British territory
4.  Subsidiary Alliance                 : To foster friendly relations with Indian states


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Indian Factory Act of 1881 aimed at regulating child labour, and the Doctrine of Lapse was a tool for territorial expansion. The Subsidiary Alliance, while superficially aiming for friendship, ultimately served British expansionist goals.  The Vernacular Press Act of 1878, however, aimed to curb the freedom of the Indian-language press, not promote it. Option (a) is incomplete, omitting the correct pairing of the Subsidiary Alliance. Option (b) is incorrect because it includes the mismatched pair involving the Vernacular Press Act. Option (d) is incorrect due to the inaccurate pairing of the Vernacular Press Act.  This question assesses knowledge of British policies and their true intentions, requiring a nuanced understanding of historical context beyond surface-level interpretations.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reformer       Significant Contribution
1. Savitribai Phule     :   Founded the Poona Sarvajanik Sabha
2. Gopal Hari Deshmukh :   Advocated for widow remarriage
3. Dadabhai Naoroji      :   Founded the East India Association in London
4. M.G. Ranade          :   Known as "Lokahitawadi"

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3 is correctly matched. Dadabhai Naoroji established the East India Association in London to advocate for Indian interests in British political circles.  The other pairings are incorrect. Savitribai Phule's significant contribution was pioneering women's education and fighting against untouchability, not founding the Poona Sarvajanik Sabha (that was founded by Justice Ranade and others). Gopal Hari Deshmukh, known as "Lokahitawadi," was a social reformer advocating for rational societal reorganization, not specifically for widow remarriage, although he likely supported the concept as part of broader reform.  M.G. Ranade was a prominent social reformer and jurist in Maharashtra, not known by the pen name "Lokahitawadi" (that title belonged to Gopal Hari Deshmukh).  The incorrect pairings highlight the importance of precise factual recall in understanding the contributions of these key figures in Indian history.  UPSC often tests the ability to differentiate between closely related facts, making this a challenging but crucial skill for aspirants.

Annie Besant, while a prominent figure in Indian nationalism, was never President of the Indian National Congress. The Servants of India Society was founded by Gopal Krishna Gokhale, not Bal Gangadhar Tilak.  The Home Rule Movement was primarily led by Annie Besant and Bal Gangadhar Tilak, not Gopal Krishna Gokhale, though Gokhale played a vital role in the earlier phases of Indian nationalism. This question tests the ability to accurately associate individuals with their primary roles and organizations in the Indian freedom struggle.  The distractors are carefully chosen to represent figures who were active in the period and involved in related movements, requiring precise knowledge to avoid incorrect matching.

**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Reform/Act                  Key Figure Involved
1. Abolition of Sati           :   Lord Curzon
2. Widow Remarriage Act       :   Lord Dalhousie

4.  Indian Councils Act of 1909:   Lord Minto

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 4 is correctly matched. The Indian Councils Act of 1909 (Morley-Minto Reforms) was implemented under Lord Minto's viceroyalty. The other pairings are incorrect. The abolition of Sati was primarily associated with Lord William Bentinck, not Lord Curzon. While Lord Dalhousie's annexations created a context for social reform, the Widow Remarriage Act was passed earlier, during the time of Lord Canning. The Permanent Settlement was implemented by Lord Cornwallis, not Lord Wellesley.  This question tests knowledge of significant administrative and legislative reforms in British India and their association with specific viceroys and governors-general.  The distractors are designed to test the precise knowledge of individuals associated with various landmark reforms.

The Satya Shodhak Samaj was founded by Jyotirao Phule, not Gopal Krishna Gokhale.  While Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was associated with the Brahmo Samaj, he was not its founder; Raja Ram Mohan Roy is more closely associated with its founding. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                      Role/Association
1. Lord Curzon                  :   Implemented the Partition of Bengal
2. Lord Minto                   :   Granted separate electorates
3. Lord Wellesley                :   Established Fort William College
4. Rabindranath Tagore         :   Authored Vande Mataram

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Lord Curzon's tenure as Viceroy of India saw the controversial Partition of Bengal in 1905, aimed at weakening Bengali nationalism.  This is a well-established historical fact.  Lord Minto, as Viceroy, played a key role in the Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, which introduced separate electorates for Muslims, a significant development in Indian politics leading to the growth of communal politics. Lord Wellesley, during his governorship, established the Fort William College in Calcutta to improve the education of civil servants, thereby contributing to the British administrative apparatus in India.  These three pairs are accurate reflections of historical events and individual roles.

Option (d) is incorrect because while Rabindranath Tagore was a towering figure in Bengali literature and contributed significantly to the nationalist movement, he did *not* author "Vande Mataram."  Bankim Chandra Chatterjee wrote "Vande Mataram," which was later adopted as a nationalist song.  The inclusion of this incorrect pairing serves as a strong distractor, testing the candidate's precise knowledge of historical figures and their contributions.  Options (a) and (b) are also incorrect as they only partially reflect the correct pairings, making the question challenging and requiring thorough knowledge of the subject matter. The question tests factual recall and the ability to differentiate between accurate and inaccurate historical associations.



**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Nationalist Leader        Key Political Action/Ideology
1. Gopal Krishna Gokhale     :   Advocated for Swaraj
2. Bal Gangadhar Tilak      :   Promoted the Swadeshi movement
3. Mahatma Gandhi          :   Led the Non-Cooperation Movement
4. Aurobindo Ghosh           :   Championed passive resistance


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2, 3 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs accurately reflect the contributions and actions of these significant figures in the Indian nationalist movement. Gopal Krishna Gokhale, a prominent Moderate leader, advocated for self-government (Swaraj) through constitutional means. Bal Gangadhar Tilak, a key figure among the Extremists, played a crucial role in promoting the Swadeshi movement, emphasizing the boycott of British goods and the use of Indian-made products. Mahatma Gandhi's leadership of the Non-Cooperation Movement marked a turning point in the struggle for independence. Aurobindo Ghosh, a prominent intellectual and revolutionary, actively championed passive resistance as a form of political action.  The question tests factual recall of major nationalist leaders and their significant contributions to the Indian independence movement. All options except (d) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.

Savarkar's association with the Abhinava Bharat, a secret revolutionary society, is well-documented. Kasturi Ranga Iyengar was a key figure in establishing and developing The Hindu, a prominent newspaper. **5. With reference to early Indian nationalism (1885-1905), consider the following pairs:**

   Leader                  Political Ideology/Approach

(d) 1 and 3 only

This question tests the candidate's understanding of the different ideological strands within the early Indian nationalist movement.  Dadabhai Naoroji and Bal Gangadhar Tilak were prominent figures within the Extremist faction, advocating for more assertive and radical methods to achieve self-rule.  Surendranath Banerjea and Gopal Krishna Gokhale were leaders of the Moderate faction, who favored constitutional methods and gradual reforms within the existing political framework.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they misclassify at least one leader's political ideology. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Association/Activity
1.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak       :  President, Indian National Congress
2.  Jawaharlal Nehru          :  Editor, *The Hindustan Times*

4.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale    :  Founder, Servants of India Society

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)


**Explanation:**

Option (c) is correct because Sarojini Naidu served as the Governor of the United Provinces (now Uttar Pradesh) and Gopal Krishna Gokhale founded the Servants of India Society.  Let's analyze the other options:

* **Option (a):**  Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress and associated with its extremist wing, but he never served as its President.  While he held significant influence, he was never formally elected to the top position.

* **Option (b):** Jawaharlal Nehru was a prominent figure in Indian politics, but he was not the editor of *The Hindustan Times*.  He was deeply involved in journalism and writing, but his association with this specific newspaper is not accurately reflected in this pair.  Sarojini Naidu did indeed become the Governor of Uttar Pradesh, making this part of the pair correct.

* **Option (d):** Dadabhai Naoroji was a significant figure in the early Indian National Congress, playing a crucial role, but he was not its General Secretary.  While he held important positions and contributed immensely, the General Secretary role is inaccurate in this context.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale's association with the Servants of India Society is accurate.

The question tests factual recall of prominent figures in the Indian National Movement and their roles, requiring the candidate to differentiate between influence and formal positions held. The distractors are designed to be plausible, making the question challenging and requiring precise knowledge.

**5. With reference to the Government of India Act, 1935, consider the following pairs:**

   Feature                                  Description
1.  Provincial Autonomy                    :  Replaced Dyarchy
2.  Federal Level Executive                 :  Governor-General as the pivot
3.  Communal Electorates                  :  Based on the Communal Award
4.  All India Federation                    :  Never formed due to unfulfilled conditions
5.  Separate Electorates for Depressed Classes: Initially part of the Communal Award, later modified by the Poona Pact

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act, 1935, introduced provincial autonomy, replacing the earlier dyarchy system, making pair 1 correct. The Governor-General was central to the federal executive structure, making pair 2 correct. The Act incorporated communal electorates as outlined in the Communal Award, making pair 3 correct. The proposed All-India Federation never materialized due to non-fulfillment of preconditions regarding the accession of princely states, making pair 4 correct.  The Act initially included separate electorates for depressed classes, later amended by the Poona Pact, making pair 5 correct. This question demands a detailed understanding of the key features and provisions of the Government of India Act, 1935, and its subsequent modifications.  The options are designed to test the candidate's nuanced understanding of the Act's complexities and its relationship with other significant events like the Communal Award and the Poona Pact. The inclusion of all correct pairs makes this a difficult question that rewards a thorough understanding of the topic.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Figure          Significant Association
1. Lord Curzon               :   Implementation of the Partition of Bengal
2. Lord Irwin                 :   Signing of the Gandhi-Irwin Pact
3. Ramsay MacDonald         :   Chairing of the Second Round Table Conference
4. Lord Willingdon            :   Governor-General during the Second Phase of Civil Disobedience

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched. Lord Curzon is directly associated with the implementation of the Partition of Bengal in 1905, a pivotal event in the Indian freedom struggle.  The Gandhi-Irwin Pact, a significant agreement between Mahatma Gandhi and Lord Irwin, the Viceroy of India, led to a temporary suspension of the Civil Disobedience Movement.  Ramsay MacDonald, the British Prime Minister at the time, chaired the Second Round Table Conference, a crucial attempt to address India's constitutional future.  Finally, Lord Willingdon served as the Governor-General of India during the second, more repressive phase of the Civil Disobedience Movement, following the breakdown of negotiations after the Second Round Table Conference.  The other options are incorrect because they exclude one or more of these historically accurate pairings.  Understanding the roles of these individuals in shaping the course of the Indian National Movement is crucial for a comprehensive understanding of this period.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legislation/Act             Key Provision/Impact
1. Indian Councils Act of 1892 :   Introduced a system of direct elections to legislative councils
2. Government of India Act 1935:   Established provincial autonomy
3. Communal Award of 1932    :   Granted separate electorates for depressed classes
4. Indian Independence Act 1947:   Established the Dominion of India and Pakistan

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

While the Indian Councils Act of 1892 did expand the legislative councils and allow for some indirect elections, it did not introduce a system of direct elections. The act primarily increased the number of members and permitted some discussion of the budget but maintained the British majority in the councils. The other three pairs are correctly matched. The Government of India Act of 1935 is famous for introducing a system of provincial autonomy. The Communal Award, announced by Ramsay MacDonald, famously introduced separate electorates for various religious and caste groups, including the depressed classes (Dalits). The Indian Independence Act of 1947 formalized the partition of India and the creation of independent India and Pakistan. Thus, option (c) is the only correct answer. The other options incorrectly include the inaccurate pairing concerning the 1892 Act.

(b) 1 and 2 only

(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

   Political Organization                     Significant Policy/Demand

3.  Home Rule League                         :   Self-Government (Home Rule)
4.  Revolutionary Terrorist Groups          :   Assassination of British Officials
5.  All India Kisan Sabha                     :   Peasant Rights


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

This question tests the understanding of the goals and actions of various political entities during the early 20th-century Indian freedom struggle.  The Indian National Congress, particularly in its later phases, advocated for complete independence (Purna Swaraj). The Muslim League famously championed the demand for separate electorates. The Home Rule League's primary objective was to secure self-government for India. Revolutionary terrorist groups employed assassination as a tactic against British officials. The All India Kisan Sabha actively worked for the betterment of peasants' rights.  All five pairs accurately reflect the main objectives and actions of these organizations. The other options are incorrect as they wrongly omit one or more of these historically accurate connections.  A correct answer demonstrates a sound grasp of the diverse political spectrum of the era.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Association/Movement
1.  Lord Curzon                 Partition of Bengal
2.  Annie Besant                Home Rule League
3.  Mahatma Gandhi            Non-Cooperation Movement
4.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak        Home Rule Movement
5.  Subhas Chandra Bose       Forward Bloc

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) All of the above


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. Lord Curzon is directly associated with the controversial Partition of Bengal in 1905, a significant event in the Indian nationalist movement.  Annie Besant played a crucial role in the Home Rule Movement, alongside Bal Gangadhar Tilak, advocating for self-governance. Mahatma Gandhi’s leadership of the Non-Cooperation Movement, a major phase of civil disobedience, is well-established.  Finally, Subhas Chandra Bose's founding of the Forward Bloc, a separate political faction within the Indian National Congress, represents a key divergence in nationalist strategies.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair, demonstrating a lack of complete understanding of the historical figures and their respective roles within the Indian independence movement.  A comprehensive understanding of the Indian National Congress and the broader nationalist movement is essential for correctly identifying these linkages.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization               Event/Policy

(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) because only the pairs involving the Muslim League and the Lahore Resolution, the Home Rule League and Tilak's leadership, and the Forward Bloc and Subhas Chandra Bose are accurately matched. While the Congress Socialist Party emerged from within the Congress, it eventually became an independent political party; therefore, pairing it with the status of an "independent political party" is not entirely accurate. Option (d) is incorrect because it wrongly includes the Congress Socialist Party-independent party pairing.  Understanding the distinct political ideologies and actions of various organizations during the Indian independence struggle is crucial for accurate matching.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

**Explanation:**

Only options 2, 3, and 5 are correctly matched. Subhas Chandra Bose authored *The Indian Struggle*, a significant autobiographical account of his political career and involvement in the Indian independence movement. Mahatma Gandhi used *Young India* as a platform to disseminate his political ideology and strategies.  Surendranath Banerjea was associated with *Amrita Bazar Patrika*, a prominent newspaper that played a role in shaping public opinion.  *Hind Swaraj* was written by Mahatma Gandhi, not Gokhale. **4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation             Key Characteristic/Impact
1.  Ilbert Bill                  Increased judicial powers for Indians
2.  Rowlatt Act                 Enhanced government's repressive powers
3.  Government of India Act 1935  Introduced provincial autonomy
4.  Indian Independence Act 1947 Granted dominion status to India
5.  Indian Councils Act 1892     Limited expansion of legislative councils


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) because the Rowlatt Act significantly strengthened the government's power to suppress dissent, the Government of India Act 1935 introduced a significant degree of provincial autonomy, and the Indian Councils Act 1892 involved a limited expansion of legislative councils. The Ilbert Bill aimed to give Indian judges the ability to try European offenders, not increased judicial powers for Indians in general. The Indian Independence Act 1947 granted complete independence, not dominion status.  Option (a) is wrong due to the inaccurate pairing of the Ilbert Bill. Option (c) is incorrect as it omits the correct pairing of the Indian Councils Act 1892. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the inaccurate pairing of the Indian Independence Act 1947.  A deep understanding of the various legislative acts passed during British rule in India is crucial for accurate matching.

(a) 2, 3, and 5 only
(b) 3 and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only options 2, 3, and 5 are correctly matched. Lala Lajpat Rai, while initially a moderate, later became involved in the Home Rule Movement advocating for self-governance. Motilal Nehru was a key figure in the Swaraj Party, a significant faction within the Congress that pursued a strategy of "council entry" to influence policy. Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel played a crucial role in the integration of the princely states into the Indian Union.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale was a prominent leader of the moderate faction of the Congress, not the extremist faction.  Jawaharlal Nehru presided over the Lahore Congress session in 1929 (not 1939). (b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 3 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

While Lala Lajpat Rai was a prominent figure in the Indian nationalist movement and associated with various organizations, he wasn't a founder of the Indian Home Rule League; that distinction primarily belongs to Annie Besant and Bal Gangadhar Tilak.  Jawaharlal Nehru was a significant leader in the Indian National Congress but never held the position of President of the All India Trade Union Congress (AITUC); Lala Lajpat Rai was the first president of AITUC.  Finally, Bal Gangadhar Tilak was not a founder of the All India Anti-Untouchability League; that organization is primarily associated with Mahatma Gandhi.  These incorrect pairings serve as effective distractors, testing the candidate's precise knowledge of individual leaders and their specific organizational affiliations within the complex landscape of the Indian National Movement. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader                      Associated Movement/Event

3.  Lala Lajpat Rai             :   Simon Go Back Campaign
4.  N.M. Joshi                  :   All India Trade Union Congress (AITUC) split

(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a prominent leader of the Home Rule Movement, alongside Annie Besant.  Mahatma Gandhi spearheaded the Non-Cooperation Movement, a significant phase of the Indian independence struggle. Lala Lajpat Rai played a crucial role in the Anti-Simon Commission movement, famously coining or popularizing the slogan "Simon Go Back."  N.M. Joshi was a key figure in the All India Trade Union Congress (AITUC), and his ideological differences led to a significant split within the organization.  Finally, Joseph Baptista was a founder of the All India Home Rule League, showcasing his dedication to Indian self-governance. Options (a), (b), and (d) incorrectly exclude one or more of these historically accurate pairings.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Newspaper/Publication       Associated Figure

**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Figure             Political Affiliation/Role
1.  Motilal Nehru               :   Swarajist Party Leader

**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Act                     Year
1.  Partition of Bengal           :   1905
2.  Morley-Minto Reforms        :   1909
3.  Rowlatt Act                   :   1919
4.  Montague-Chelmsford Reforms :   1919
5.  Jallianwala Bagh Massacre    :   1919


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. The partition of Bengal took place in 1905, a pivotal event that sparked the Swadeshi movement. The Morley-Minto Reforms were introduced in 1909, offering limited constitutional changes.  The Rowlatt Act was passed in 1919, granting the government extraordinary powers to suppress dissent. The Montague-Chelmsford Reforms, also known as the Government of India Act 1919, introduced further constitutional reforms. The Jallianwala Bagh massacre occurred in 1919, a tragic event that significantly impacted the course of the Indian independence movement.  These dates are firmly established in historical records and represent key milestones in the political development of India during the British Raj.  The incorrect options demonstrate the importance of accurate chronological knowledge of these significant events.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                          Known For/Associated With
1.  Lord Curzon                    :   Partition of Bengal
2.  Lord Lytton                    :   Vernacular Press Act
3.  Lord Dalhousie                 :   Doctrine of Lapse
4.  Lord Hastings                  :   Anglo-Nepalese War
5.  Lord William Bentinck          :   Abolition of Sati


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. Lord Curzon is infamously known for his role in the Partition of Bengal in 1905. Lord Lytton enacted the Vernacular Press Act of 1878, restricting the freedom of the Indian press.  Lord Dalhousie implemented the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy that resulted in the annexation of several Indian princely states.  Lord Hastings' tenure as Governor-General saw the Anglo-Nepalese War.  Lord William Bentinck is remembered for the abolition of Sati, a significant social reform.  These associations are well-documented and represent significant aspects of British rule in India.  The incorrect options highlight the need for thorough knowledge of the actions and policies of these key figures in British Indian history.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Jawaharlal Nehru, along with detailed explanations:


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Person                     Position/Association
    1. Jawaharlal Nehru         :  President, Lahore Congress
    2. Jawaharlal Nehru         :  Minister of External Affairs
    3. Lal Bahadur Shastri      :  Successor to Jawaharlal Nehru as Prime Minister
    4. Mahatma Gandhi          :  Opponent of Nehru's socialist leanings

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

Jawaharlal Nehru's presidency over the Lahore Congress session in 1929 is a well-established fact, where the declaration of Purna Swaraj was adopted.  His significant role as India's first Minister of External Affairs, shaping the nation's foreign policy, is also widely known. Lal Bahadur Shastri's succession to Nehru as Prime Minister after Nehru's death is a matter of historical record.  While Nehru and Gandhi shared a complex relationship marked by collaboration and disagreement,  Gandhi did express concerns about Nehru's socialist leanings and their potential impact on India's development.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Person                     Historical Event/Movement
    1. Jawaharlal Nehru         :  Non-Cooperation Movement
    2. Subhas Chandra Bose    :  Forward Bloc Founder
    3. Mahatma Gandhi          :  Champaran Satyagraha
    4. Lord Mountbatten          :  Partition of India


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

Jawaharlal Nehru's active participation in the Non-Cooperation Movement is well-documented.  Subhas Chandra Bose's founding of the Forward Bloc is a key event in his political career and the history of Indian nationalism. Mahatma Gandhi's leadership of the Champaran Satyagraha is a foundational moment in his career and the Indian independence movement. Lord Mountbatten's role in overseeing the Partition of India is central to understanding this pivotal moment in Indian history.  All four pairs accurately reflect the historical connections between the individuals and events.  Therefore, options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude at least one correct pairing.


**3. With reference to the Nehru Report, consider the following pairs:**

    Feature                      Description
    1. Dominion Status           :  Rejected by Nehru Report
    2. Joint Electorates          :  Proposed by Nehru Report
    3. Fundamental Rights        :  Included in Nehru Report
    4.  Separate Electorates      :  Recommended by Nehru Report


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Nehru Report, drafted in 1928, proposed Dominion Status as a pathway to self-governance for India, thus rejecting complete independence. Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect. The report advocated for joint electorates, rejecting the system of separate electorates based on religious identity. Pair 2 is correct. The report also included a chapter on fundamental rights, outlining basic civil liberties. Pair 3 is correct.  Pair 4 is wrong because separate electorates were specifically rejected.  Therefore only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either include incorrectly matched pairs or exclude correctly matched ones.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

    Person                     Associated Ideology/Policy
    1. Jawaharlal Nehru         :  Non-Alignment Movement
    2. Mahatma Gandhi          :  Satyagraha
    3.  Lord Curzon              : Permanent Settlement
    4.  Dadabhai Naoroji         :  Drain Theory


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Jawaharlal Nehru played a crucial role in establishing and promoting the Non-Aligned Movement during the Cold War. Mahatma Gandhi's advocacy and practice of Satyagraha as a method of non-violent resistance are well-known. Dadabhai Naoroji's articulation of the "Drain Theory," highlighting the economic exploitation of India under British rule, is a significant contribution to nationalist thought. However, Lord Curzon is associated with implementing policies like the partition of Bengal and the creation of the North-West Frontier Province, but not the Permanent Settlement, which is linked to Lord Cornwallis. Thus, only pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect.


**5. With reference to the Government of India Act of 1935, consider the following pairs:**

    Feature                      Characteristic
    1. Provincial Autonomy       :  Replaced Dyarchy
    2. All-India Federation      :  Never established
    3.  Communal Electorates     : Abolished by the Act
    4.  Adult Franchise           : Implemented fully


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act 1935 introduced provincial autonomy, replacing the earlier system of dyarchy. The proposed All-India Federation, a key feature of the Act, never materialized due to the non-participation of many princely states. The Act, however, did not abolish communal electorates; it actually retained and in some cases extended them.  Adult franchise was not fully implemented; the Act extended the franchise to a limited section of the Indian population.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d)  incorrectly include pairs 3 and/or 4.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader of Indian National Congress      Year of Presidency

3. Surendranath Banerjea                : 1885

5.  Womesh Chandra Bonnerjee             : 1885

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Womesh Chandra Bonnerjee presided over the inaugural session of the Indian National Congress in 1885. Dadabhai Naoroji's presidencies were in 1886, 1893, and 1906.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale's presidency was in 1905.  Badruddin Tyabji's presidency was in 1887. Therefore, only pairs 3 and 5 are correctly matched. The other options incorrectly assign presidencies to various Congress leaders.  The question tests factual recall of key figures and their roles in the early years of the Indian National Congress, highlighting the importance of understanding the leadership transitions within the organization during its formative years.  Option (a), (b), and (d) represent plausible distractors by including some correct and some incorrect pairings, thus requiring careful analysis of each pair.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Event                                    Congress President
1. Surat Split                             : Gopal Krishna Gokhale
2. Lucknow Pact (1916)                     : Ambika Charan Majumdar
3. Calcutta Session (1886)                 : Dadabhai Naoroji
4.  Lahore Session (1929)                 : Jawaharlal Nehru
5.  Haripura Session (1938)               : Subhas Chandra Bose


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 5 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Surat Split of 1907 was presided over by Rash Behari Ghosh, not Gopal Krishna Gokhale. The Lucknow Pact of 1916 was presided over by Ambika Charan Majumdar. Dadabhai Naoroji presided over the Calcutta session of 1886. Jawaharlal Nehru presided over the Lahore session of 1929. Subhas Chandra Bose presided over the Haripura session of 1938.  Therefore, only pairs 3 and 5 are correctly matched. This question assesses the candidate's knowledge of significant events in the Indian National Congress and their corresponding presidents.  The inclusion of incorrect pairings, such as the Surat Split and the involvement of prominent leaders like Gokhale and Nehru, acts as a strong distractor, making simple recall inadequate for success.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Movement                                    Key Leader
1. Non-Cooperation Movement              : Bal Gangadhar Tilak
2. Civil Disobedience Movement           : Subhas Chandra Bose
3. Quit India Movement                     : Mahatma Gandhi
4.  Home Rule Movement (1916)            : Annie Besant
5.  Swadeshi Movement                     :  Dadabhai Naoroji



Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 3 and 4 only
(b) 2 and 5 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

While Tilak was a significant figure in Indian nationalism, he wasn't the primary leader of the Non-Cooperation Movement; that role belonged to Mahatma Gandhi. Similarly, Subhas Chandra Bose was not the primary leader of the Civil Disobedience Movement, although he was a prominent participant.  The Quit India Movement was indeed led by Mahatma Gandhi.  Annie Besant played a crucial role in the Home Rule Movement of 1916. Dadabhai Naoroji, while a key figure in early Indian nationalism, was not the primary leader of the Swadeshi Movement; it had a broader leadership base. Thus, only pairs 3 and 4 correctly match movements with their key leaders. This question tests the understanding of various movements within the Indian independence struggle and their primary leaders, requiring detailed knowledge beyond superficial understanding of the movement's chronology.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Congress Session Location            Year
1. Calcutta                               : 1901
2. Surat                                  : 1907
3. Lucknow                               : 1916
4.  Lahore                                : 1929
5.  Allahabad                             : 1939


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 2, 3 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5
(d) 1 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Indian National Congress held sessions in Calcutta in multiple years, but not in 1901.  The Surat session was indeed in 1907. The Lucknow session was in 1916. The Lahore session was in 1929. The Allahabad session was not in 1939 but in 1939. Therefore, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. This question tests factual knowledge related to the locations and years of important Congress sessions. The inclusion of incorrect years for known session locations and the inclusion of a less-known session location (Allahabad) adds a layer of difficulty, testing for precise and detailed recall.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                 Publication
1.  Dadabhai Naoroji                     :  Hind Swaraj
2.  Mahatma Gandhi                      :  Poverty and Un-British Rule in India
3.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak                  :  New India
4.  Annie Besant                         :  Kesari
5.  Subhas Chandra Bose                 : Forward


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji authored "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India," not "Hind Swaraj," which was written by Mahatma Gandhi.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak edited "Kesari," not "New India," which was associated with Annie Besant.  Subhas Chandra Bose was associated with the publication "Forward."  Therefore, only pairs 4 and 5 are correctly matched.  This question tests the candidate’s knowledge of prominent nationalist leaders and their associated publications, requiring specific knowledge of their writings and journalistic activities.  The inclusion of plausible distractors, like associating Gandhi with Naoroji's book, makes this question challenging and tests the candidate’s ability to differentiate between closely related information.



**6. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                     Political Affiliation/Group
1.  Motilal Nehru                           :  No-changers
2.  Vallabhbhai Patel                       :  Swarajists
3.  C. Rajagopalachari                     :  No-changers

5.  Jawaharlal Nehru                       :  Congress Socialist Party


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2, 4 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Motilal Nehru was a prominent Swarajist, not a No-changer. Vallabhbhai Patel was indeed associated with the No-changers. C. Rajagopalachari was a No-changer. Chittaranjan Das was a key leader of the Swarajists.  Jawaharlal Nehru was associated with the Congress Socialist Party. Therefore, only pairs 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched. This question tests the understanding of the different factions within the Indian National Congress, requiring knowledge of their ideologies and key figures. The inclusion of closely related but incorrect affiliations (like associating Nehru with the No-changers) creates strong distractors, requiring careful analysis and understanding of the nuances within the Congress's internal dynamics.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Title/Position Held

(c) 3 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Kailash Nath Katju was the first Law Minister of India.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because, while all three individuals held significant positions in the Indian government, none of them were the first to hold the post of Law Minister. The question tests factual recall of a specific historical position. The distractors are designed to be plausible, as all named individuals were prominent figures in the early years of independent India, leading a candidate to potentially misremember their exact roles.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Figure       Comparison Made

(d) 4 only

The other options are incorrect because they misattribute the comparison to other prominent figures of the Indian independence movement. The question assesses factual recall and understanding of historical comparisons and interpretations.  The distractors include other significant figures from the era, making it challenging for a candidate who might not precisely remember the details of Gokhale's critique.

**19. Consider the following pairs:**

    Land Revenue System         Region of Implementation
