**20. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reform/Issue        British Government's Attitude Post-1857
1.  Sati                        Supported its abolition
2.  Widow Remarriage          Actively promoted it
3.  Caste System               Attempted to dismantle it

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Following the 1857 revolt, the British government supported the abolition of Sati, though the process was gradual and faced resistance.  However, they did not actively promote widow remarriage or attempt to dismantle the caste system. Instead,  their post-1857 policies often inadvertently strengthened caste and communal divisions.  This question assesses the candidate's knowledge of British social policy and its complexities. The distractors are designed to highlight potential misconceptions about British intentions regarding social reform in India.  The question assesses evaluation and interdisciplinary linkage understanding (linking social reform with political context).


These questions exemplify the desired format and difficulty level, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and evaluation while incorporating plausible distractors.  They require a deeper understanding of the subject matter than simple rote learning.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                      Title/Position Held
1.  Rabindranath Tagore         Nobel Laureate
2.  Lord Curzon                  Viceroy of India
3.  C. Rajagopalachari          Governor-General of India
4.  Vallabhbhai Patel           President of the Indian National Congress
5.  Sarojini Naidu              Governor of the United Provinces

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

Rabindranath Tagore was indeed a recipient of the Nobel Prize in Literature.  C. Rajagopalachari served as the last Governor-General of India.  Sarojini Naidu held the position of Governor of the United Provinces.  These are all verifiable historical facts.

Option (a) is incorrect because while 1 and 3 are correct, Vallabhbhai Patel never held the position of President of the Indian National Congress. Though a prominent leader, he was never elected to the presidential post.  

Option (b) is incorrect for the same reason as (a) and because Lord Curzon's primary position was Viceroy of India, not a title.  The term "Viceroy" itself denotes a position.

Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the incorrect pairings mentioned above, further highlighting the importance of precise factual knowledge in these kinds of questions. The question tests the candidate's ability to differentiate between titles and positions held and to recall accurate historical information about prominent figures in Indian history.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization                Associated Act/Policy
1. Archaeological Survey of India : Ancient Monuments Preservation Act, 1904
2.  Ministry of Culture          :  National Mission for Manuscripts (NMM)
3. Police Commission            : Lord Wellesley's Subsidiary Alliance
4.  Indian National Congress    :  Curzon's Approach (to Indian Politics)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

The Archaeological Survey of India is indeed responsible for enforcing the Ancient Monuments Preservation Act, 1904, a crucial piece of legislation for the protection of historical sites. This is a direct and easily verifiable fact.

Option (b) is incorrect because while the Archaeological Survey of India is under the aegis of the Ministry of Culture and recommended the establishment of the National Mission for Manuscripts, the Ministry of Culture itself didn't "create" or directly "associate" with the NMM in the way the question implies.  The relationship is more nuanced than a simple association.

Option (c) is incorrect because while the Indian National Congress was certainly impacted by Curzon's policies, there's no direct association or "act" called "Curzon's Approach."  Curzon's policies were multifaceted and influenced various aspects of Indian politics.  The pair lacks the precise factual link required for a correct match.

Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the inaccurate pairings described above, and further, Lord Wellesley's Subsidiary Alliance is not directly associated with the Police Commission.  While both relate to British administration in India, they are distinct policies.  This highlights the need for precise understanding of the historical context and the specific links between entities.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Figure            Associated Movement/Event
1.  Mahatma Gandhi             Rowlatt Satyagraha
2.  Vallabhbhai Patel          Ahmedabad Mill Strike
3.  Lord William Bentinck     Bardoli Satyagraha
4.  Lord Wellesley             Non-Cooperation Movement

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Mahatma Gandhi was the leader of the Rowlatt Satyagraha, a significant event in the Indian independence movement. Vallabhbhai Patel played a key role in the Ahmedabad Mill Strike, using his skills in negotiation and mediation to resolve the conflict.

Option (b) is incorrect because it excludes the correct pairing of Vallabhbhai Patel and the Ahmedabad Mill Strike.

Option (c) is incorrect because Lord William Bentinck was not associated with the Bardoli Satyagraha;  this event occurred much later and was primarily associated with Vallabhbhai Patel. Also, Lord Wellesley did not directly lead or have primary involvement in the Non-Cooperation Movement.  The Non-Cooperation Movement was primarily led by Mahatma Gandhi.

Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the inaccurate pairings mentioned above, thus emphasizing the importance of precise knowledge of historical events and their leaders.  The question tests the candidate's ability to correctly link historical figures to specific movements, which requires detailed knowledge of Indian history.


**4.  With reference to prominent figures of the Indian independence movement, consider the following pairs:**

   Person                      Published Work/Newspaper
1.  Dadabhai Naoroji           Poverty and Un-British Rule in India
2.  Bankim Chandra Chatterjee  Anand Math
3.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak        Amrita Bazar Patrika
4.  Rabindranath Tagore        Gitanjali

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji authored "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India," a seminal work on the economic exploitation of India under British rule. Bankim Chandra Chatterjee wrote "Anand Math," a novel that significantly influenced Indian nationalism. Rabindranath Tagore's "Gitanjali" is a collection of poems that won him the Nobel Prize in Literature. These are all established facts.

Option (a) is incorrect because it excludes the correct pairing of Rabindranath Tagore and Gitanjali.

Option (c) is incorrect because Bal Gangadhar Tilak did not publish the Amrita Bazar Patrika.  While he was a prolific writer and editor, the Amrita Bazar Patrika was associated with other nationalist leaders.

Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the incorrect pairing mentioned above, thus highlighting the need for precise knowledge of the published works of important historical figures.  The question tests the examinee's ability to connect authors with their writings, a crucial aspect of understanding the intellectual and cultural landscape of the Indian independence movement.


**5. With reference to the early phases of the Indian National Congress, consider the following pairs:**

   Person                    Position/Role in INC
1.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale     President of the INC (1905)
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji           President of the INC (1906)
3.  Surendranath Banerjea      Founder of INC
4.  A. O. Hume                Key figure in the founding of the INC

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Gopal Krishna Gokhale presided over the 1905 session of the Indian National Congress. Dadabhai Naoroji presided over the 1906 session. A. O. Hume played a crucial role in the founding of the INC. These are all well-documented historical facts.

Option (a) is incorrect because it excludes the accurate pairing of A. O. Hume with his role in the founding of the INC.

Option (b) is incorrect because it excludes the correct pairings of Gokhale and Naoroji as presidents of the INC.

Option (d) is incorrect because Surendranath Banerjea was not a founder of the INC; while a prominent leader, he wasn't among the initial founders. The question assesses the candidate's understanding of the early leadership and organizational structure of the Indian National Congress.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   City                 Significant Event

4. Allahabad           Location of the Congress Working Committee meetings

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched.  The first session of the Indian National Congress was held in Bombay in 1885.  While the text doesn't explicitly state the location of *every* Congress session, it mentions the Bombay session of 1918.  Madras served as a significant administrative center for the East India Company, and the text highlights its importance.  Finally, the text mentions Allahabad as a location for Congress Working Committee meetings. These facts are all verifiable and consistent with historical records of the Indian National Congress and the British East India Company.  The options are designed to create plausible distractors, making the examinee carefully consider each pair before selecting the correct answer.  Option (a), (b) and (c)  present partially correct information,  tempting the candidate to choose an incomplete answer.  Only option (d) encompasses all the correctly matched pairs, demonstrating a comprehensive understanding of the historical context.



**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person               Association with a Major Movement
1. Vallabhbhai Patel     Leader of the Non-Cooperation Movement

(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

While Vallabhbhai Patel was a prominent figure in the Indian National Congress and participated in many movements, he is primarily known for leading the Bardoli Satyagraha, not the Non-Cooperation Movement.  Mahatma Gandhi was indeed the key leader of the Kheda Satyagraha, which focused on peasant grievances due to crop failure.  Rajendra Prasad played a significant role in the Champaran Satyagraha, supporting Gandhi's efforts.  N.G. Ranga's major contribution was to the Kisan movement, and his involvement with the Bardoli Satyagraha, though possible, isn't as prominently documented as Patel's leadership.  The question tests the candidate's ability to distinguish between primary and secondary roles within major historical events. Options (a), (b) and (d) include at least one incorrect pairing, designed as distractors to test the candidate's knowledge of the specific leadership roles within these movements.  The correct answer, (c), demonstrates an understanding of the key individuals involved in the Kheda and Champaran Satyagrahas.

   Book                   Author

These works are significant in understanding the intellectual and philosophical underpinnings of the Indian independence movement. **4. With reference to the early phase of the Indian National Congress (1885-1905), consider the following pairs:**

Gopal Krishna Gokhale was a leader of the Moderate faction, not the Extremists.  Surendranath Banerjea did indeed found the Indian Association, a crucial precursor to the Congress. W.C. Bonnerjee was the first president of the Indian National Congress.  The options are designed to include plausible but incorrect statements, testing the candidate's detailed knowledge of the period. **5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy             Primary Impact
1.  Rowlatt Act             Increased nationalist resistance
2.  Doctrine of Lapse      Led to the annexation of several princely states
3.  Ilbert Bill             Caused widespread communal tension
4.  Wood's Despatch        Focused primarily on military reforms

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

The question assesses the candidate's understanding of British policies and their impact on the Indian political landscape. The Rowlatt Act, with its repressive measures, significantly fueled nationalist resistance. The Doctrine of Lapse, a policy of annexation, led to the absorption of several princely states into British India. The Ilbert Bill, though debated, did not primarily cause communal tension; that was more a result of other policies and events. Wood's Despatch was primarily focused on educational reforms, not military ones.  The options are carefully constructed to include plausible but incorrect connections, testing the candidate's ability to differentiate between the true impact of each act or policy. Option (a) correctly identifies the impact of the Rowlatt Act and the Doctrine of Lapse, demonstrating a solid understanding of their historical consequences. Options (b), (c), and (d) include at least one incorrect or misleading pairing, functioning as distractors.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and require detailed knowledge of Indian history and the individuals involved.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Publication                          Author/Associated Person
1.  Young India                         :   Lord Irwin
2.  Hind Swaraj                         :   Annie Besant
3.  Kesari                              :   Bal Gangadhar Tilak
4.  Bande Mataram                      :   M.A. Jinnah
5.  New India                           :   Jawaharlal Nehru

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 3 and 5 only
(d) 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3, associating *Kesari* with Bal Gangadhar Tilak, is correctly matched.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak founded and edited the Marathi newspaper *Kesari*, a significant platform for his nationalist views and advocacy of Swaraj.

The other options are incorrect for the following reasons:

* **Pair 1:**  While Mahatma Gandhi wrote in *Young India*, Lord Irwin was the Viceroy of India during a crucial period of Gandhi's political activity, including the Gandhi-Irwin Pact.  However, there's no direct authorship or primary association between Lord Irwin and *Young India*.

* **Pair 2:**  *Hind Swaraj* was authored by Mahatma Gandhi, not Annie Besant.  Besant was a prominent Theosophist and nationalist leader, but she is not associated with this particular publication.

* **Pair 4:**  While M.A. Jinnah was a pivotal figure in Indian politics and the creation of Pakistan, he is not associated with the publication *Bande Mataram*.  This newspaper was a significant nationalist publication, but it wasn't primarily associated with Jinnah.

* **Pair 5:**  Annie Besant, not Jawaharlal Nehru, was associated with the publication *New India*. Nehru was a key figure in the Indian National Congress and later became the first Prime Minister of India, but *New India* was primarily associated with Besant's Home Rule Movement.


**2. With reference to the Indian freedom struggle, consider the following pairs:**

   Individual/Organization             Action/Policy
1. Lord William Bentinck                :   Implemented the Subsidiary Alliance System
2. Lord Wellesley                       :   Took control of Mysore state due to alleged maladministration
3.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak                  :   Criticized the Montford Reforms
4. Mahatma Gandhi                      :  Opposed the partition of India
5.  Annie Besant                         :  Led the Home Rule Movement

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Pairs 3, 4, and 5 are correctly matched. Bal Gangadhar Tilak, known for his extremist views, strongly criticized the inadequate nature of the Montford Reforms.  Mahatma Gandhi, despite his efforts at reconciliation, actively opposed the partition of India. Annie Besant played a leading role in the Home Rule Movement, advocating for greater Indian self-governance.

The incorrect pairs are:

* **Pair 1:** Lord William Bentinck is incorrectly linked to the Subsidiary Alliance System. This system was a key feature of Lord Wellesley's governance.  Bentinck implemented significant social reforms but not this specific policy.

* **Pair 2:** Lord Wellesley is incorrectly paired with taking control of Mysore. While he was instrumental in the downfall of Tipu Sultan and the subsequent British control over Mysore, the annexation and subsequent taking over of the administration was a more complex process involving multiple Governors-General and not solely attributed to Wellesley. Lord William Bentinck later assumed control of Mysore due to alleged maladministration.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                   Stance on Untouchability
1.  Lord Curzon                           :   Supported the abolition of Untouchability
2.  M.K. Gandhi                           :   Actively opposed Untouchability
3.  Lord Hastings                         :   Remained neutral on the issue of Untouchability
4.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak                   :   Supported the continuation of Untouchability
5.  Aurobindo Ghosh                      :   Advocated for the reform of Untouchability


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 only
(b) 2 and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 5 are definitively and accurately matched. M.K. Gandhi is well-known for his staunch opposition to untouchability, a key element of his social reform agenda. Aurobindo Ghosh, while not as explicitly focused on the issue as Gandhi, advocated for social reform that implicitly included addressing the issue of untouchability as part of a broader vision of societal transformation.

The other options are problematic due to insufficient evidence or inaccurate representation:

* **Pair 1:**  Lord Curzon's policies primarily focused on administrative and economic reforms; there is no clear evidence to support a definitive stance on untouchability.

* **Pair 3:**  Lord Hastings' actions largely focused on military and territorial expansion.  His position on untouchability is not well-documented or consistently clear.

* **Pair 4:**  While Tilak's primary focus was on political nationalism, there's no strong evidence to definitively claim he supported the continuation of untouchability. His social reform views were less prominent than his political work.  Attributing a specific stance on untouchability to him would be an oversimplification.


These questions are designed to test not just factual recall but also the ability to analyze and evaluate information, differentiate between strong and weak evidence, and avoid making assumptions based on incomplete data—all crucial skills for success in the UPSC exam.  The distractors are carefully chosen to represent plausible but ultimately incorrect connections, making the questions more challenging.

(b) 1, 2, and 3 only

(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

Jawaharlal Nehru played a crucial role in drafting the *Objectives Resolution*, a foundational document for the Indian Constitution.  Abul Kalam Azad authored *India Wins Freedom*, a significant historical account of the Indian independence movement. Ram Manohar Lohia was a prominent leader of the Socialist Party in India, advocating for socialist ideals and policies.  Dr. Rajendra Prasad, as the President of the Constituent Assembly, played a pivotal role in the drafting and adoption of the *Indian Constitution*.  The options that exclude one or more of these correctly matched pairs are therefore incorrect. **5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                 Associated Figure

(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. Lord Canning is associated with the policy of Masterly Inactivity, a cautious approach to governance. Lord Linlithgow served as Viceroy during the enactment of the Government of India Act 1935. The other options contain inaccuracies. The Indian Councils Act of 1892 was enacted during the viceroyalty of Lord Lansdowne, not Lord Curzon. While the Rowlatt Act was passed during the Viceroyalty of Lord Chelmsford, it's more strongly associated with the repressive policies of the British government during that period than with Chelmsford himself. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of specific acts and policies within the British Indian context and their association with key figures, requiring accurate factual recall.  The distractors are carefully chosen to test the candidate's understanding of the context surrounding each act.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Individual/Organization       Activity/Association
1.  Jawaharlal Nehru             :  Differed with Mahatma Gandhi on certain policies
2.  Narsinh Mehta                :  Influenced Mahatma Gandhi's philosophy
3.  Ahmedabad Textile Labour Association : Founded by Mahatma Gandhi
4.  Jayaprakash Narayan          : Shared ideological alignment with Mahatma Gandhi

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched.  Jawaharlal Nehru, while a close associate and successor to Gandhi, held differing views on certain political and economic strategies.  This difference in approach is well-documented in historical accounts of the Indian National Congress and the post-independence period. Narsinh Mehta, a prominent Gujarati poet and saint, significantly influenced Gandhi's philosophy of life and his approach to social reform, particularly through his devotional poetry.  The Ahmedabad Textile Labour Association (ATLA) was a key organization founded by Mahatma Gandhi, demonstrating his commitment to labor rights and social justice.  Finally, Jayaprakash Narayan, a prominent socialist leader, shared a strong ideological affinity with Gandhi, particularly regarding non-violent resistance and social reform. Their collaboration on various social and political movements further strengthens this connection.  Therefore, all four pairs reflect accurately documented historical relationships and activities.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Movement                 Location
1.  Champaran Satyagraha           :  Bihar
2.  Kheda Satyagraha               :  Gujarat

4.  Ahmedabad Mill Strike          :  Gujarat

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

While Champaran Satyagraha took place in Bihar and Kheda Satyagraha in Gujarat, and Ahmedabad Mill Strike in Gujarat, the Rowlatt Satyagraha was a nationwide movement, not confined to a single province like Punjab.  Although protests and arrests related to the Rowlatt Act occurred in Punjab, the movement's scope extended across India. The other three pairs accurately reflect the geographical locations of the respective events.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 4 are correctly matched.

Ahimsa, the principle of non-violence, is synonymous with Gandhi's philosophy, making this a straightforward match. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Viceroy/Governor-General          Action Related to Press
1. Lord Lytton                         : Implemented the Vernacular Press Act of 1878
2. Lord Ripon                          : Repealed the Vernacular Press Act of 1878
3. Lord Curzon                         : Increased restrictions on the press during Swadeshi movement
4. Lord Metcalfe                       : Lifted restrictions on the Indian press in 1835

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Lytton's administration enacted the Vernacular Press Act of 1878, a restrictive measure aimed at controlling the Indian-language press, which was seen as increasingly critical of British rule.  This act severely curtailed the freedom of the press in India.  Subsequently, Lord Ripon, recognizing the unjust nature of the restrictions, repealed the Vernacular Press Act in 1882, demonstrating a comparatively more liberal approach towards the press.  Lord Metcalfe's tenure saw a period of relative freedom for the Indian press when he lifted existing restrictions in 1835. This reflects a more open policy compared to the subsequent restrictive measures implemented later.  While Lord Curzon's time witnessed increased restrictions on the press, particularly during the Swadeshi movement,  it is important to note that the specific act mentioned in the question (Vernacular Press Act) is directly linked to Lytton and Ripon's actions.  Option (d) is incorrect as it includes an inaccurate association with Lord Curzon. Option (a) is too narrow, and options (b) are incomplete, neglecting Metcalfe's significant contribution.  The correct answer accurately reflects the historical record concerning the interplay between these viceroys and their policies towards the Indian press.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                    Significant Contribution/Association
1. Dadabhai Naoroji                       : Founded the East India Association in London
2. Surendranath Banerjea                 : Founded the Indian Association in Calcutta
3. A. O. Hume                             : Founded the Indian National Congress
4. W. C. Bonnerjee                        : First President of the Indian National Congress


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent figure in the Indian independence movement, established the East India Association in London to advocate for Indian interests in Britain.  Surendranath Banerjea played a crucial role in the early nationalist movement, founding the Indian Association in Calcutta, which served as a precursor to the Indian National Congress. A. O. Hume, a retired British civil servant, is widely credited with the founding of the Indian National Congress in 1885, providing a platform for organized nationalist activity. W. C. Bonnerjee presided over the inaugural session of the Indian National Congress, making him its first president.  All four pairs accurately represent the contributions of these individuals to the growth of Indian nationalism and the establishment of key political organizations.  Therefore, option (d) is the only correct answer, encompassing all the correctly matched pairs.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Land Revenue System                     Region Primarily Implemented
1. Ryotwari System                          : Bengal Presidency
2. Zamindari System                         : Madras Presidency
3. Mahalwari System                         : North-Western Provinces
4. Permanent Settlement                     : Bombay Presidency

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Mahalwari system, a land revenue system prevalent in parts of northern India, was primarily implemented in the North-Western Provinces.  Options 1 and 2 are incorrect because the Ryotwari system was mainly implemented in Madras and Bombay Presidencies, while the Zamindari system was primarily in Bengal.  The Permanent Settlement was primarily in Bengal. The question tests the knowledge of the different land revenue systems implemented by the British and the regions where they were predominantly applied. Option (c) is the only correct answer, accurately reflecting the historical implementation of the Mahalwari system.  The other options represent incorrect pairings of land revenue systems and regions.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Governor-General/Viceroy             Policy/Action Implemented
1. Lord Dalhousie                         : Introduced the Doctrine of Lapse
2. Lord Curzon                           : Partition of Bengal
3. Lord Lytton                            : Implemented the Vernacular Press Act
4. Lord Wellesley                          : Introduced the Subsidiary Alliance System


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Dalhousie's tenure as Governor-General saw the implementation of the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy that led to the annexation of several Indian states. Lord Lytton's administration implemented the Vernacular Press Act, restricting the freedom of the Indian-language press. Lord Wellesley's period as Governor-General witnessed the introduction of the Subsidiary Alliance system, a key element of British expansionist policy. Option (b) is incorrect because it excludes the accurate pairing of Lord Wellesley and the Subsidiary Alliance. Option (a) is too narrow, and option (d) is incorrect as it incorrectly links Lord Curzon with the Partition of Bengal. The Partition of Bengal was actually implemented by Lord Curzon, but this specific act is not directly mentioned in the source material.  The correct option (c) accurately reflects the historical record concerning the policies and actions of these Governors-General.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Social Reformer                        Significant Reform/Contribution
1. Raja Ram Mohan Roy                  :  Abolition of Sati
2. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar           : Widow Remarriage Act
3.  Dadabhai Naoroji                     :  Economic critique of British rule

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Raja Ram Mohan Roy is renowned for his pivotal role in the abolition of Sati, a practice of widow immolation. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar championed the cause of widow remarriage and played a significant role in the passing of the Widow Remarriage Act. Dadabhai Naoroji is celebrated for his insightful economic critiques of British rule in India, exposing the exploitative nature of colonial policies. Option (d) is correct as all three pairs accurately reflect the significant contributions of these social reformers.  The other options are incomplete, failing to recognize the multifaceted contributions of these figures to social and political reform in India.  The question assesses the ability to connect social reformers with their specific contributions to social reform during the Indian renaissance.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and require in-depth knowledge of Indian history and the roles of various organizations and individuals.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Individual        Action/Association
1.  Lord Curzon                     :  Established Pusa Agricultural Research Institute
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji                :  Authored "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India"
3.  Subhas Chandra Bose            :  Formed the Forward Bloc
4.  Mahatma Gandhi                 :  Led the Non-Cooperation Movement
5.  The Crown                        :  Held paramount power over Princely States

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched.  Lord Curzon, during his viceroyalty, established the Pusa Agricultural Research Institute (now the Indian Agricultural Research Institute) to modernize Indian agriculture. Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent early nationalist leader, authored the seminal work "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India," which detailed the economic exploitation of India under British rule. Subhas Chandra Bose, after a split with the Congress, formed the Forward Bloc, a political party advocating for complete independence. Mahatma Gandhi led the Non-Cooperation Movement, a major non-violent resistance campaign against British rule.  Finally, the British Crown held paramount power over the Princely States in India, meaning it had ultimate authority and control over their internal affairs, despite their nominal independence.  The other options incorrectly exclude one or more of these accurately matched pairs, demonstrating a lack of complete understanding of the historical context and the roles played by these individuals and entities.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Movement                     Location Primarily Associated
1.  The Wavell Plan                    :  Simla
2.  The Partition of Bengal             :  Calcutta
3.  The Champaran Satyagraha         :  Bihar
4.  The Quit India Movement            :  Bombay
5.  The Tebhaga Movement              :  Bengal


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 5 only
(d) 2, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

The Wavell Plan, a British proposal for Indian independence, was primarily associated with Simla, where negotiations took place. The Champaran Satyagraha, Mahatma Gandhi's first major campaign in India, was launched in Bihar. The Tebhaga movement, a peasant uprising demanding land redistribution, was centered in Bengal.  Options (a), (b), and (d) contain inaccuracies. While the Partition of Bengal had significant consequences for Calcutta, it wasn't the *primary* location associated with the event's initiation.  Similarly, the Quit India Movement, though widespread, had multiple centers of activity, and Bombay was not its singular focal point.  Understanding the nuances of historical events and their geographical contexts is crucial for a correct response. The careful selection of distractors tests the candidate's precise knowledge, preventing simple elimination strategies.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                 Role/Association
1.  Nirmal Kumar Bose                   :  Secretary to Mahatma Gandhi during Noakhali
2.  Mahadeo Desai                       :  Long-time secretary to Mahatma Gandhi
3.  Pyarelal                              :  Author of Mahatma Gandhi's biography
4.  Robert Clive                          :  Established the Dual Government in Bengal
5.  Lord Cornwallis                      :  Abolished the Dual Government in Bengal


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2, 3, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

Mahadeo Desai served as a long-time personal secretary to Mahatma Gandhi. Pyarelal, another close associate, authored a multi-volume biography of Gandhi.  Lord Cornwallis, as Governor-General, abolished the Dual Government system in Bengal, a system previously established by Robert Clive. Option (a) is incorrect as while Nirmal Kumar Bose was associated with Gandhi, he wasn't his secretary during the Noakhali incident.  Option (c) incorrectly includes Nirmal Kumar Bose and incorrectly attributes the abolition of the Dual Government to Robert Clive. Option (d) omits the correct association of Lord Cornwallis with the abolition of the Dual Government.  The question tests the candidate’s ability to recall specific details about key figures and administrative systems in British India, highlighting the complexities and nuances of historical events.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader/Organization                Slogan/Policy
1.  Lal Bahadur Shastri               :  "Jai Jawan, Jai Kisan"
2.  Indian National Congress         :  Advocated for Purna Swaraj
3.  Muslim League                     :  Demanded the creation of Pakistan
4.  Lord Curzon                       :  Implemented the Partition of Bengal
5.  The Crown                        :  Declared Princely States' independence


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 5 only
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Lal Bahadur Shastri is correctly associated with the slogan "Jai Jawan, Jai Kisan" (Hail the Soldier, Hail the Farmer). The Indian National Congress adopted the goal of Purna Swaraj (complete self-rule). The Muslim League, under Jinnah's leadership, advocated for the creation of Pakistan. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because Lord Curzon did not implement the Partition of Bengal (that was Lord Curzon's Viceroyalty, but the partition was actually implemented by the then Viceroy, Lord Minto) and the Crown did not declare the Princely States' independence;  instead, it held paramountcy over them.  The question tests the candidate’s understanding of major political movements, slogans, and policies during the Indian independence struggle, requiring recall of specific details about prominent leaders and organizations.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Year                                  Event
1.  1878                               :  Vernacular Press Act
2.  1885                               :  Foundation of the Indian National Congress
3.  1785                               :  Fox's India Bill
4.  1898                               :  Lord Curzon becomes Viceroy of India
5.  1872                               :  First All-India Census


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The Vernacular Press Act was enacted in 1878. The Indian National Congress was founded in 1885. Fox's India Bill was introduced in 1785. Lord Curzon assumed the viceroyalty in 1898. Option (d) is incorrect because the first All-India Census was attempted in 1881, not 1872. This question tests the candidate's chronological understanding of key events in Indian history, requiring precise knowledge of dates and their association with significant legislation and political appointments.  The inclusion of a nearly correct but ultimately wrong date for the census serves as a strong distractor.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader                      Movement/Association
1. Mahatma Gandhi             :   Ahmedabad Textile Labour Association
2. Bal Gangadhar Tilak        :   Indian Home Rule League
3. M.N. Roy                   :   Congress Socialist Party
4. Tej Bahadur Sapru          :   National Liberal Federation
5. Jawaharlal Nehru            :   Bharat Naujawan Sabha


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Mahatma Gandhi founded the Ahmedabad Textile Labour Association in 1920 to address the concerns of textile workers.  This association played a crucial role in the labor movement and Gandhi's larger socio-economic vision for India.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak, a prominent leader of the Indian independence movement, played a key role in establishing the Indian Home Rule League in 1916. This organization aimed to promote self-governance and actively pushed for India's independence from British rule. Tej Bahadur Sapru was a prominent figure in the National Liberal Federation, a significant political organization during the Indian independence struggle.  The National Liberal Federation represented a more moderate approach to achieving self-governance compared to the more radical groups.

Option (a) is incorrect because M.N. Roy is associated with the formation of the Communist Party of India, not the Congress Socialist Party. The Congress Socialist Party, though influenced by socialist thought, was a distinct entity.  Option (b) is incorrect as Jawaharlal Nehru was not directly associated with the Bharat Naujawan Sabha, although he was a significant influence on the younger generation of nationalists. Option (c) is incorrect as it incorrectly includes M.N. Roy's association with the Congress Socialist Party. The inclusion of these incorrect pairings makes options (a), (b), and (c) incorrect.  Therefore, only option (d) accurately reflects the correct pairings.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Concept/Ideology              Prominent Advocate
1. Swaraj                         :   Dadabhai Naoroji
2. Satyagraha                     :   M.K. Gandhi
3. Socialism                      :   Bhagat Singh
4. Ramrajya                       :   Gopal Krishna Gokhale
5. Ahimsa                         :   Vinoba Bhave


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji, a pioneer of Indian nationalism, was a strong advocate of Swaraj, meaning self-rule. His contributions to the early nationalist movement laid the groundwork for future struggles. Mahatma Gandhi championed Satyagraha, a philosophy of non-violent resistance, as a powerful tool for achieving political and social change in India. This ideology became a defining characteristic of the Indian independence movement. Bhagat Singh, a prominent revolutionary, was a staunch advocate for socialism, believing in economic equality and social justice.  His revolutionary activities were deeply rooted in socialist ideals.

Option (a) is incomplete, omitting the crucial pairing of Bhagat Singh with socialism. Option (b) is also incomplete, leaving out Dadabhai Naoroji's advocacy for Swaraj. Option (d) is incorrect because it incorrectly attributes Ahimsa primarily to Vinoba Bhave; while Vinoba Bhave was a proponent of Ahimsa, Gandhi is more strongly associated with its widespread adoption and implementation within the Indian independence movement.  Option (c) accurately captures the direct and primary associations between the concepts and their most prominent advocates within the context of the Indian independence movement.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Publication                     Author/Editor
1. Hind Swaraj                   :   Mahatma Gandhi
2. Kesari                          :   Bal Gangadhar Tilak
3. Rang de Basanti Chola          :   Bhagat Singh
4. Amrita Bazar Patrika           :   Motilal Ghosh
5.  India                           :   British Committee of the Indian National Congress

(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, and 5 only
(d) All of the above

**Correct Answer:** (d) All of the above

**Explanation:**

Mahatma Gandhi authored Hind Swaraj, a seminal work outlining his political philosophy and critique of modern civilization. Bal Gangadhar Tilak edited the influential Marathi newspaper Kesari, which played a crucial role in shaping public opinion and mobilizing support for the Indian independence movement. Bhagat Singh authored Rang de Basanti, a powerful poem that became a rallying cry for Indian revolutionaries. Motilal Ghosh was associated with the establishment and editing of the Amrita Bazar Patrika, a prominent nationalist newspaper that played a significant role in disseminating nationalist ideas. The British Committee of the Indian National Congress published the journal "India" to propagate the Indian perspective in Britain.

All the pairs presented are correctly matched, highlighting the significant contributions of these publications and their authors/editors to the Indian independence movement.  There are no incorrect pairings, making option (d) the only correct choice.  The inclusion of multiple prominent publications and their creators makes this a challenging question, requiring strong factual recall.


**4. With reference to the Indian Independence Movement, consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Legislation               Key Figure/Leader
1. Champaran Satyagraha           :   Rajendra Prasad

3. Non-Cooperation Movement     :   Motilal Nehru
4.  Partition of India             :   Lord Mountbatten

(b) 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) All of the above

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

Rajendra Prasad played a significant role alongside Mahatma Gandhi in the Champaran Satyagraha, providing crucial support and organization.  Mahatma Gandhi led the widespread protests against the Rowlatt Act, a repressive piece of legislation enacted by the British. Lord Mountbatten, as the last Viceroy of India, played a pivotal role in the Partition of India, although it was a deeply complex and controversial event with multiple factors involved. The Gandhi-Irwin Pact was a significant agreement negotiated between Mahatma Gandhi and Lord Irwin, leading to a temporary suspension of the Civil Disobedience Movement.

Option (a) is incorrect as it omits the correct association of the Gandhi-Irwin Pact with Lord Irwin. Option (b) is also incorrect, leaving out the involvement of Rajendra Prasad in the Champaran Satyagraha. The inclusion of multiple events and individuals makes this a challenging question.

Jawaharlal Nehru became the first Prime Minister of India after independence in 1947, a fact widely acknowledged in historical records and textbooks.  M.A. Jinnah assumed the position of the first Governor-General of Pakistan upon its creation in 1947.  These are undisputed historical facts. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Commission                                   Provision/Outcome
1. Government of India Act, 1935                 :   Established Provincial autonomy
2. Indian Independence Act, 1947                 :   Granted Dominion status to India
3. Simon Commission                               :   Recommended Dominion status for India
4. Nehru Report (1928)                           :   Proposed adult suffrage


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act, 1935, significantly restructured the Indian governance system, introducing a system of provincial autonomy.  This marked a substantial devolution of power from the central government to the provinces, granting them considerable control over their internal affairs.  The Act's provisions laid the groundwork for the future federal structure of India, although the envisioned All-India Federation was never fully implemented.  Option 2 is incorrect as the Indian Independence Act, 1947, granted complete independence (not Dominion status) to India and Pakistan.  The Simon Commission, while investigating constitutional reforms, did not explicitly recommend Dominion status as the ultimate goal; its report was largely rejected by Indian nationalists. The Nehru Report, while advocating for Dominion Status as the next step, did indeed propose adult suffrage as a key feature of the future Indian constitution. Therefore, only pair 1 accurately reflects a direct outcome or provision of the mentioned Act/Commission. The other options incorrectly link Acts/Commissions with features or outcomes that were either not directly associated with them or were proposed but not directly implemented.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Document                                     Key Feature
1. Government of India Act, 1919                     :   Introduced Dyarchy
2. Government of India Act, 1935                     :   Established a Federal Public Service Commission
3. Nehru Report (1928)                               :   Proposed joint electorates


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act, 1919, implemented the Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms, a key feature of which was the introduction of Dyarchy, a dual system of governance in the provinces.  The Government of India Act, 1935, established a Federal Public Service Commission as part of its comprehensive constitutional framework. This commission was responsible for recruiting and managing civil servants at the federal level. The Nehru Report, while advocating for a variety of constitutional changes, did not propose joint electorates as a central feature; instead, it suggested reserving seats for religious minorities for a decade within a system of joint electorates.  Therefore, pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched, while pair 3 is incorrect due to a misrepresentation of the Nehru Report's proposals regarding electorates.


**3. With reference to the Government of India Act, 1935, consider the following pairs:**

   Feature                                              Impact
1. Establishment of Provincial Public Service Commissions:   Strengthened provincial administrative capacity.
2. Increased local bodies' authority                     :   Improved local governance efficiency.
3. Allocation of seats to princes                        :   Enhanced representation of princely states in the federal structure.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act 1935 established Provincial Public Service Commissions, significantly enhancing the capacity and efficiency of provincial administrations. These commissions were responsible for recruiting and managing provincial civil servants, ensuring merit-based appointments and promoting administrative professionalism.  The Act also increased the authority and responsibilities of local bodies, leading to improvements in local governance. This increased power, however, was accompanied by restrictions on their power to levy taxes. The Act also allocated seats to representatives from princely states in the federal legislature, ensuring their participation in the governance of the newly formed federation.  This aimed to integrate the princely states into the larger Indian federation, although it did not fully resolve the complex relationship between the states and the central government.  All three pairs accurately reflect the Act's features and their impacts.


**4. With reference to the Indian Independence Act, 1947, consider the following pairs:**

   Provision                                           Consequence
1. Grant of independence to India and Pakistan      :   Partition of the Indian subcontinent
2. Grant of sovereignty to the Constituent Assembly of India:   Establishment of a democratic republic
3. Effective date of August 14–15, 1947              :   Immediate transfer of power


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Indian Independence Act, 1947, directly resulted in the partition of the Indian subcontinent into India and Pakistan.  The Act's provisions formalized the division of British India, leading to the creation of two independent states. The Act also stipulated that the transfer of power would be effective from August 14–15, 1947, marking the end of British rule and the beginning of independence for both nations.  However, while the Act granted sovereignty to the Constituent Assemblies of both India and Pakistan, the establishment of a democratic republic in India was a subsequent development, resulting from the adoption and implementation of the Indian Constitution in 1950. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 accurately reflect direct consequences of the Act's provisions.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Person                                             Association/Activity
1. Gopal Krishna Gokhale                             :   Founded the Servants of India Society
2. Annie Besant                                       :   Led the Home Rule Movement
3. B.R. Ambedkar                                     :   Advocated for separate electorates for depressed classes

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Gopal Krishna Gokhale, a prominent Indian nationalist and social reformer, founded the Servants of India Society in 1905. This organization aimed to train individuals for public service and promote social and political reform.  Annie Besant, an Irish theosophist and nationalist, played a crucial role in leading the Home Rule Movement in India during World War I. This movement advocated for self-governance within the British Empire. B.R. Ambedkar, a Dalit leader and architect of the Indian Constitution, strongly advocated for separate electorates for the depressed classes (Dalits) during the constitutional negotiations of the 1930s. He believed that separate electorates would protect Dalit interests from the dominance of the caste Hindu majority.  All three pairs accurately reflect the individuals and their key associations or activities.  The other options incorrectly exclude one or more of these accurately matched pairs.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader                      Significant Association
1. Subhas Chandra Bose       :   President, Indian National Congress
2. Jawaharlal Nehru           :   President, Indian National Congress
3. Mahatma Gandhi            :   President, Indian National Congress

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three individuals—Subhas Chandra Bose, Jawaharlal Nehru, and Mahatma Gandhi—served as Presidents of the Indian National Congress at different points in its history.  Subhas Chandra Bose's presidency was marked by internal conflict within the Congress, while Jawaharlal Nehru's leadership steered the party through crucial phases of the independence movement. Mahatma Gandhi, though not always formally holding the presidential position, exerted immense influence on the Congress's direction and policies, shaping its strategies and goals significantly.  The other options are incorrect because they exclude at least one individual who demonstrably held the position of Congress President.  This question tests factual recall of key figures and their roles in the Indian National Congress.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization                 Founder/Key Figure
1. Forward Bloc                 :   Mahatma Gandhi
2. Azad Hind Fauj              :   Jawaharlal Nehru
3. Indian National Army (INA) :   Subhas Chandra Bose

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Forward Bloc is incorrectly linked to Mahatma Gandhi in option 1; it was founded by Subhas Chandra Bose after his split with the Congress. Option 2 incorrectly attributes the founding of the Azad Hind Fauj (also known as the Indian National Army) to Jawaharlal Nehru; it was primarily led and organized by Subhas Chandra Bose.  Option 3 correctly identifies Subhas Chandra Bose as the key figure behind the Indian National Army. Option (c) is the only correct option because it accurately identifies the founder of the INA. The other options contain at least one incorrect pairing, demonstrating a misunderstanding of the key figures associated with these significant organizations in the Indian independence movement.  The question assesses factual knowledge and the ability to differentiate between related historical figures and organizations.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Ideology          Prominent Advocate
1. Complete Independence     :   Jawaharlal Nehru
2. Dominion Status            :   Motilal Nehru
3. Non-violence                :   Subhas Chandra Bose

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Jawaharlal Nehru was a staunch advocate for complete independence for India, consistently pushing for the goal of Purna Swaraj. Motilal Nehru, while a significant leader in the independence movement, initially supported dominion status as a transitional step towards full independence, as reflected in the Nehru Report.  Option 3 is incorrect; while Subhas Chandra Bose was a prominent figure in the Indian independence movement, he was a critic of Gandhi's strategy of non-violence and advocated for a more militant approach.  Therefore, only options 1 and 2 are correctly matched. This question tests the understanding of different political ideologies within the Indian National Congress and their proponents.  The inclusion of a distractor (non-violence linked to Bose) requires careful analysis and understanding of historical nuances.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Event                          Location
1.  Tripuri Congress Session      :   Madras
2.  Haripura Congress Session    :   Gujarat
3.  Lahore Congress Session      :   Punjab

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Tripuri Congress session was held in Tripuri, Central Provinces (present-day Madhya Pradesh), not Madras. The Haripura Congress session was indeed held in Gujarat. The Lahore Congress session correctly took place in Lahore, Punjab. Option (c) is the only correct choice because it accurately matches two of the three events to their respective locations. The incorrect placement of the Tripuri Congress session serves as a significant distractor, testing the candidate's precise knowledge of the locations of important Congress sessions. This question demands precise factual recall related to the Indian National Congress’s historical sessions.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Figure        Significant Contribution/Association
1.  Bhagat Singh            :  The Philosophy of the Bomb
2.  Sukhdev                 :  Central Legislative Assembly Bombing
3.  Bhagwati Charan Vohra :  The Philosophy of the Bomb

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

While Bhagat Singh was a revolutionary figure associated with several acts of revolutionary violence, he did not author "The Philosophy of the Bomb."  This book is attributed to Bhagwati Charan Vohra, making option 3 correct. Sukhdev was indeed involved in the Central Legislative Assembly bombing, along with Bhagat Singh and Batukeshwar Dutt.  Option 1 is incorrect due to the misattribution of authorship.  The question demands a precise understanding of the contributions and associations of key figures in the Indian revolutionary movement.  The use of plausible but incorrect attributions tests the candidate's detailed knowledge of the topic.



**6. Consider the following pairs:**

   Document/Report          Key Feature/Recommendation

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

The Nehru Report, drafted by Motilal Nehru, advocated for Dominion Status, not complete independence.  Therefore, option 1 is incorrect.  The Motilal Nehru Report, however, did indeed recommend Dominion Status as a step towards self-governance. The Government of India Act of 1935 introduced a significant amount of provincial autonomy. Therefore, options 2 and 3 are correctly matched. This question evaluates the candidate’s understanding of key policy documents and their provisions during the Indian independence movement.  The incorrect pairing of the Nehru Report with complete independence acts as a strong distractor, demanding precise knowledge of the report's contents.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Historical Figure          Association with Bundelkhand
    1.  Mahmud of Ghazni       :  Invaded Bundelkhand
    2.  Asaf Khan              :  Served as a governor of Bundelkhand
    3.  Prithviraj Chauhan     :  Led an expedition into Bundelkhand
    4.  Raja Chhatrasal        : Ruled Bundelkhand independently
    5.  The Chandelas         :  Ruled Bundelkhand for centuries

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1, 3, and 5 only
(b) 1, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1, 3, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

Option (a) is correct because Mahmud of Ghazni's invasions extended to Bundelkhand, Prithviraj Chauhan led expeditions in the region, and the Chandela dynasty's long rule is well-documented in Bundelkhand's history.

Option (b) is incorrect because while Chhatrasal was a significant ruler in Bundelkhand, his rule wasn't entirely independent; he engaged in alliances and conflicts with other powers, including the Mughals.  

Option (c) is incorrect as it omits the well-established connections of Prithviraj Chauhan and the Chandelas with Bundelkhand.

Option (d) is incorrect because the association of Asaf Khan with Bundelkhand as a governor lacks historical evidence.  While individuals from Bundelkhand families might have risen to high Mughal positions, there's no direct evidence of Asaf Khan's governorship in Bundelkhand.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Dynasty/Empire       Geographical Location
    1.  Pratiharas           :  Karnataka
    2.  Sharqi Sultanate     :  Chota Nagpur
    3.  Vijayanagara Empire :  Karnataka
    4.  Chandelas           :  Bundelkhand
    5.  Ganga Dynasty      :  Karnataka

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 3, 4, and 5 only
(b) 4 and 5 only
(c) Only 4
(d) Only 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 3, 4, and 5 only

**Explanation:**

Option (a) is correct because the Vijayanagara Empire's influence and control extended significantly across Karnataka. The Chandela dynasty’s association with Bundelkhand is historically well-established. The Ganga dynasty is also known for its rule in Karnataka.

Option (b) is incorrect because it leaves out the significant Vijayanagara presence in Karnataka.

Option (c) is incorrect as it excludes the other two correctly matched pairs.

Option (d) is incorrect because, while the Vijayanagara Empire is correctly paired,  it omits the Chandelas and Gangas, crucial dynasties in their respective regions. The Pratiharas and Sharqi Sultanate are incorrectly linked to the given locations.


**3.  Consider the following pairs:**

    Historical Event/Period          Location Primarily Associated
    1.  Second Anglo-Maratha War   :  Madras Presidency
    2.  Disturbances in Bundelkhand :  Bundelkhand
    3.  Eka Movement                :  Awadh
    4.  Salt Satyagraha              :  Karnataka
    5.  Quit India Movement        :  Madras Presidency

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 2, 3, and 4 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) Only 2
(d) 2 and 3 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Option (b) is correct. The Disturbances in Bundelkhand were localized to Bundelkhand itself. The Eka Movement was a significant peasant movement concentrated in Awadh.

Option (a) is incorrect. While the Salt Satyagraha had widespread participation, it wasn't primarily associated with Karnataka.  The Quit India Movement also had activities across India; it wasn't concentrated in the Madras Presidency.

Option (c) is incorrect; it omits the correctly matched pair of the Eka movement and Awadh.

Option (d) is incorrect. As mentioned, the Quit India Movement and the Salt Satyagraha had broader geographical reach than specified in the options.  The Second Anglo-Maratha War also had a wider theater of operations than just the Madras Presidency.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

    Individual          Significant Contribution/Association
    1.  Queen Victoria     :  Patron of the Mohammedan Anglo-Oriental College
    2.  Napoleon Bonaparte:  Observed India's commerce as crucial to Europe
    3.  Mahatma Gandhi    :  Shaved his head during the Champaran Satyagraha
    4.  Subhas Chandra Bose:  Started Azad Hind Radio in Japan
    5.  Sir Syed Ahmed Khan:  Advocated for a nation-state based on individual rights in India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) Only 4


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Option (a) is correct. Napoleon Bonaparte's famous quote highlights the importance of Indian commerce for Europe. Subhas Chandra Bose's association with Azad Hind Radio in Japan is well-documented.

Option (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because  Queen Victoria's patronage of the Mohammedan Anglo-Oriental College is not historically accurate. Mahatma Gandhi's act of shaving his head and adopting a loincloth occurred during his South India tour, not Champaran.  Sir Syed Ahmed Khan's views were more nuanced than a straightforward advocacy for a nation-state based solely on individual rights; he emphasized community identity as well.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Leader                                      Movement/Organization
    1.  Sayyid Ahmad Khan                      :  Deoband Movement
    2.  Annie Besant                           :  Central Hindu College, Banaras
    3.  Swami Shraddhananda                   :  Gurukul Kangri
    4.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy                    :  Prarthana Samaj
    5.  Mahatma Gandhi                        :  Ahmedabad Textile Labour Association

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 3 and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Annie Besant played a crucial role in establishing the Central Hindu College in Benaras, which later developed into the Banaras Hindu University. Swami Shraddhananda, a prominent figure in the Arya Samaj, founded the Gurukul at Kangri, near Haridwar, as a center for traditional Indian education. Mahatma Gandhi founded the Ahmedabad Textile Labour Association to champion the rights of textile workers.  These three pairs are correctly matched.

Option (a) is incorrect because Sayyid Ahmad Khan was associated with the Aligarh Movement, not the Deoband Movement. The Deoband Movement was led by figures like Muhammad Qasim Nanautavi and Rashid Ahmad Gangohi. Option (b) is incorrect for the same reason. Option (d) is incorrect as it omits the correct pairing of Annie Besant with the Central Hindu College.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Organization/Movement              Prominent Figure
    1.  Satyashodhak Samaj              :  Gopal Baba Walangkar
    2.  Servants of India Society        :  Gopal Krishna Gokhale
    3.  Ramakrishna Mission              :  Sarada Devi
    4.  Aligarh Movement                 :  William Bentinck
    5.  Brahmo Samaj                     :  Henry Vivian Derozio

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2, 3, and 5 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) Only 2

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Servants of India Society was indeed founded by Gopal Krishna Gokhale.  The Ramakrishna Mission, while founded by Swami Vivekananda, saw significant contributions and influence from Sarada Devi, Ramakrishna's wife and a revered figure within the movement.  These two pairs are correctly matched.

Option (a) is incorrect because while Gopal Baba Walangkar was a significant Dalit leader, he wasn't the founder or primary leader of the Satyashodhak Samaj; that distinction belongs to Jyotirao Phule. Option (b) is incorrect because Henry Vivian Derozio was associated with the Young Bengal Movement, not the Brahmo Samaj (though the Brahmo Samaj incorporated some of the Derozian ideals). William Bentinck was a Governor-General, not directly associated with the Aligarh Movement. Option (d) is incorrect as it excludes the correct pairing of Sarada Devi with the Ramakrishna Mission.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

    Social Reform Movement             Key Focus/Characteristic
    1.  Aruvippuram Movement           :  Upliftment of Ezhavas in Kerala
    2.  Singh Sabha Movement            :  Modern Western Education for Sikhs
    3.  Vaikom Satyagraha              :  Temple Entry for Untouchables in Travancore
    4.  Self-Respect Movement         :  Rejection of Brahminical Religion
    5.  Ahmadiyya Movement             :  Universal Religion and Opposition to Jihad


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) Only 3 and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs accurately reflect the key focus or characteristic of the respective social reform movements. The Aruvippuram Movement, spearheaded by Sree Narayana Guru, directly addressed the upliftment of the Ezhava community in Kerala. The Singh Sabha Movement prioritized modern Western education for Sikhs. The Vaikom Satyagraha specifically targeted temple entry restrictions for untouchables in Travancore. The Self-Respect Movement, led by E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker, explicitly rejected Brahminical religion and culture. The Ahmadiyya Movement championed a universalist interpretation of Islam and actively opposed the concept of Jihad as a means of conflict.

Options (a), (b), and (d) are therefore incomplete and incorrect, failing to acknowledge the accurate pairings of all five movements with their respective focuses.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

    Reform Leader                      Significant Contribution/Association
    1.  Dadabhai Naoroji                  :  Rahnumai Mazdayasnan Sabha
    2.  Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar         :  Widow Remarriage Legislation
    3.  Swami Dayananda Saraswati       :  Gurukul Kangri
    4.  Keshab Chandra Sen              :  Brahmo Samaj of India
    5.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale            :  All India Anti-Untouchability League


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 4 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) Only 2

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was instrumental in the legalisation of widow remarriage in British India. Keshab Chandra Sen, after a schism within the Brahmo Samaj, founded the Brahmo Samaj of India. These two pairs are correctly matched.

Option (a) is incorrect because Dadabhai Naoroji, while a significant Parsi leader, wasn't directly associated with the founding of the Rahnumai Mazdayasnan Sabha;  other Parsi figures like Naoroji Furdonji were more prominently involved. Option (c) is incorrect because  Gopal Krishna Gokhale established the Servants of India Society, not the All India Anti-Untouchability League (that was associated with Mahatma Gandhi).  Option (d) is incorrect as it leaves out the correct pairing of Keshab Chandra Sen with the Brahmo Samaj of India. Swami Dayananda Saraswati was not directly associated with the Gurukul Kangri; although the Gurukul was associated with the Arya Samaj which he founded.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Publication                                  Author/Editor
    1.  Satyarth Prakash                         :  Gopal Ganesh Agarkar
    2.  Tahdhib-ul-Akhlaq                       :  Sayyid Ahmad Khan
    3.  Sudharak                                  :  Annie Besant
    4.  Rast Goftar                             :  Behramji M. Malabari
    5.  Tattvabodhini Patrika                    :  Debendranath Tagore
