(a) 2 and 5 only
(b) 1, 2, and 5 only
(c) 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) Only 2

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Sayyid Ahmad Khan authored or edited *Tahdhib-ul-Akhlaq*. Debendranath Tagore was associated with the *Tattvabodhini Patrika*.  These two pairs are correctly matched.

Option (b) is incorrect because *Satyarth Prakash* was authored by Swami Dayananda Saraswati, not Gopal Ganesh Agarkar. Option (c) is incorrect because *Rast Goftar* was associated with the Rahnumai Mazdayasnan Sabha, and while Behramji M. Malabari was involved in Parsi reform, he wasn't directly linked to *Rast Goftar* in the same way as other figures within the movement. Option (d) is incorrect as it omits the correct pairing of *Tattvabodhini Patrika* with Debendranath Tagore.  Annie Besant was not directly associated with *Sudharak*, which was connected with Gopal Ganesh Agarkar.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Event                     Prominent Figure
1. Swadeshi Movement                 :   Gopal Krishna Gokhale
2. Non-Cooperation Movement       :   Bal Gangadhar Tilak
3. Khilafat Movement                 :   Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
4. Quit India Movement                :   Subhas Chandra Bose


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only the pair connecting the Khilafat Movement with Mahatma Gandhi is correctly matched.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale was a prominent leader of the Moderate faction within the Indian National Congress, which initially opposed the more radical aspects of the Swadeshi Movement.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak, while a significant figure in the Indian nationalist movement, was primarily associated with the more aggressive phase of the movement that followed the Swadeshi Movement, not the Swadeshi Movement itself. Subhas Chandra Bose played a crucial role in the Quit India Movement, but his association with the earlier movements wasn't as central as Gandhi's role in the Khilafat Movement. The Khilafat Movement, aimed at supporting the Ottoman Caliphate, saw Gandhi's significant involvement in uniting Hindus and Muslims under a common cause, marking a crucial phase in his leadership.  The other options present incorrect pairings of historical events and their prominent figures, demonstrating a lack of accurate historical understanding.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Ideology                  Associated Movement
1.  Gandhian Philosophy              :   Home Rule Movement
2.  Marxism                          :   Quit India Movement
3.  Incipient Socialism                :   Swadeshi Movement


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Swadeshi Movement, with its emphasis on self-reliance and boycott of British goods, exhibited elements of incipient socialism, advocating for economic independence and challenging the existing economic order. While Gandhi's philosophy influenced many movements, the Home Rule Movement was primarily led by figures like Tilak and Annie Besant, who, while not explicitly Marxist or socialist, held differing views from Gandhi on certain aspects of political strategy.  The Quit India Movement, while having diverse participants, wasn't primarily organized or characterized by Marxist ideology. Therefore, only the pairing of incipient socialism with the Swadeshi Movement accurately reflects the ideological underpinnings of the movement.  The other options incorrectly link ideologies with movements, highlighting potential misconceptions regarding the ideological complexities of the Indian freedom struggle.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Action Taken During Swadeshi Movement     Location
1.  Boycott of British Educational Institutions :   Punjab
2.  Boycott of Manchester cloth and Liverpool salt:   Bengal
3.  Establishment of Swadeshi textile mills      :   Madras


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The boycott of Manchester cloth and Liverpool salt was a prominent feature of the Swadeshi Movement, especially in Bengal, where the movement originated in response to the Partition of Bengal. The establishment of Swadeshi textile mills was a significant aspect of the movement aimed at promoting indigenous industries, and this occurred across various regions, including Madras. The boycott of British educational institutions was indeed part of the movement’s strategy, but its geographic concentration wasn't limited to the Punjab alone; it occurred across India. Thus, options 2 and 3 correctly link the actions to their relevant locations. Option 1 is partially correct but lacks the comprehensive geographic representation. The other options present inaccurate links between actions and locations, demonstrating a need for precise geographical knowledge of the movement's spread and impact.



**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                    Role in Swadeshi Movement
1.  Surendranath Banerjea                  :   Leader of the Extremist faction
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji                        :   Prominent figure in the Moderate faction
3.  Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar                :   Prominent Organiser in Maharashtra


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Surendranath Banerjea was a prominent leader of the Moderate faction, not the Extremist faction, within the Indian National Congress during the Swadeshi Movement. Dadabhai Naoroji, a pioneer of Indian nationalism, was indeed a key figure in the Moderate faction. Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar played a significant organizational role in the Swadeshi Movement's activities within Maharashtra. Therefore, only the pairings of Dadabhai Naoroji with the Moderate faction and Sakharam Ganesh Deuskar with his role in Maharashtra are correctly matched. The incorrect pairing of Surendranath Banerjea with the Extremist faction highlights the importance of understanding the internal dynamics and factions within the Indian nationalist movement.  The other options incorrectly link individuals with their roles, demonstrating the need for precise knowledge of the participants and their positions within the movement.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Impact of Swadeshi Movement             Domain Affected
1.  Rise of new industries                  :   Agriculture
2.  Growth of national consciousness        :   Politics
3.  Promotion of vernacular education       :   Culture


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Swadeshi Movement's impact extended beyond the economic sphere. While it did lead to the rise of new industries, its influence on agriculture was indirect and less direct than its impact on politics and culture. The movement significantly fostered national consciousness by uniting Indians against British rule and promoting a sense of shared identity. The movement also promoted vernacular education as part of its broader cultural revival agenda. Therefore, options 2 and 3 accurately reflect the movement's impact on politics and culture. Option 1 is partially correct but overstates the direct impact on agriculture. The other options show a misunderstanding of the multifaceted impact of the Swadeshi Movement beyond pure economic effects.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                    Association/Organization
1. Dadabhai Naoroji                         :  East India Association
2. Surendranath Banerjea                  :  British India Association
3.  Raja Rammohun Roy                     :  Atmiya Sabha
4.  Sayyid Ahmad Khan                      :  Scientific Society


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji founded the East India Association in London in 1866, aiming to advocate for Indian interests within British political circles.  Raja Rammohun Roy established the Atmiya Sabha (Society of Friends), a significant early reformist organization focused on social and religious reform. Sayyid Ahmad Khan founded the Scientific Society, reflecting his focus on promoting Western scientific knowledge among Muslims in India.  The inclusion of Surendranath Banerjea with the British India Association is incorrect. While Banerjea was a prominent leader in the Indian Association, a precursor to the Indian National Congress, he was not associated with the British India Association. The British India Association, formed from a merger of earlier organizations, was more focused on the interests of the landed gentry, a group with which Banerjea's more radical nationalist views clashed. Options (a), (c), and (d) are therefore incomplete, failing to accurately reflect the correct pairings.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                 Political Ideology/Stance
1. Mahatma Gandhi                          :  Complete Independence (Poorna Swaraj)
2. Subhas Chandra Bose                    :  Dominion Status
3. Jawaharlal Nehru                         :  Militant Nationalism
4.  Lord Minto                              :  Separate Electorates


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Mahatma Gandhi, while initially advocating for dominion status, later championed the goal of complete independence (Poorna Swaraj). Lord Minto's association with the granting of separate electorates to Muslims through the Morley-Minto Reforms is well-documented.  The pairings of Subhas Chandra Bose with dominion status and Jawaharlal Nehru with militant nationalism are incorrect. Bose was a strong advocate for complete independence and vehemently opposed the acceptance of dominion status.  While Nehru initially held more moderate views, his political stance evolved towards a more assertive form of nationalism, but it wasn't solely characterized as 'militant' nationalism.  Other options are incorrect because they lack the accurate pairings of Gandhi and Minto.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                       Primary Aim/Effect
1. Vernacular Press Act, 1878           :   Promote vernacular education
2.  Indian Factory Act, 1881              :   Regulate child labor in factories
3.  Ilbert Bill                             :   Equalize criminal jurisdiction between British and Indian officials
4.  Government Regulation (1829)        :   Abolish Sati


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 4 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The Indian Factory Act of 1881 was a landmark piece of legislation primarily aimed at regulating child labor in factories, setting limits on working hours and minimum ages. The Government Regulation of 1829, a significant social reform, effectively abolished the practice of Sati.  The other pairings are incorrect. The Vernacular Press Act of 1878 was designed to curb the freedom of the Indian-language press, not to promote education. While the Ilbert Bill aimed to partially equalize the criminal jurisdiction between British and Indian officials, it didn't fully achieve this goal and faced significant opposition.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are inaccurate because they include incorrectly matched pairs.

    Person                                    Contribution/Role

(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 2 only

**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 4 only

**Explanation:**

Lord Dalhousie is correctly associated with the implementation of the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy that led to the annexation of several Indian states. Thomas Munro is not associated with the Permanent Settlement. Therefore, only options 2 and 4 are correctly matched.

(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 4 only

The Indian Association in Calcutta, led by figures like Surendranath Banerjea, actively pursued wider public interests and engaged in sustained political agitation, distinguishing itself from earlier, more conservative organizations. The East India Association, established in London by Dadabhai Naoroji, played a crucial role in representing Indian concerns and lobbying within British political circles. The other pairings are inaccurate. The Poona Sarvajanik Sabha, while involved in broader reform, wasn't primarily focused on landlord interests.  The British India Association represented primarily the interests of landlords and the wealthy, not broader public interests. The Scientific Society was founded by Sayyid Ahmad Khan, not the British India Association. Therefore, only options 2 and 4 are correctly matched.

(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lord Curzon is directly associated with the Partition of Bengal. Lord Irwin's tenure as Viceroy saw the negotiation and signing of the Gandhi-Irwin Pact. Sir Michael O'Dwyer was the Lieutenant Governor of Punjab during the Jallianwala Bagh Massacre. Edwin Montagu played a key role in the formulation of the Government of India Act, 1919. However, General Dyer was the subject of the Hunter Commission's inquiry, not its leader.  The question tests factual knowledge of key figures in British Indian administration and their association with significant historical events.  The inclusion of the seemingly correct but ultimately incorrect pair 5 acts as a significant distractor, highlighting the importance of precise factual recall over generalized knowledge. The question assesses factual recall, and analytical skills.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Association/Role
1.  Dadabhai Naoroji          : President, Indian National Congress
2.  Lala Lajpat Rai           : President, All India Trade Union Congress (AITUC)
3.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale    : President, Indian National Congress
4.  Subhas Chandra Bose      : President, Indian National Congress
5.  Sarojini Naidu            : President, Indian National Congress

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

**Explanation:**

All five pairs represent accurate historical associations. Dadabhai Naoroji, Gopal Krishna Gokhale, Subhas Chandra Bose, and Sarojini Naidu all served as Presidents of the Indian National Congress at different times, reflecting the Congress's evolving leadership and the participation of diverse individuals in its leadership.  Their presidencies mark significant periods in the Congress's history and the broader Indian independence movement.  Similarly, Lala Lajpat Rai's presidency of the All India Trade Union Congress (AITUC) highlights his significant role in the labour movement and its connection to the broader nationalist struggle.  The AITUC, established in 1920, played a crucial role in organizing and representing Indian workers, often working in collaboration with the Congress.  The inclusion of all five pairs as correctly matched underscores the multifaceted nature of Indian nationalism and the diverse individuals who shaped its trajectory.  The other options incorrectly exclude some of these historically verifiable associations.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation            Key Characteristic/Impact
1.  Ancient Monuments Preservation Act : Enacted during Lord Curzon's Viceroyalty
2.  Rowlatt Act                 : Led to widespread protests, including a no-tax campaign
3.  Widow Remarriage Act       : Implemented during Lord Dalhousie's tenure
4.  Government of India Act 1919:  Introduced Dyarchy

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The Ancient Monuments Preservation Act was indeed passed during Lord Curzon's time as Viceroy, reflecting his interest in preserving India's historical heritage. The Rowlatt Act, a highly repressive piece of legislation, sparked widespread protests and civil disobedience, including the no-tax campaign suggested by Swami Shraddhanand, as it curtailed civil liberties and was seen as an infringement on fundamental rights. The Government of India Act of 1919 (also known as the Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms) did introduce the system of Dyarchy, a dual system of governance in which certain subjects were under the control of elected Indians and others under the British.  However, the Widow Remarriage Act was not implemented during Lord Dalhousie's tenure. While Dalhousie was a significant figure in British India, the Widow Remarriage Act was passed later, showcasing the gradual evolution of social reforms within the larger context of British rule in India.  The other options are incorrect because they either include the incorrectly matched pair (3) or exclude some of the correctly matched ones.

Dadabhai Naoroji's influential work exposing British economic exploitation is *Poverty and Un-British Rule in India*. Aurobindo Ghosh's philosophical treatise is *The Life Divine*. Valentine Chirol, a British journalist, authored *Indian Unrest*, offering a contemporary perspective on the Indian nationalist movement.  However, the book *Gokhale - My Political Guru* was not written by C.R. Das. This introduces a plausible distractor, as both Das and Gokhale were prominent figures in the Indian National Congress, making the incorrect pairing seem possible to someone with superficial knowledge. The other options are incorrect because they either include the incorrect pairing (5) or exclude some of the correctly matched pairs.

**5. With reference to the Indian National Congress, consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Movement                     Key Figure/Leader

(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

The first four pairs correctly identify key figures associated with major movements within the Indian National Congress. Mahatma Gandhi's leadership of the Non-Cooperation, Quit India, and Civil Disobedience Movements is a cornerstone of understanding the Indian independence struggle. His strategies of non-violent resistance profoundly shaped the course of the movement.  Similarly, Annie Besant and Bal Gangadhar Tilak played pivotal roles in the Home Rule Movement, advocating for greater self-governance and mobilizing popular support for the cause of Indian independence. This movement, although separate from the Congress, worked closely with it and helped transition the Congress from a deliberative body to a mass movement.  The Surat Split, however, was not led by a single individual but rather represented a significant internal division within the Congress between the Moderates and Extremists. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Figure             Association

4.  Lord Linlithgow               :   Viceroy of India during the Cripps Mission
5.  E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker       :   Leader of the Self-Respect Movement


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Cripps Mission, a significant event in the lead-up to Indian independence, was headed by Stafford Cripps.  Both Jawaharlal Nehru and Mahatma Gandhi criticized the proposals put forth by the mission, highlighting its shortcomings and failure to address the core demands of Indian nationalists for immediate self-governance.  Lord Linlithgow served as the Viceroy of India during this crucial period, and his role in the eventual failure of the mission is noteworthy.  While Winston Churchill was indeed the head of the British War Cabinet, his strong opposition to significant concessions to India is well documented, making his presence indirectly relevant to the Cripps Mission's failure.  E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker's inclusion is a deliberate distractor, connecting a prominent social reformer of the era to a completely different movement unrelated to the Cripps Mission.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they either exclude crucial correctly matched pairs or include the incorrectly matched pair concerning E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker.

(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Quit India Movement was launched under the leadership of Mahatma Gandhi, though the movement continued even after his arrest. The Gandhi-Irwin Pact was a significant agreement between Mahatma Gandhi and Lord Irwin, the Viceroy of India at the time.  The formation of the Indian National Army (INA) is undeniably associated with Subhas Chandra Bose, who became its supreme commander. Mahatma Gandhi was the sole representative of the Indian National Congress at the Second Round Table Conference. **5. With reference to the Indian Independence Movement, consider the following pairs:**

Mahatma Gandhi was instrumental in the founding and development of the Ahmedabad Textile Labour Association (ATLA), a significant trade union in India's early labor movement.  His involvement showcased his commitment to improving the working conditions and rights of Indian laborers.  Option 1 is thus correctly matched.

Jawaharlal Nehru served as the President of the Indian National Congress on multiple occasions, but not exclusively.  Several other leaders held this position during the Indian independence movement. Therefore, option 2 is incorrectly matched due to its overly definitive nature.

Narsinh Mehta was a prominent Gujarati poet and saint, but he did not author "Hind Swaraj."  This work is attributed to Mahatma Gandhi. Option 3 is therefore incorrect.

Jayaprakash Narayan was a prominent socialist leader and played a significant role in various movements, including the Quit India Movement. However, he wasn't the sole leader; the movement was characterized by collective leadership including Mahatma Gandhi.  Therefore, option 4 is incorrectly matched because of its assertion of sole leadership.



**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Concept/Ideology                 Championed By
1. Ramrajya                           :   Jawaharlal Nehru
2. Swaraj                             :   Bal Gangadhar Tilak
3. Ahimsa                             :   Mahatma Gandhi
4. Non-violence                       :   Subhas Chandra Bose


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Mahatma Gandhi is unequivocally associated with the concept and practice of Ahimsa (non-violence) as the cornerstone of his philosophy and political strategy.  His philosophy profoundly influenced the Indian independence movement.  Option 3 is correctly matched.

While both Jawaharlal Nehru and Mahatma Gandhi advocated for a better India,  "Ramrajya" (ideal state) is more closely linked to Gandhi's vision of a morally upright and just society. Nehru's vision, while aiming for social justice, was rooted in a socialist framework. Therefore, option 1 is incorrectly matched.

The concept of Swaraj (self-rule) was embraced by many Indian nationalist leaders, including Bal Gangadhar Tilak, but it wasn't solely his concept.  Many contributed to its development and popularization.  Option 2 is thus incorrect due to its exclusive attribution.

Subhas Chandra Bose, while a nationalist leader, didn't primarily champion non-violence. His approach was more aligned with a more assertive and sometimes militaristic strategy.  Therefore, option 4 is incorrectly matched.


**3. With reference to Mahatma Gandhi's life and work, consider the following pairs:**

   Location                          Activity/Event
1. Champaran                         :   Salt Satyagraha
2. Dandi                              :   Indigo movement
3. Birla House, New Delhi            :   Assassination
4. South Africa                       :   Initial experiments with Satyagraha


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Mahatma Gandhi's assassination took place at Birla House in New Delhi. Option 3 is correctly matched.  His initial experiments and development of Satyagraha as a method of non-violent resistance occurred during his time in South Africa, fighting against racial discrimination against Indians. Option 4 is correctly matched.

The Champaran Satyagraha focused on the plight of indigo farmers in Bihar, not the Salt Satyagraha, which involved the symbolic defiance of the salt tax at Dandi. Option 1 is incorrectly matched.

The Dandi March was the site of the Salt Satyagraha, not the Indigo movement, which happened in Champaran. Option 2 is incorrectly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Legislation                     Key Provision/Impact
1. Indian Councils Act 1892          :   Introduction of Dyarchy
2. Government of India Act 1919      :   Establishment of a bicameral legislature
3. Government of India Act 1935      :   Provincial Autonomy
4. Indian Independence Act 1947      :   Partition of India


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act 1935 is famously known for introducing Provincial Autonomy, granting greater self-governance to the provinces of British India. Option 3 is correctly matched.  The Indian Independence Act 1947 formally partitioned India into India and Pakistan. Option 4 is correctly matched.

The Indian Councils Act of 1892 did not introduce Dyarchy; that came later with the Government of India Act 1919. Option 1 is incorrectly matched.

The Government of India Act 1919 did introduce significant reforms but not the establishment of a bicameral legislature at the central level; it expanded the legislative councils but didn't create a full bicameral system. Option 2 is incorrectly matched.



**5. With reference to the Indian National Congress, consider the following pairs:**

   Session Location                 President
1. Calcutta                          :   Dadabhai Naoroji
2. Surat                             :   Gopal Krishna Gokhale

4. Nagpur                            :   Mahatma Gandhi

(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Lahore session of the Indian National Congress in 1929 is notable for Jawaharlal Nehru's presidency, where the goal of Purna Swaraj (complete independence) was declared. Option 3 is correctly matched. The Nagpur session of 1920 saw Mahatma Gandhi's presidency, marking a significant shift in the Congress's strategy towards mass movements and non-cooperation. Option 4 is correctly matched.

Dadabhai Naoroji presided over the Calcutta session in 1886, not 1929. Option 1 is incorrectly matched.

Gopal Krishna Gokhale presided over the Bengal session in 1905, not the Surat split of 1907. Option 2 is incorrectly matched.  The Surat split was a significant event marked by internal conflict within the Congress.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Event                       Associated Figure
1.  Quit India Movement                   :    Lord Wavell
2.  Dandi March                           :    C. Rajagopalachari
3.  Formation of INA                      :    Rash Behari Bose
4.  Gandhi-Irwin Pact                     :    Lord Irwin
5.  Lahore Congress Session (1929)       :    Jawaharlal Nehru

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The Quit India Movement was launched in 1942,  while Lord Wavell was the Viceroy of India during the later stages of the Indian independence movement, notably proposing the Wavell Plan in 1945.  Therefore, pairing them is incorrect. The Dandi March was directly led by Mahatma Gandhi, not C. Rajagopalachari, though Rajagopalachari led significant salt satyagraha movements in other parts of India. Rash Behari Bose was indeed involved in the early stages of the Indian National Army (INA) formation, alongside Mohan Singh, but Subhas Chandra Bose became its most prominent leader.  The Gandhi-Irwin Pact was a direct agreement between Mahatma Gandhi and Lord Irwin, the Viceroy of India at the time.  Finally, the Lahore Congress Session of 1929 saw Jawaharlal Nehru elected as Congress President, a pivotal moment signifying the shift towards the goal of Purna Swaraj. Thus, options 3, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legislation                                 Key Provision
1.  Government of India Act, 1935           :   Introduction of Dyarchy
2.  Rowlatt Act                               :   Curtailed civil liberties
3.  Indian Councils Act of 1909              :   Increased elected representation in councils
4.  Defence of India Rules                     :   Emergency measures during wartime

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act of 1935, instead of introducing Dyarchy, actually *abolished* it at the provincial level and introduced provincial autonomy.  The Rowlatt Act was indeed notorious for severely curtailing civil liberties in India. The Indian Councils Act of 1909 (Morley-Minto Reforms) did expand elected representation in legislative councils, though indirectly and with limitations. The Defence of India Rules were implemented as emergency measures to bolster the war effort during World War II, restricting civil liberties.  Therefore, options 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Figure                        Role/Association
1.  Annie Besant                           :   Founder of the Congress

4.  C. Rajagopalachari                     :   President of the Indian National Congress

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Annie Besant was a prominent leader in the Indian independence movement and played a significant role in the Home Rule Movement, but she was not a founder of the Indian National Congress.  A.O. Hume is considered one of the founders. Subhas Chandra Bose was indeed a prominent leader of the Forward Bloc, a political party he founded after leaving the Congress.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a crucial figure in the Home Rule Movement, advocating for self-governance. C. Rajagopalachari did serve as President of the Indian National Congress, making this pair correct. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Movement/Event                          Primary Goal
1.  Simon Commission                       :   To achieve Dominion Status for India
2.  Quit India Movement                   :   Immediate British withdrawal from India
3.  Home Rule Movement                     :   Establishment of a Responsible Government

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Simon Commission's primary mandate was to review the workings of the Government of India Act, 1919, not to achieve Dominion Status.  While Dominion Status was a goal discussed during the period, it wasn't the Commission's express objective. The Quit India Movement's central goal was the immediate end of British rule in India. The Home Rule Movement aimed primarily at achieving self-government or Dominion Status, not necessarily a "Responsible Government" in the specific sense of a fully independent government. Therefore, only the second pair is correctly matched.


**5. With reference to the Indian National Congress, consider the following pairs:**

   Session Location                       Key Decision/Event
1.  Lahore (1929)                         :   Declaration of Purna Swaraj
2.  Karachi (1931)                        :   Adoption of the Gandhi-Irwin Pact
3.  Calcutta (1928)                       :   Rejection of the Nehru Report

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Lahore Session of the Indian National Congress in 1929 is famously known for the adoption of the resolution declaring Purna Swaraj (complete independence) as the Congress's goal. The Karachi Session in 1931 primarily focused on endorsing the Gandhi-Irwin Pact and did not reject the Nehru Report; the Nehru Report had already been approved in the Calcutta Session of 1928. The Calcutta Session of 1928 actually *approved* the Nehru Report, which proposed Dominion Status, though it faced internal dissent.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader of the Quit India Movement             Location Associated with the Quit India Movement
1. Mahatma Gandhi                             :   Ahmednagar Fort
2. Aruna Asaf Ali                              :   Gowalia Tank Maidan, Bombay
3. Jayaprakash Narayan                        :   Ballia
4. Usha Mehta                                 :   Underground Radio in Bombay
5. Ram Manohar Lohia                          :   Underground Activities in Bombay


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)


**Explanation:**

The Quit India Movement, launched on August 9, 1942, saw widespread participation across India.  Mahatma Gandhi was the foremost leader, though his immediate arrest along with other top Congress leaders triggered spontaneous uprisings. While Gandhi was imprisoned in the Aga Khan Palace in Pune (near Ahmednagar), he wasn't directly associated with the activities at Ahmednagar Fort in the way Aruna Asaf Ali was associated with Gowalia Tank Maidan, where the Quit India Resolution was passed.  Jayaprakash Narayan's leadership was instrumental in Ballia's parallel government, a significant aspect of the movement's decentralized nature. Usha Mehta's underground radio in Bombay played a crucial role in disseminating information and maintaining morale. Ram Manohar Lohia was indeed involved in underground activities, but his primary contribution wasn't solely confined to Bombay. His activities were spread across various locations.  Therefore, options 1 and 5 are partially incorrect, making option (c) the most accurate representation of the correct pairings.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Individual/Group Involved in the Quit India Movement     Type of Involvement
1. Students                                              :   Formation of Parallel Governments
2. Workers                                                :   Underground Radio Broadcasts
3. Socialists                                              :   Subversive Activities
4. Forward Bloc                                         :   Distribution of Arms and Ammunition
5. Gandhi Ashramites                                    :   Cyclone Relief Work


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)


**Explanation:**

The Quit India Movement was characterized by diverse forms of participation.  Students were actively involved in protests and strikes, but not primarily in establishing parallel governments. That was more the domain of local leaders and activists. Workers participated significantly through strikes, but their involvement wasn't central to operating underground radios.  Socialists and members of the Forward Bloc were prominently involved in subversive activities and the distribution of arms and ammunition, reflecting the movement's shift towards more militant resistance after the arrest of top leaders. Cyclone relief work was undertaken primarily by the parallel governments, not specifically by Gandhi Ashramites, although many Ashramites may have participated. Therefore, only options 3 and 4 accurately reflect the primary type of involvement for those groups during the Quit India Movement.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Key Figure in the Quit India Movement            Role/Activity
1. Biju Patnaik                                    :   Leading the Parallel Government in Satara
2. Sucheta Kripalani                               :   Underground Radio Operations in Bombay
3. Achyut Patwardhan                              :   Organizing the Tamluk Jatiya Sarkar
4. Chhotubhai Puranik                             :   Subversive Activities in Gujarat
5. Aruna Asaf Ali                                   :   Hoisting the National Flag on August 9, 1942


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) 2, 3, and 5 only
(d) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)


**Explanation:**

The Quit India Movement saw numerous individuals emerge as key players.  Biju Patnaik played a significant role, but not primarily in Satara's parallel government. Sucheta Kripalani's involvement wasn't focused on radio operations in Bombay, although she was active in the movement. Achyut Patwardhan was indeed involved in the Tamluk Jatiya Sarkar (parallel government in Midnapore), as were several other leaders. Chhotubhai Puranik's activities were crucial in Gujarat's subversive actions.  Aruna Asaf Ali's act of hoisting the flag on August 9, 1942, is well-documented.  Therefore, options 3, 4, and 5 accurately reflect the prominent roles played by these individuals during the movement; options 1 and 2 are incorrect.


**4.  Consider the following pairs:**

   Post-Quit India Movement Development             Description
1. Rajagopalachari Formula                         :   Proposed a plebiscite for partition
2. Desai-Liaqat Pact                               :   Advocated for an interim government with equal Congress-League representation
3. Wavell Plan                                      :   Proposed a reconstructed executive council with equal Hindu-Muslim representation
4. Cripps Mission                                   :   Offered Dominion Status after the war
5. Cabinet Mission Plan                            :   Outlined a process for a constituent assembly


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)


**Explanation:**

The period following the Quit India Movement saw numerous attempts to resolve the constitutional deadlock. The Rajagopalachari Formula, proposed in 1944, included a plebiscite in Muslim-majority areas to determine their future, a key element of the proposal.  The Desai-Liaqat Pact focused on establishing an interim government with equal representation from the Congress and the Muslim League. The Wavell Plan aimed to reconstruct the executive council with parity between Hindus and Muslims. The Cripps Mission, though preceding the Quit India Movement, significantly offered Dominion Status after the war.  The Cabinet Mission Plan, also post-Quit India, proposed a framework for a constituent assembly to draft a new constitution. Therefore, all the pairs are correctly matched.

3.  Communist Party of India                           :   Supported the British war effort during WWII

5.  Indian National Congress                           :   Launched the Quit India Movement

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 3 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)


**Explanation:**

The Indian National Movement involved various organizations with diverse ideologies. The Forward Bloc was directly associated with Subhas Chandra Bose's leadership and his more radical approach to independence. The Hindu Mahasabha's opposition to the Quit India Movement stemmed from its differing views on the path to independence.  The Communist Party of India's support for the British war effort during World War II reflected its international alignment and strategic considerations. The Muslim League's advocacy for Pakistan is well-established. The Indian National Congress, as the primary driving force, directly launched the Quit India Movement. Therefore, all the pairs are correctly matched.  The options are designed to be plausible distractors, testing the candidate's knowledge of the nuanced relationships between these organizations and their respective stances.

   Act/Legislation                      Key Provision/Feature

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Post-Civil Disobedience Movement Strategy  | Prominent Advocate
1.  Constructive work focusing on Gandhian principles |  M.K. Gandhi
2.  Constitutional struggle and participation in elections | Jawaharlal Nehru
3.  Resumption of non-constitutional mass struggle |  Subhas Chandra Bose

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The period immediately following the withdrawal of the Civil Disobedience Movement witnessed a significant debate within the Indian National Congress regarding the future course of action.  Mahatma Gandhi strongly advocated for a return to constructive work, focusing on social reform and nation-building activities aligned with his philosophy of Satyagraha. This emphasis on constructive work formed a core element of his strategy for the immediate future.  Simultaneously, a strong leftist faction within the Congress, prominently led by figures like Subhas Chandra Bose and Jawaharlal Nehru, vehemently opposed a return to solely constructive work and advocated for the immediate resumption of non-constitutional mass struggles against British rule. They believed that the momentum of the movement should be maintained through direct action, continuing the fight for independence without relying on constitutional means.  While Jawaharlal Nehru did participate in the debate regarding participation in elections, he was fundamentally critical of prioritizing this as the primary strategy over mass action. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 reflect accurate pairings of strategies and their key proponents.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Provision of the Government of India Act, 1935 |  Description
1.  All-India Federation                    |  Never materialized due to non-participation of princely states.
2.  Provincial Autonomy                   |  Replaced dyarchy with complete autonomy for provinces.
3.  Federal Legislature (Bicameral)       |  Council of States elected directly, Federal Assembly indirectly.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

The Government of India Act, 1935, introduced several significant changes to the Indian political landscape.  The proposed All-India Federation, aiming to unite British Indian provinces and princely states, was a crucial element of the Act. However, the federation ultimately failed to materialize due to the unwillingness of many princely states to join, failing to meet the Act's conditions regarding the number and population of participating states.  The Act also introduced provincial autonomy, replacing the earlier system of dyarchy (dual governance) with full autonomy for the provinces in most matters. This represented a significant step towards self-governance at the provincial level.  However, the description of the Federal Legislature is incorrect. While the Act did establish a bicameral legislature, the Council of States had both elected and nominated members, and the Federal Assembly's election process was indeed indirect. Thus, only pairs 1 and 2 accurately reflect the features of the 1935 Act.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Post-World War II Event |  Outcome
1.  Royal Indian Navy (RIN) Revolt      |  Led to immediate transfer of power to India.
2.  Indian National Army (INA) Trials  |  Generated widespread nationalist sentiment.
3.  Cabinet Mission Plan               |  Proposed a united India with substantial autonomy for provinces.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The post-World War II period in India was marked by several significant events that impacted the course of the independence movement. The INA trials, while not directly resulting in immediate transfer of power, significantly fueled nationalist sentiment across India, exposing the weaknesses of British authority and highlighting the sacrifices made by Indian soldiers.  The Cabinet Mission Plan, while ultimately failing to prevent partition, did propose a framework for a united India with a substantial degree of autonomy for the provinces, reflecting a significant shift in British policy towards eventual self-governance.  The RIN revolt, while demonstrating the erosion of British control over the armed forces and contributing to the atmosphere of change, did not directly cause the immediate transfer of power. The transfer of power was a complex process influenced by a multitude of factors.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 correctly match the event with its outcome.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Individual / Group                               |  Stance on Office Acceptance (1937 Elections)
1.  Jawaharlal Nehru                           |  Initially opposed, later reconciled.
2.  Congress Socialists                          |  Strongly opposed.
3.  Gandhi                                      |  Initially opposed, later gave approval.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 only
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

The 1937 provincial elections presented the Indian National Congress with a crucial dilemma: whether to accept office in the provincial governments formed under the Government of India Act, 1935.  Jawaharlal Nehru, initially a strong opponent of office acceptance due to his belief in the need for continued mass struggle, eventually reconciled with the decision after the Congress's impressive electoral performance. This change in stance reflects a pragmatic approach to using the limited power offered by the Act as a stepping stone towards greater autonomy. The Congress Socialists, a left-wing faction within the Congress, consistently and vehemently opposed office acceptance, fearing it would compromise the revolutionary character of the freedom struggle and dilute the focus on complete independence.  Mahatma Gandhi, initially hesitant due to his concerns about the potential compromises inherent in working within the existing system, eventually gave his approval for Congress leaders to accept office, strategically aiming to use legislative positions to further the cause of independence.  Therefore, all three pairs correctly reflect the stance of the individuals and groups on the issue of office acceptance.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                      |  Role in Partition
1.  Lord Mountbatten                          |  Proposed the June 3 Plan for partition.
2.  V.P. Menon                               |  Key architect of the integration of princely states.
3.  Clement Attlee                             |  Announced the deadline of June 30, 1948, for the transfer of power.

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

The partition of India in 1947 was a complex event with numerous key players. Lord Mountbatten, as the Viceroy of India, played a crucial role in formulating the June 3 Plan, which laid out the framework for the partition of India into India and Pakistan. This plan included provisions for the partition of Punjab and Bengal, referendums in certain areas, and the creation of two separate dominions. V.P. Menon, a key advisor to Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, was instrumental in the smooth and relatively swift integration of the princely states into the Indian Union after independence. His strategic use of a combination of negotiation, persuasion, and pressure was vital in preventing the Balkanization of India. Clement Attlee, as the British Prime Minister, made the landmark announcement setting June 30, 1948, as the deadline for the transfer of power to India, regardless of whether a consensus had been reached on the constitution. This announcement significantly accelerated the process leading to independence, putting immense pressure on Indian political leaders to reach an agreement. Therefore, all three pairs correctly identify the roles of these individuals in the events surrounding partition and integration.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, focusing on the Non-Cooperation Movement, Khilafat Movement, and related historical events and figures.  The questions are designed to be challenging and test a deep understanding of the subject matter.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   **Event/Movement**                     **Prominent Leader**
1.  Home Rule Movement                  :   Mahatma Gandhi
2.  Non-Cooperation Movement           :   Subhas Chandra Bose
3.  Khilafat Movement                    :   Muhammad Ali Jinnah
4.  Civil Disobedience Movement         :   C. Rajagopalachari


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (d) 4 only

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because C. Rajagopalachari, while not the sole leader, was a prominent figure within the Civil Disobedience Movement.  The other options are incorrect due to mismatches in leadership.  The Home Rule Movement was primarily led by Bal Gangadhar Tilak and Annie Besant, not Mahatma Gandhi.  While Subhas Chandra Bose was involved in the Indian National Congress and participated in various movements, he wasn't a primary leader of the Non-Cooperation Movement. Similarly, Muhammad Ali Jinnah, although supportive of the Khilafat Movement, was not its central leader; the Ali brothers (Muhammad Ali and Shaukat Ali) played more significant roles.  The question highlights the need for precise knowledge of leadership roles in various movements within the Indian freedom struggle.  Incorrect options act as plausible distractors, testing the candidate's ability to distinguish between involvement and leadership.


**2. With reference to the Indian National Movement, consider the following pairs:**

   **Act/Reform**                         **Primary Impact**
1.  Rowlatt Act                             :   Increased Indian discontent
2.  Montford Reforms                      :   Introduced Dyarchy
3.  Government of India Act 1935          :   Established Provincial Autonomy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched. The Rowlatt Act, with its repressive measures, significantly increased Indian discontent and fueled the Non-Cooperation Movement. The Montford Reforms, while intended to grant some autonomy, introduced the system of Dyarchy (dual governance) in provinces. The Government of India Act of 1935, a landmark piece of legislation, significantly devolved power to the provinces by establishing Provincial Autonomy.  The question tests factual recall of key legislative acts and their consequences during the Indian freedom struggle. The inclusion of all correct pairs makes it a challenging question, requiring thorough knowledge of the period.  Incorrect options are designed to be implausible, thus discouraging guesswork.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   **Movement/Event**                      **Key Characteristic**
1.  Khilafat Movement                      :   Focus on support for Turkey
2.  Non-Cooperation Movement             :   Emphasis on non-violent non-cooperation
3.  Civil Disobedience Movement           :   Salt Satyagraha


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

All three pairs accurately reflect key characteristics. The Khilafat Movement centered around support for the Ottoman Caliph and the preservation of the Ottoman Empire, a crucial religious and emotional issue for Indian Muslims. The Non-Cooperation Movement, as its name suggests, was built upon the principle of non-violent non-cooperation with British rule. The Civil Disobedience Movement famously included the Salt Satyagraha, a pivotal event that symbolized defiance against British authority.  This question tests conceptual understanding and the ability to link movements with their defining features. The correct answer includes all three pairs, requiring comprehensive knowledge to avoid overlooking any detail. Distractors are carefully chosen to be plausible yet incorrect, emphasizing the need for precise understanding.

(c) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Only the second pair is correctly matched. The Chauri Chaura incident occurred in 1922. The other options are incorrect because of inaccurate years. The Nagpur Congress Session took place in 1920, not 1921. Gandhi's arrest in relation to the Non-Cooperation Movement happened in 1922, not 1920. This question tests factual recall of specific dates and events. The correct answer is only one pair, requiring precise knowledge of the chronology of events to avoid selecting incorrect options which are close to the correct dates. The inclusion of plausible distractors increases the difficulty level.

(b) 1, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched. Lord Irwin, the Viceroy of India at the time, played a crucial role in negotiating the Gandhi-Irwin Pact. Mustafa Kemal Ataturk, also known as Kemal Pasha, was instrumental in the abolition of the Caliphate in Turkey, ending the significance of the Khilafat issue. Motilal Nehru spearheaded the drafting of the Nehru Report, a significant constitutional proposal. Subhas Chandra Bose famously led the Forward Bloc, a faction within the Indian National Congress.  This question assesses factual recall of key personalities and their contributions during the period. The correct answer includes all four pairs, making it challenging and requiring complete knowledge to answer. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Historical Event                     Key Figure
1.  Non-Cooperation Movement          :   Motilal Nehru
2.  Salt Satyagraha                     :   Lal Bahadur Shastri
3.  Quit India Movement                 :   Aruna Asaf Ali
4.  INA Trial                           :   Prem Kumar Sehgal

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four pairs are correctly matched. Motilal Nehru was a prominent participant and leader in the Non-Cooperation Movement, actively supporting Gandhi's initiatives.  Lal Bahadur Shastri played a significant role in the Salt Satyagraha, demonstrating his commitment to the cause of independence. Aruna Asaf Ali's courageous leadership during the Quit India Movement, notably her hoisting of the Congress flag in defiance of British authorities, is well documented.  Prem Kumar Sehgal was one of the key defendants in the INA trial, a pivotal event that challenged British authority in India during World War II.  The other options are incorrect because they exclude at least one of these accurately matched pairs, demonstrating a lack of comprehensive understanding of the key figures' involvement in these pivotal historical events.  The question tests factual recall and understanding of the Indian independence movement's key personalities and their contributions.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Legislation                       Associated Event
1. Rowlatt Act                       :   Jallianwala Bagh Massacre
2. Salt Law                          :   Dandi March
3.  Government of India Act 1935     :   Provincial Autonomy

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched. The Rowlatt Act, a repressive piece of legislation, created an environment of fear and unrest that directly contributed to the Jallianwala Bagh massacre. The Salt Law, which imposed a tax on salt, was directly challenged by Gandhi's Dandi March, a symbolic act of civil disobedience. The Government of India Act 1935 introduced the concept of provincial autonomy, a significant step towards self-governance. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incomplete, failing to recognize the strong links between the legislation and the associated events. This question assesses factual recall and an understanding of the causal relationships between legislation and events in the Indian independence struggle.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Movement                Primary Goal
1.  Khilafat Movement                :   Protection of Ottoman Caliphate

3.  Quit India Movement                :   Immediate Independence

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three pairs accurately reflect the primary goals of the respective movements. The Khilafat Movement's central aim was to protect the Ottoman Caliphate and the position of the Sultan of Turkey as the religious head of Muslims. The Non-Cooperation Movement, spearheaded by Gandhi, aimed at achieving Swaraj (self-rule) through non-violent means. The Quit India Movement, launched in 1942, demanded immediate independence from British rule.  The other options are incorrect as they exclude at least one of these correctly paired goals, indicating a lack of thorough knowledge of the objectives of these crucial movements within the Indian nationalist struggle. The question tests factual recall and understanding of the distinct goals of major political movements in India.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization                         Prominent Leader

(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Jawaharlal Nehru was a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress, serving as its president and playing a crucial role in shaping India's post-independence trajectory.  Muhammad Ali Jinnah was the undisputed leader of the Muslim League, advocating for the creation of Pakistan.  While B.R. Ambedkar was a significant figure in the fight against untouchability, he was not a primary leader of the Harijan Sevak Sangh; that organization was founded by Mahatma Gandhi.  Option (a) is incorrect because it excludes Jinnah's leadership role in the Muslim League. Option (c) is incorrect because it only includes Jinnah. Option (d) is incorrect because it incorrectly attributes leadership of the Harijan Sevak Sangh to Ambedkar. This question assesses factual knowledge of key leaders and their associations with major political organizations during the Indian independence movement.


**5. With reference to the Indian Independence Movement, consider the following pairs:**

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Leader                                    Association/Movement
1.  Jawaharlal Nehru                         :   President, Lahore Congress
2.  Subhas Chandra Bose                     :   President, Bengal Provincial Congress Committee
3.  Dadabhai Naoroji                         :   President, Indian National Congress (multiple terms)
4.  Rajendra Prasad                          :   President, Indian National Congress (multiple terms)
5.  Govind Ballabh Pant                     : Chief Minister, Uttar Pradesh

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs provided are correctly matched. Jawaharlal Nehru presided over the Lahore Congress session in 1929, where the declaration of Purna Swaraj was adopted. Subhas Chandra Bose served as the president of the Bengal Provincial Congress Committee. Dadabhai Naoroji held the presidency of the Indian National Congress on multiple occasions, a significant achievement in the early years of the Congress. Rajendra Prasad also served as the Congress President multiple times, showcasing his prominent role in the organization.  Govind Ballabh Pant served as the Chief Minister of Uttar Pradesh, a major political position within India's federal structure.  Therefore, option (c) encompassing all five pairs is the correct answer.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                    Role during Quit India Movement
1.  Gandhi                                   :   Leader of the movement
2.  Aruna Asaf Ali                           :   Presided over Congress session after arrests
3.  Jayaprakash Narayan                     :   Underground leader
4.  Lord Wavell                             :   Commander-in-Chief of the Indian Army

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Mahatma Gandhi was the designated leader of the Quit India Movement.  Following the mass arrests of Congress leaders on August 9, 1942, Aruna Asaf Ali stepped forward to preside over a crucial Congress session, demonstrating leadership in a critical moment. Jayaprakash Narayan was a key figure in the underground activities during the movement, coordinating resistance efforts.  However, Lord Wavell was the Viceroy of India during the Quit India Movement, not the Commander-in-Chief of the Indian Army.  Therefore, option (b), including pairs 1, 2, and 3, is correct. Option (d) is incorrect due to the mismatched information regarding Lord Wavell's role. Options (a) and (c) are incomplete, omitting correctly matched pairs.


**3. With reference to the Non-Cooperation Movement, consider the following pairs:**

   Person                                   Participation/Role

(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All pairs are correctly matched.  Motilal Nehru, a prominent lawyer, gave up his legal practice to participate in the Non-Cooperation Movement. Jawaharlal Nehru was an active participant in the movement.  C.R. Das presided over the Ahmedabad session of the Congress during the movement, though he was in jail at the time.  M.A. Jinnah initially supported the Non-Cooperation Movement but later withdrew his support.  Rabindranath Tagore is known to have opposed the more extreme aspects of the movement, such as the burning of foreign clothes.  Therefore, option (c) is the correct answer. Other options incorrectly exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Person                     Role/Association
1.  Jawaharlal Nehru          President, Lahore Congress Session (1929)
2.  Subhas Chandra Bose      President, Haripura Congress Session (1938)
3.  Rajendra Prasad           President of the Congress after Bose's resignation (1939)
4.  Maulana Abul Kalam Azad President, Ramgarh Congress Session (1940)
5.  Govind Ballabh Pant       Mover of resolution at Tripuri Congress Session (1939)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, and 5 only
(d) All of the above


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Jawaharlal Nehru presided over the Lahore Congress session of 1929, where the declaration of Purna Swaraj (complete independence) was made. Subhas Chandra Bose was unanimously elected president of the Haripura Congress session in 1938. Following Subhas Chandra Bose's resignation from the Congress presidency in 1939, Rajendra Prasad was elected to succeed him.  The Ramgarh Congress session of 1940 was presided over by Maulana Abul Kalam Azad.  Finally, Govind Ballabh Pant moved a crucial resolution at the Tripuri Congress session in 1939, which sought to reaffirm faith in Gandhian policies and indirectly challenged Bose's leadership.  These are all well-established facts in the history of the Indian National Congress.  The options are designed to test the candidate's knowledge of these specific events and the individuals involved. Incorrect options strategically include plausible but incorrect pairings to increase the difficulty level.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Movement                     Key Figure/Leader
1.  Bardoli Satyagraha                Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel
2.  Vaikom Satyagraha                  K. Kelappan
3.  Khudai Khidmatgars                 Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan
4.  Chittagong Armoury Raid            Surya Sen
5.  Salt Satyagraha at Dharasana       Sarojini Naidu


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) All of the above
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel effectively led the Bardoli Satyagraha, a significant peasant movement. K. Kelappan played a pivotal role in the Vaikom Satyagraha, a movement for temple entry for lower castes. Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan's Khudai Khidmatgars were a non-violent Pashtun movement in the North-West Frontier Province. Surya Sen masterminded the Chittagong Armoury Raid, a significant armed rebellion. Sarojini Naidu led a salt satyagraha at Dharasana following Gandhi's arrest, demonstrating the significant role of women in the movement.  These are well-documented historical events. The incorrect options use a combination of correct and incorrect pairings, creating plausible distractors to challenge the examinee's in-depth knowledge.



**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Political Document/Resolution        Prominent Feature/Demand
1.  Nehru Report                         Dominion Status
2.  Delhi Manifesto                     Conditions for attending Round Table Conference
3.  Karachi Resolution                   Fundamental Rights and National Economic Programme
4.  Poona Pact                           Abolition of separate electorates for Depressed Classes
5.  Pakistan Resolution                 Creation of independent Muslim states


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(c) All of the above
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. The Nehru Report of 1928 primarily advocated for dominion status for India. The Delhi Manifesto outlined the conditions under which the Indian National Congress would participate in the Round Table Conferences. The Karachi Resolution of 1931 is notable for its articulation of fundamental rights and a national economic program. The Poona Pact of 1932 resulted in the abolition of separate electorates for the depressed classes. The Lahore Resolution (also known as the Pakistan Resolution) of 1940 demanded the creation of separate Muslim states in India.  These are all significant historical documents and resolutions that shaped the course of the Indian independence movement. The incorrect options cleverly mix correct and incorrect pairings, making it challenging to identify the entirely correct set.



**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Congress Session                  President
1.  Tripuri Session (1939)           Subhas Chandra Bose
2.  Haripura Session (1938)          Rajendra Prasad
3.  Ramgarh Session (1940)          Maulana Abul Kalam Azad
4.  Lahore Session (1929)           Jawaharlal Nehru
5.  Nagpur Session (1920)           Madan Mohan Malaviya


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 3, and 4 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 1, 3, 4, and 5 only
(d) All of the above


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched.  Subhas Chandra Bose presided over the Tripuri Congress session in 1939. Maulana Abul Kalam Azad presided over the Ramgarh Congress session in 1940. Jawaharlal Nehru presided over the Lahore Congress session in 1929.  However,  Rajendra Prasad did *not* preside over the Haripura Session (1938) – that was Subhas Chandra Bose. Similarly, Madan Mohan Malaviya did not preside over the Nagpur Session (1920) –  that session was presided over by C. Vijayaraghavachariar. The distractors in the incorrect options are designed to test detailed knowledge of Congress presidencies throughout the crucial period.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Act/Policy                          Key Characteristic/Outcome
1.  Government of India Act, 1919     Introduction of Dyarchy
2.  Government of India Act, 1935     Establishment of Provincial Autonomy
3.  Communal Award                    Separate Electorates for Minorities
4.  Gandhi-Irwin Pact                 Suspension of Civil Disobedience Movement
5.  Cripps Mission Proposals           Offer of Dominion Status


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(c) All of the above
(d) 2, 3, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched. The Government of India Act, 1919, introduced the system of dyarchy (dual governance) in the provinces. The Government of India Act, 1935, established a system of provincial autonomy. The Communal Award of 1932 introduced separate electorates for various religious and caste groups. The Gandhi-Irwin Pact of 1931 led to the temporary suspension of the Civil Disobedience Movement.  The Cripps Mission proposals of 1942 offered dominion status to India.  These are all foundational aspects of the political development of India during the pre-independence era. The incorrect options strategically utilize close but not entirely accurate pairings to assess the candidate's nuanced understanding of these historical events and policies.
